Ghaybah Munqati'ah: Definitions and Rationale
Defining ghaybah munqati'ah and presenting three scholarly opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ghaybah munqati'ah and explain the rationale behind the three opinions, identifying which is considered closest to fiqh.

Core Idea
Ghaybah munqati'ah terminates guardian's authority when waiting for his opinion would lose a suitable match.

Guardianship in marriage is based on the guardian's kindness (shafaqah). When a guardian's absence is so prolonged that waiting for his consent would harm the woman's interest, his right to object is lost. This concept, known as ghaybah munqati'ah (interrupted absence), has been defined by Hanafi scholars in three different ways. In this lesson, we explore these definitions and understand why one is considered closer to the spirit of fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Why is ghaybah munqati'ah relevant? It terminates the guardian's right to object to a marriage, allowing the woman to proceed without his consent. Understand that the definition is not fixed but based on practicality.
2
State Al-Quduri's definition
The guardian is in a town where caravans arrive only once a year. This is a fixed temporal criterion.
Al-Quduri's view is the most objective but may be rigid.
3
State the second opinion
The minimum travel period (three days' journey) is sufficient, because there is no maximum limit. This opinion comes from some later scholars.
This criterion is based on travel distance, not a full year.
4
State the third opinion
When seeking the guardian's opinion would cause the loss of a suitable match (kufu), his absence is considered interrupted. This is the view of Shams al-A'imma.
This opinion is described as 'closer to fiqh' because it focuses on the consequence.
5
Analyze the rationale
The third opinion is preferred because guardianship is based on shafaqah (kindness). Retaining authority when it harms the woman's interest contradicts this principle. The text also mentions a case from al-Jami' al-Saghir where hiding in the same city qualifies.
The rationale overrides rigid time/distance criteria.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والغيبة المنقطعة ان يكون فى بلد لاتصل اليه القوافل فى السنة الامرة وهو اختيار القدورى وقيل أدنى مدة السفر لانه لانهاية لاقصاه وهو اختيار بعض المتاخرين وقيل اذا كان بحال يفوت الكفوباستطلاع رايه وهذا اقرب الى الفقه لانه لانظر في ابقاء ولايته حينئذ . ترجمه غیبت منقطعہ یہ ہے کہ ایسے شہر میں ہو کہ نہ پہنچے قافلہ اس کی طرف سال میں مگر ایک مرتبہ اور یہ قدوری کا پسندیدہ ( قول ہے ) اور کہا گیا کہ ادنی مدت سفر اس لئے کہ منتہی سفر کی کوئی انتہا نہیں ہے اور یہ قول بعض متأخرین کا پسند کردہ ہے اور کہا گیا کہ جب ایسے حال میں ہو کہ کفو فوت ہو جائے اسکی رائے پر اطلاع پانے سے اور یہ قول اقرب الی الفقہ ہے۔ اس لئے وقت ولایت کو باقی رکھنے میں کوئی شفقت نہیں ۔ تشریح. مصنف اس عبارت میں غیبت منقطہ کی تعریف کرنا چاہتے ہیں۔ اس بارے میں صاحب قدوری کا مذ ہب مختار تو یہ ہے کہ آدمی ایسے شہر میں چلا جائے جہاں قافلے سال میں ایک ہی مرتبہ جاتے ہیں۔ بعض متأخرین کا مذہب مختار یہ ہے کہ ادنی مدت سفر یعنی تین دن کی مسافت پر چلے جانے سے غیبت منقطعہ متحقق ہو جائے گی۔ اس لئے کہ مدت سفر کی کوئی انتہا نہیں ہے۔ لہذا ادنی مدت سفر کا اعتبار کیا گیا ہے۔ بعض حضرات جن میں شمس الائمہ مرضی ہیں ان کی رائے یہ ہے کہ اگر ولی ایسی جگہ چلا گیا کہ اگر اس کی رائے معلوم کی جائے تو کفو فوت ہو جائے گا۔ پس ایسی صورت میں غیبت منقطعہ کا تحقق ہوگا۔ یہ قول دلائل فقیہ سے زیادہ قریب ہے کیونکہ کفوفوت ہونے کے باوجود اس کی ولایت کو باقی رکھنے میں کوئی شفقت نہیں ہے۔ حالانکہ ولایت کا مدار ہی شفقت پر ہے۔ اس وجہ سے جامع بصغیر میں کہا گیا کہ کوئی ولی شہر میں چھپ گیا اور اس کے بارے میں کسی کو علم نہیں تو یہ بھی غیبت منقطعہ ہوگی۔ واللہ اعلم ۔
And the interrupted absence is that one is in a town where caravans do not arrive in the year except once; this is the choice of al-Quduri. And it was said: the minimum travel period, because its farthest limit has no end; this is the choice of some later scholars. And it was said: when it is such that a suitable match is lost by seeking his opinion; this is closer to fiqh because there is no regard in preserving his guardianship then. Translation: Interrupted absence is that one is in a city where a caravan does not reach it in a year except once, and this is al-Quduri's preferred opinion. And it was said: the minimum travel period because there is no end to the farthest travel, and this is the preferred opinion of some later scholars. And it was said: when he is in a state that a suitable match is lost by seeking his opinion, and this opinion is closer to fiqh because there is no kindness in keeping his guardianship then. Elaboration: The author intends to define interrupted absence. Regarding this, the chosen opinion of al-Quduri is that a man goes to a city where caravans go once a year. The chosen opinion of some later scholars is that the minimum travel period, i.e., a distance of three days, constitutes interrupted absence, because there is no end to travel duration, so the minimum travel period is considered. Some people, including Shams al-A'imma al-Marwazi, hold the opinion that if the guardian goes to a place such that if his opinion is sought, a suitable match would be lost, then interrupted absence is established. This opinion is closer to fiqh because although a suitable match is lost, there is no kindness in keeping his guardianship, whereas guardianship is based on kindness. For this reason, in al-Jami' al-Saghir it is said: if a guardian hides in the city and no one knows about him, this is also interrupted absence. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage defines 'ghaybah munqati'ah' (interrupted absence) – a legal concept in Hanafi marriage law where a guardian's absence is so extended that his consent can no longer be obtained, thereby losing his right to object to the marriage. The author presents three Hanafi opinions: (1) Al-Quduri's view: the guardian is in a town reached by caravans only once a year. (2) Some later scholars: the minimum travel distance (three days) suffices, as there is no maximum. (3) Shams al-A'imma's view: the key is that a suitable match (kufu) would be lost by waiting for the guardian's opinion. The author considers the third opinion closest to fiqh because guardianship is based on kindness (shafaqah), and retaining it when a suitable match is lost shows no kindness. Al-Jami' al-Saghir extends this to a guardian hiding in the same city. The passage thus clarifies the conditions under which a guardian's authority terminates due to absence.

Key Terms
الغيبة المنقطعة (al-ghaybah al-munqati'ah): Absence of the guardian that is so prolonged that seeking his opinion is impractical, thereby terminating his right to object to the marriage.
الكفو (al-kufu): A suitable match in status and lineage.
الشفقة (al-shafaqah): Kindness and care, the basis of guardianship authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which opinion on ghaybah munqati'ah is considered 'closer to fiqh'?
A) The guardian is in a city where caravans come once a year.
B) The guardian is at least three days travel away.
C) The guardian's absence causes loss of a suitable match if his opinion is sought.
D) The guardian hides in the same city with no one knowing.

Key Takeaway
The definition of ghaybah munqati'ah is not fixed; the most principled approach prioritizes the loss of a suitable match, reflecting the underlying rationale of guardianship (shafaqah).

Guardianship for a Majnunah: Who Has Priority – Father or Son?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on guardian priority for a majnunah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on guardianship of a majnunah when father and son conflict and explain why the son's priority is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Guardianship follows 'usubah, not degree of kindness – the son precedes the father.

This lesson examines a classical Hanafi dispute over who should contract the marriage of a mentally incompetent woman (majnunah) when both her father and her adult son are alive. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) rule that the son is the proper guardian, while Imam Muhammad holds the father is preferred. We will analyze the proofs on each side and understand why the Hanafi school adopts the view of the two shaykhs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the parties
We have a mentally incompetent woman (majnunah) who has a living father and an adult son from a previous marriage. Both claim guardianship (wilayah) to contract her marriage.
The woman herself lacks legal capacity, so a guardian is required.
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs) say the son is the wali. Imam Muhammad says the father is the wali.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; both positions are based on valid reasoning.
3
Examine Imam Muhammad's proof (dalil)
Imam Muhammad argues that the father has greater shafaqah (kindness and care) than the son, and guardianship is fundamentally about ensuring the ward's welfare, so the one with more kindness should be preferred.
Shafaqah is an essential quality in a guardian.
4
Examine the Shaykhayn's proof
The two shaykhs argue that priority in guardianship follows the order of 'usubah (residuary heirship). The son is a stronger 'asabah than the father; in inheritance, the son takes the residue and the father gets a fixed share (1/6). Since guardianship is based on 'usubah, the son is preferred.
They illustrate with the maternal grandfather (not an 'asabah) vs. a paternal cousin (an 'asabah) – the cousin is preferred despite possibly having less kindness.
5
Understand the Hanafi response and mufta bihi
The response to Imam Muhammad is that shafaqah is considered in its essence (asl al-shafaqah), not in its excess. Since both father and son possess the essence of shafaqah, the tiebreaker is 'usubah, which favors the son. Therefore, the mufta bihi (operative) position is that the son is the wali.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah prefers the Shaykhayn's view, and this is the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا اجتمع فى المجنونة ابوها وابنها فالولّى فى انكاحها ابنها فى قول أبي حنيفة وابي يوسف وقال محمد ابوها لانه اوفر شفقة من الابن ولهما ان الابن هو المقدم فى العصوبة وهذه الولاية مبنية عليها ولا معتبر بزيادة الشفقة كاب الام مع بعض العصبات والله اعلم
ترجمه اور جب جمع ہو جا ئیں مجنونہ عورت میں اس کا باپ اور اس کا بیٹا تو اس کا نکاح کرنے میں اس کا ولی اقرب اس کا بیٹا ہے شیخین کے قول کے مطابق ۔ اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ اس کا با پیاس لئے کہ باپ بیٹے کے مقابلہ میں زیادہ شفقت رکھتا ہے۔ اور شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بیٹا عصبہ ہونے میں مقدم ہے۔ اور یہ ولایت اسی عصو بت پر مبنی ہے اور زیادتی شفقت کا اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا جیسا کہ ماں کا باپ یعنی نانا بعض عصبات کے ساتھ ۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک مجنونہ عورت کا باپ ہے اور پہلے شوہر سے بالغ بیٹا ہے تو اس مجنونہ کے نکاح کی ولایت کس کو حاصل ہوگی ۔

كتاب النكاح
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم اس سلسلہ میں شیخین کا مذہب تو یہ ہے کہ حق ولایت بیٹے کو ہے۔ اور امام محمد کا مذہب ہے کہ حق ولایت باپ کو ہے۔ امام محمد کی دلیل کہ باپ میں شفقت زیادہ ہے بمقابلہ بیٹا کے۔ اور اس ولایت کا مدار شفقت پر ہے۔ لہذا زیادتی شفقت کی وجہ سے باپ کو ولایت حاصل ہوگی بیٹے کو نہیں ۔
شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عصبہ ہونے میں بیٹا مقدم ہے چنانچہ بیٹے کی موجودگی میں باپ کو صرف چھٹا حصہ ملتا ہے اور بیٹا عصبہ ہوتا ہے اور یہ ولایت منی ہے عصوبت پر لہذا بیٹا ہی ولی ہوگا باپ نہیں۔ اور زیادتی شفقت کے بارے میں امام محمد کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ولایت میں نفس شفقت معتبر ہے۔ ڈزیادتی شفقت معتبر نہیں مثلاً کسی کا نانا ہے اور پچیرا بھتیجا تو ولایت میں پچیرا بھتیجا مقدم ہوگا۔ حالانکہ نانا میں شفقت محبت زیادہ ہوتی ہے۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ شفقت کا اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا۔ واللہ اعلم
And when the father and son of a mentally incompetent woman are together, the guardian for her marriage is her son according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: her father, because he has more kindness than the son. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that the son is preferred in 'asabah (residuary heirship), and this guardianship is based on it, and increase in kindness is not considered, like the maternal grandfather with some 'asabah. And Allah knows best. Translation: And when the father and son of a mentally incompetent woman are together, the closer guardian for her marriage is her son according to the two shaykhs. And Imam Muhammad said: her father, because the father has more kindness than the son. And the proof of the two shaykhs is that the son is preferred in 'asabah, and this guardianship is based on it, and increase in kindness is not considered, like the maternal grandfather with some 'asabah. Elaboration: The issue is that a mentally incompetent woman has a father and an adult son from a previous husband. In this series, the opinion of the two shaykhs is that the right of guardianship belongs to the son. And Imam Muhammad's opinion is that the right belongs to the father. Imam Muhammad's proof: the father has more kindness compared to the son, and this guardianship is based on kindness, so due to greater kindness, the father gets guardianship, not the son. The proof of the two shaykhs is that the son is preferred in 'asabah; indeed in the presence of the son, the father gets only one-sixth, and the son is the 'asabah, and this guardianship is based on 'asabah. Therefore, the son is the guardian, not the father. And regarding the increase in kindness, the response to Imam Muhammad's proof is that in guardianship, the essence of kindness is considered, not the increase of kindness. For example, someone has a maternal grandfather and a paternal cousin; in guardianship, the paternal cousin is preferred, even though the maternal grandfather has more love and kindness. Thus it became known that kindness is not considered. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding guardianship over a mentally incompetent woman (majnunah) when both her father and her adult son are alive. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the son is the rightful guardian (wali) for her marriage. Imam Muhammad argues for the father, citing the father's greater kindness (shafaqah). The rejoinder by the two shaykhs is that guardianship is based on the principle of 'asabah (residuary heirship), not merely on degree of kindness. In Islamic inheritance, the son is a stronger 'asabah than the father; similarly, guardianship follows the same order. They illustrate with the maternal grandfather (who is not an 'asabah) versus a paternal cousin: the cousin, being an 'asabah, is preferred despite possibly having less affection. Thus the son's priority is upheld. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that of the two shaykhs, giving guardianship to the son over the father.

Key Terms
المجنونة (al-majnunah): A mentally incompetent woman who lacks legal capacity to contract marriage herself.
العصوبة (al-'usubah): Being a residuary heir (asabah) – one who inherits the remainder after fixed shares.
الشفقة (al-shafaqah): Kindness and care that a guardian feels for the ward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school regarding guardianship of a majnunah when father and son conflict?
A) The father is the wali because of greater kindness.
B) The son is the wali because of stronger 'usubah.
C) The woman may choose her own guardian.
D) The matter is referred to the qadi.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when both father and son are present as potential guardians for a majnunah, the son is the rightful wali because guardianship is based on 'usubah (heirship hierarchy), not on the degree of kindness (shafaqah).

Kafa'ah in Marriage: Definition and Proof
Stating the ruling and proofs for considering kafa'ah in marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kafa'ah, identify the proofs, and explain why guardians have the right to annul a marriage without kafa'ah.

Core Idea
Kafa'ah is wajib for guardians' objection, not contract validity — the marriage stands but can be voided.

The concept of kafa'ah (compatibility) ensures that marriages are harmonious and protect family honor. In this lesson, we will examine the Hanafi position on kafa'ah, the textual and rational proofs, and the practical effect of its absence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Kafa'ah is declared 'معتبرة' (considered) in marriage, meaning it is a condition for the guardians' right to object. The marriage itself remains valid without it.
The ruling is not that kafa'ah is a pillar or condition of validity.
2
Locate the textual proof
The passage cites two hadiths: (1) 'لا يزوج النساء إلا الأولياء ولا يزوجن إلا من الأكفاء' and (2) the hadith of Ali (from Tirmidhi) listing three things not to be delayed, including marrying a woman when her equal is found.
The first hadith is acknowledged as weak by muhaddithun, but the second is considered stronger.
3
Analyze the proof's strength
Although the primary hadith has weakness, the Hanafi school relies on the cumulative evidence: the stronger hadith of Ali, the rational proof (qiyas), and the practice of the Companions.
The passage admits the weakness but maintains the ruling via other supports.
4
Understand the rational proof (qiyas)
Marriage involves six interests that are best realized between equals. A noble woman naturally refuses to be a 'bed' for a base man, so kafa'ah is required to achieve harmony and prevent disgrace.
The metaphor of 'firash' (bed) illustrates the asymmetry: the husband is the mustafrish, the wife is the firash.
5
Apply the ruling: guardian's right to annul
If a woman marries without a suitable match (ghayr kuf'), the guardians can seek annulment from the qadi to protect themselves from 'ar (disgrace). This right exists even if the contract is valid.
The annulment is a remedy for the guardian, not automatic invalidation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الكفاءة
ترجمه فصل كفاءة کے بیان میں ہے۔
الكفاءة في النكاح معتبرة قال عليه السلام الالايزوج النساء الا الا ولياء ولا يزوجن الامن الاكفاء ولان انتظام المصالح بين المتكافيين عادة لان الشريفة تابى ان تكون مستفرشة للخسيس فلابد من اعتبار ها بخلاف جانبها لان الزوج مستفرش فلاتغيظه دناءة الفراش واذا زوجت المرأة نفسها من غير كفو
فللاولياء ان يفرقوا بينهما دفعا لضرر العار عن انفسهم
ترجمہ کفو کا ہونا نکاح میں معتبر ہے۔ فرمایا حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے خبر دار نہ نکاح کریں عورتوں کا مگر اولیاء اور نہ کریں نکاح مگر ہمسروں سے اور اس لئے کہ انتظام مصالح عادة دو ہمسروں کے درمیان حاصل ہو سکتے ہیں۔ اس لئے کہ شریفہ عورت کمینہ مرد کا فراش بننے سے انکار کرے گی۔ پس ضروری ہے کفاءۃ کا اعتبار بخلاف عورت کی جانب کے اس لئے کہ شوہر فراش بنانے والا ہے۔ لہذا فراش کا کمینہ ہونا اس کو غضبناک نہیں بنائے گا۔ اور جب نکاح کیا عورت نے اپنا بغیر کفو کے تو اولیاء کو یہ حق ہے کہ ان دونوں کے درمیان تفریق کر دیں اپنے اوپر سے ضرر عار کو دفع کرنے کے لئے۔
تشریح کفاوت کے معنی ہمسری، برابری، کونظیر ، مساوی بالكفاءة فی النکاح یہ ہے کہ شوہر عورت کا مساوی ہو اسکے حسب میں، نسب میں، دین میں ہعمر میں ، جمال میں۔ وغیرہ ذالک نکاح میں کفارہ کا اعتبار اس لئے کیا گیا ہے تا کہ اولیاء کا حق فسخ ہو کر نکاح لازم ہو جائے نکاح میں کفو کے معتبر ہونے پر دلیل حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا فرمان ہے خبر دار عورتوں کا نکاح نہ کریں مگر اولیاء اور نہ کریں نکاح مگر ہمسروں سے یعنی کفو میں محدثین کے نزدیک یہ حدیث اس درجہ کی نہیں ہے جس سے استدلال کیا جائے کیونکہ بعض راوی متہم بالکذب ہیں۔ زیادہ صحیح حدیث علی کی ہے جسکو ترمذی نے روایت کیا۔ حدیث کا ترجمہ یہ ہے تین چیزیں ہیں جن کو موخر نہ کرے۔ نماز جب وقت آ جائے۔ جنازہ جب حاضر ہو جائے۔ اور بغیر شوہر والی عورت جب اس کا کفومل جائے۔ دوسری عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ نکاح کے چھ مصالح ہیں اور وہ مصالح پورے طور پر اس وقت حاصل ہو سکتے ہیں جبکہ نکاح ہمسروں میں منعقد ہو اسلئے ہم کہتے ہیں کہ مصالح نکاح کو حاصل کرنے کیلئے کفو کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔ لہذا کفاء ت کا اعتبار ضروری ہے۔ البتہ عورت کی جانب میں کفاءت معتبر نہیں مرد شریف خاندان کا ہو اور عورت
Chapter on Kafa'ah. Translation: A chapter on kafa'ah. Kafa'ah in marriage is considered. He (peace be upon him) said: 'Beware, let none give women in marriage except guardians, and let none marry except to equals.' And because the arrangement of interests between equals is customary, for the noble woman refuses to be a bed for a base man, so it must be considered, unlike her side because the husband is the one who makes the bed, so the baseness of the bed does not anger him. And if a woman marries herself without a suitable match, the guardians have the right to separate them to ward off the harm of disgrace from themselves. Translation: Compatibility is considered in marriage. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Beware, let none give women in marriage except guardians, and let none marry except to equals.' And because the arrangement of interests usually occurs between equals, because a noble woman refuses to be a bed for a base man, so consideration of compatibility is necessary, unlike the woman's side because the husband is the one who makes the bed, so the baseness of the bed does not anger him. And when a woman marries herself without a suitable match, the guardians have the right to separate them to ward off the harm of disgrace from themselves. Elaboration: The meaning of kafa'ah is equality, parity, like, equivalence. Kafa'ah in marriage is that the husband be equal to the woman in his lineage, descent, religion, age, beauty, etc. The consideration of kafa'ah in marriage is for the guardians to have the right of annulment so that the marriage becomes binding. The proof for considering compatibility in marriage is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Beware, let none give women in marriage except guardians, and let none marry except to equals.' According to hadith scholars, this hadith is not of such a level as to be used as evidence because some narrators are accused of lying. A more authentic hadith is that of Ali, narrated by Tirmidhi. The translation of the hadith: 'Three things which should not be delayed: prayer when its time comes, the funeral when it is presented, and the woman without a husband when her equal is found.' The second rational proof is that there are six interests of marriage, and these interests can be fully achieved only when the marriage is contracted between equals. Therefore, we say that for achieving the interests of marriage, compatibility is necessary. Hence, consideration of compatibility is necessary. However, in the woman's side, compatibility is not considered; the man may be of noble lineage and the woman...
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage begins a new section (fasl) on kafa'ah (compatibility/suitability) in marriage. It states that kafa'ah is a valid consideration in marriage. Two proofs are offered: a hadith from the Prophet commanding that women be given only to equals, and a rational argument that the interests of marriage are best realized between equals. The text acknowledges that the primary hadith is weak in the eyes of hadith scholars, but another hadith from Ali (transmitted by Tirmidhi) mentioning three things not to be delayed (including marrying a woman when her match appears) serves as stronger evidence. The rational argument is that six interests of marriage (presumably continuity, offspring, companionship, etc.) are achieved through equality. The text also notes a crucial difference: kafa'ah is considered from the woman's side (her family may object if the husband is not equal), but not from the man's side—a noble man may marry a woman of lower status because the husband is the one 'making the bed,' so the lowliness of the bed does not disgrace him. The guardians have the right to annul the marriage if a woman marries herself without a suitable match, to protect themselves from dishonor. The passage is incomplete, but it establishes the principle of kafa'ah and its basis.

Key Terms
الكفاءة (al-kafa'ah): Equality between husband and wife in lineage, religion, and other relevant attributes, with the effect that guardians may object if missing.
الفراش (al-firash): Metaphor for the marital bed; the husband is the 'one who makes the bed' (mustafrish) and the wife is the bed (firash).
العار (al-'ar): Disgrace or shame that may fall upon the family if a woman marries below her status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is kafa'ah considered necessary in marriage?
A) Because the husband will be angry if his wife is of low status.
B) To ensure that the interests of marriage are achieved and guardians are protected from disgrace.
C) Because the Prophet commanded it in a mutawatir hadith.
D) Because it is a pillar of the marriage contract.

Key Takeaway
Kafa'ah is a wajib consideration for guardians, not a pillar of marriage — its absence allows annulment by the guardian to prevent disgrace.

Nikah — Marriage

Guardianship in Marriage: Son vs Father
Intra-Hanafi dispute on guardianship precedence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on guardianship precedence between a woman's son and father, explain the proofs of the two views, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Guardianship in marriage follows asabah, not affection: the son outranks the father.

When a woman's son and father both exist, who contracts her marriage? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute. This lesson examines the arguments from two eminent authorities: the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the Hanafi school prioritises structural kinship (asabah) over sentiment (shafaqah) in determining guardianship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
What is the exact point of disagreement? The dispute is not whether guardianship exists, but who has precedence when both son and father are alive.
The issue is precedence, not validity of marriage.
2
State the view of Shaykhayn and their proof
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf argue the son is the guardian because asabah (agnatic inheritance) is the basis of guardianship, and the son is the strongest asabah — he excludes the father except for one-sixth.
Asabah is a structural, legal relationship.
3
State the view of Imam Muhammad and his proof
Imam Muhammad argues that guardianship is based on shafaqah (affection), and the father has greater affection, so he should be guardian.
Imam Muhammad’s view is a minority within the Hanafi school.
4
Analyse the response of Shaykhayn to Imam Muhammad's proof
They respond that mere affection is considered, not greater affection. To prove this, they give an example: a paternal cousin (asabah) is preferred over a maternal grandfather, even though the grandfather has more affection.
This example shows affection is not the decisive factor.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its practical effect
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Shaykhayn: the son has precedence. Therefore, if both son and father exist, the son must perform the marriage contract.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب النكاح اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم اس سلسلہ میں شیخین کا مذہب تو یہ ہے کہ حق ولایت بیٹے کو ہے۔ اور امام محمد کا مذہب ہے کہ حق ولایت باپ کو ہے۔ امام محمد کی دلیل کہ باپ میں شفقت زیادہ ہے بمقابلہ بیٹا کے۔ اور اس ولایت کا مدار شفقت پر ہے۔ لہذا زیادتی شفقت کی وجہ سے باپ کو ولایت حاصل ہوگی بیٹے کو نہیں۔ شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عصبہ ہونے میں بیٹا مقدم ہے چنانچہ بیٹے کی موجودگی میں باپ کو صرف چھٹا حصہ ملتا ہے اور بیٹا عصبہ ہوتا ہے اور یہ ولایت مبنی ہے عصوبت پر لہذا بیٹا ہی ولی ہوگا باپ نہیں۔ اور زیادتی شفقت کے بارے میں امام محمد کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ولایت میں نفس شفقت معتبر ہے۔ زیادتی شفقت معتبر نہیں مثلاً کسی کا نانا ہے اور پچیرا بھتیجا تو ولایت میں پچیرا بھتیجا مقدم ہوگا۔ حالانکہ نانا میں شفقت محبت زیادہ ہوتی ہے۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ شفقت کا اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا۔ واللہ اعلم
Book of Marriage. In this matter, the madhhab of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that the right of guardianship belongs to the son. And the madhhab of Imam Muhammad is that the right of guardianship belongs to the father. Imam Muhammad's proof: the father has more affection compared to the son. And this guardianship is based on affection. Therefore, due to greater affection, the father will have guardianship, not the son. The proof of the two shaykhs: the son is precedence in being an asabah (residuary heir). Thus, when the son is present, the father receives only one-sixth, and the son is the asabah. And this guardianship is based on asabah. Therefore, the son will be the guardian, not the father. And regarding greater affection, the response to Imam Muhammad's proof is that in guardianship, mere affection is considered, not greater affection. For example, if someone has a maternal grandfather and a paternal cousin, then the paternal cousin is given precedence in guardianship, even though the maternal grandfather has more affection and love. Thus, it is understood that affection is not considered. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding who has the right of guardianship (wilayah) in marriage for a woman: the son or the father. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the son has precedence, while Imam Muhammad holds that the father has precedence. The reasoning: Imam Muhammad argues that guardianship is based on affection (shafaqah), and the father has greater affection. The two shaykhs counter that guardianship is based on asabah (residuary inheritance rights), and the son is a stronger asabah, as he excludes the father from inheritance except one-sixth. They also rebut the affection argument by pointing to other relatives: a paternal cousin (asabah) is preferred over a maternal grandfather even though the latter has more affection, proving that affection alone is not determinative. Thus, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that of the two shaykhs: the son has precedence. The Zahir al-Riwayah position aligns with Shaykhayn, as Imam Muhammad's view is a minority opinion (Nawadir).

Key Terms
ولایت (wilayah): The right and authority to contract a woman in marriage, exercised by her guardian.
شفقت (shafaqah): Affection and care that a guardian has for the woman.
عصبہ (asabah): Agnatic relatives who inherit residuary shares after Quranic heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, who has the right of guardianship (wilayah) in marriage when both a son and father of a woman are present?
A) The father, because he has more affection.
B) The son, because he is the stronger asabah.
C) The father, because he is the older relative.
D) Both equally have the right.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, guardianship in marriage is determined by asabah (agnatic inheritance) — the son outranks the father, contrary to common assumptions based on affection.

The Basis and Proof of Kafa'ah in Marriage
Defines kafa'ah, cites hadith evidence, and explains the legal effect for guardians.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of kafa'ah, cite the primary hadith evidence (including its authenticity), and explain why kafa'ah is only required from the husband's side.

Core Idea
Kafa'ah protects noble families from shame, but only the husband must be equal to the wife.

This lesson introduces the concept of kafa'ah (suitability) in marriage. We will explore its definition, the proofs from the Sunnah that establish it, and the important distinction that it applies only to the husband, not the wife. The passage also explains the guardians' right to annul a marriage when kafa'ah is absent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Kafa'ah is considered in marriage; it is a requirement (wajib) for the husband, giving guardians a right to annul if absent.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The text cites two hadiths: a weaker one about guardians and equals, and a stronger one from Ali (ra) about delaying three things, narrated by al-Tirmidhi.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith commands marriage to equals, implying kafa'ah is necessary. The rational proof of six interests reinforces this.
4
Evaluate the rational proof
Marriage has six interests (masalih) that are best achieved between equals, making kafa'ah a logical requirement.
5
Note the practical consequence
If a woman marries without kafa'ah, her guardians can annul the marriage before the birth of a child.

معتبر ہوتی ہے نسب میں اس لئے کہ نسب کے ساتھ باہم فخر ہوتا ہے۔ پس قریش بعض بعض کا کفو ہیں اور عرب کفو ہیں بعض کا ۔ اور اصل اس میں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول ہے کہ قریش بعض کفو ہے بعض کا بطن بطن کا۔ مگر یہ کہ نسب مشہور ہو جیسے خاندان خلافت گو یا امام محمد نے کہا شان خلافت کو ظاہر کرنے اور فتنہ کو دور کرنے کے لئے ۔ اور بنو باہلہ عامتہ العرب کا کفو نہیں۔ اس لئے کہ وہ معروف بالخساستہ ہیں۔ تشریح مبسوط میں ہے کہ مرد کے حق میں کفاءت معتبر ہوگی۔ نسب حریت، مال، پیشہ اور حسب میں۔ اور بعض نے تقویٰ ، اسلام اور عقل کا بھی اضافہ کیا ہے۔ اور منہاج میں ہے کہ امام شافعی کفاءۃ کا اعتبار کرنے میں سلامت عیوب ،عفت اور پیشہ میں ۔ امام احمد دین اور مذہب کا بھی اضافہ کرتے ہیں۔ مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ نسب ہیں کفاءت معتبر ہے۔ کیونکہ نسب کے ساتھ بھی آپس میں ایکدوسرے پر فخر کرتے ہیں۔ اور جو چیز ایسی ہو کہ اس ساتھ لوگ فخر کرتے ہیں کفاءت کا اعتبار کیا گیا ہے پس ایک قریشی دوسرے قریشی کا کفو ہو گا۔ اور قریش کے علاوہ ایک عرب دوسرے عرب کا کفو ہوگا۔ دلیل اس سلسلے میں فرمان رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم ہے کہ قریش آپس میں ایک دوسرے کا کفو ہیں ۔ ایک بطن دوسرے بطن کا اور عرب آپس میں ایک دوسرے کا کفو ہیں ایک قبیلہ دوسرے قبیلہ کا۔ اور غیر عرب اعاجم آپس میں ایک دوسرے کا کفو ہیں۔ ایک مرد دوسرے مرد کا۔ اور قریش میں باہم ایک دوسرے پر فضیلت معتبر نہیں۔ بیان کردہ حدیث کی وجہ سے۔ لہذا ہر قریشی دوسرے قریشی کا کفو بن جائے گا۔ کیونکہ حدیث الائمته من قریش کی وجہ سے ہر قریشی میں خلافت کی صلاحیت و اہلیت ہوتی ہے۔ البتہ قریش کے علاوہ دوسرے عرب قریش کا کفو نہیں بن سکتے۔ کیونکہ قریش کے علاوہ دوسرے عرب میں خلافت کی صلاحیت نہیں ہے۔ پس غیر قریش عرب قریش کے مساوی نہیں ہیں۔ لہذا کفو بھی نہیں بن سکتے ہیں۔ امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ قریش میں باہم ایک دوسرے پر فضیلت نہیں ہے۔ ہاں مگر کوئی نسب مشہور ہو۔ جیسے خاندان خلافت پس اس مشہور خاندان میں تفاضل معتبر ہوگا۔ چنانچہ قریش میں سے خاندان خلافت کی لڑکی
Chapter on Kafa'ah. Translation: The chapter on the explanation of kafa'ah. Kafa'ah is considered in marriage. He (the Prophet) said, 'Beware, do not marry women except through guardians, and do not marry except to equals.' And because the arrangement of interests usually occurs between two equals, because a noble woman refuses to be a bed for a base man. So it is necessary to consider kafa'ah, unlike the woman's side, because the husband is the one who makes the bed, so the lowness of the bed does not anger him. And if a woman marries herself to a non-eligant (ghayr kufu), then the guardians have the right to separate them to repel the harm of shame from themselves. Translation: The condition of kufu (equality) is considered in marriage. The Prophet said: 'Beware, do not marry women except through guardians, and do not marry except to equals.' And because the arrangement of interests can usually be achieved between two equals. Because a noble woman will refuse to be the bed of a base man. So it is necessary to consider kafa'ah, unlike the woman's side, because the husband is the one who makes the bed, so the lowness of the bed will not make him angry. And when a woman marries herself without kufu, the guardians have the right to separate them to repel the harm of shame from themselves. Explanation: The meaning of kafa'ah is equality, similarity, peer, equal. Kafa'ah in marriage is that the husband is equal to the woman in his lineage, nobility, religion, age, beauty, etc. The consideration of kafa'ah in marriage is so that the guardians' right of annulment is removed and the marriage becomes binding. The evidence for the validity of kufu in marriage is the statement of the Prophet: 'Beware, do not marry women except through guardians, and do not marry except to equals,' i.e., kufu. According to muhaddithun, this hadith is not of a level that can be used as evidence, because some narrators are accused of lying. The more authentic hadith is that of Ali, which al-Tirmidhi narrated. The translation of that hadith is: 'There are three things that should not be delayed: prayer when its time comes, the funeral when it is present, and an unmarried woman when a kufu is found for her.' The second rational proof is that marriage has six interests, and those interests can be fully achieved only when the marriage is contracted between equals. Therefore, we say that for achieving the interests of marriage, it is necessary that kufu exists. Hence, the consideration of kafa'ah is necessary. However, kafa'ah is not considered on the woman's side; if a man is of noble family and the woman is of lower family, there is no harm. Because the husband is the one who makes the bed, so the bed being low and inferior will not anger him. Now a branched example: if a woman marries herself without kufu, then her guardians have the right to obtain her for themselves to repel the harm of shame. But this right of annulment is before the woman gives birth to a child. After the child is born, the guardians do not retain the right of annulment. Kafa'ah will be considered in lineage. Then kafa'ah is considered in lineage, because it is by lineage that mutual pride occurs. So Quraysh are equals of one another, and Arabs are equals of one another. The basis for this is the statement of the Prophet: 'Quraysh are equals of one another, lineage by lineage; and Arabs are equals of one another, tribe by tribe; and the non-Arabs (mawali) are equals of one another, man by man.' And superiority among Quraysh is not considered because of what we have narrated. And it is narrated from Muhammad (Imam Muhammad) that unless it is a famous lineage like the family of the caliphate, as if he said to glorify the caliphate and calm the fitna. And Banu Bahilah are not equals of the common Arabs because they are known for lowliness. Translation: Then kafa'ah is considered in lineage because it is by lineage that mutual pride occurs. So Quraysh are equals of one another, and Arabs are equals of one another. The basis for this is the statement of the Prophet: 'Quraysh are equals of one another, lineage by lineage; and among Arabs, some tribes are equals of other tribes; and the non-Arabs are equals of one another, man by man.' And among Quraysh, superiority of one over another is not considered because of the hadith we narrated. And it is narrated from Imam Muhammad that unless it is a famous lineage like the family of the caliphate, as if he said to manifest the glory of the caliphate and to calm the fitna. And Banu Bahilah are not equals of the common Arabs because they are known for lowliness. Explanation: In al-Mabsut, it is stated that kafa'ah is considered for the man in lineage, freedom, wealth, profession, and social standing. And some have added piety, Islam, and intelligence. And in al-Minhaj, it is stated that Imam al-Shafi'i considers kafa'ah in freedom from defects, chastity, and profession. Imam Ahmad adds religion and school. The author says: That kafa'ah is considered in lineage. Because it is by lineage that people pride themselves on one another. And whatever thing is such that people take pride in it, kafa'ah is considered in it. So one Qurayshi is the kufu of another Qurayshi. And besides Quraysh, one Arab is the kufu of another Arab. The proof in this matter is the statement of the Messenger of God: 'Quraysh are equals of one another, one lineage equals another lineage; and Arabs are equals of one another, one tribe equals another tribe; and non-Arab foreigners (ajam) are equals of one another, one man equals another man.' And among Quraysh, superiority of one over another is not considered due to the mentioned hadith. Therefore, every Qurayshi becomes the kufu of another Qurayshi, because due to the hadith 'The leaders (imams) are from Quraysh', every Qurayshi has the potential and qualification for the caliphate. But besides Quraysh, other Arabs cannot become the kufu of Quraysh, because other Arabs besides Quraysh do not have the potential for the caliphate. Thus, non-Quraysh Arabs are not equal to Quraysh, therefore they cannot become kufu. Imam Muhammad says that among Quraysh, superiority of one over another is not present. Yes, unless there is a famous lineage, like the family of the caliphate, then in that famous lineage, superiority is considered. So, among Quraysh, the daughter of the caliphal family...
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive explanation of kafa'ah (suitability/equality) in marriage from the Hidayah commentary. It begins by defining kafa'ah and stating that it is considered in marriage. The proof includes a hadith (though noted as weak by muhaddithun) and a stronger hadith from Ali (ra) narrated by al-Tirmidhi, along with rational proof related to the six interests (masalih) of marriage. The text clarifies that kafa'ah is only required from the husband's side, not the wife's, as the husband is the one who 'makes the bed' and the lowness of the bed does not anger him. It then details that if a woman marries without kafa'ah, her guardians have the right to annul the marriage before the birth of a child. The second part focuses on kafa'ah in lineage. It states that Quraysh are equals of one another, Arabs are equals of one another, and non-Arabs (mawali or ajam) are equals of one another. No superiority is considered among Quraysh in general, except as per Imam Muhammad's view that notable lineages like the caliphal house are an exception where superiority is recognized. The Banu Bahilah are excluded from being kufu of common Arabs due to their low status. The tashrih (explanation) adds that kafa'ah is also considered in freedom, wealth, profession, and social standing, with some including piety, Islam, and intellect. It briefly mentions the differences with Shafi'i and Hanbali schools regarding the factors of kafa'ah.

Key Terms
کفاءت (kafa'ah): Equality between spouses in marriage, primarily in lineage, freedom, wealth, profession, and social standing.
کفو (kufu): An equal, suitable match in the context of marriage.
نسب (nasab): Lineage or family descent.
موالی (mawali): Non-Arab freedmen or clients; considered equals among themselves for kafa'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the strongest hadith evidence for kafa'ah in marriage?
A) The hadith 'Do not marry women except through guardians and do not marry except to equals.'
B) The hadith of Ali (ra) about delaying three things, narrated by al-Tirmidhi.
C) The rational proof of the six interests.
D) The consensus of muhaddithun.

Key Takeaway
Kafa'ah is a required consideration for the husband's side, established through hadith and rationality, and its absence gives guardians a limited right of annulment.

Kafa'ah in Lineage: Rules for Quraysh, Arabs, and Non-Arabs
Details the rules of kafa'ah in lineage, with specific categories for Quraysh, Arabs, and non-Arabs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to categorize the three groups for kafa'ah in lineage (Quraysh, Arabs, non-Arabs) and state the exceptional view of Imam Muhammad regarding the caliphal house.

Core Idea
Lineage is the primary factor: Quraysh equals Quraysh, Arabs equals Arabs, non-Arabs equals non-Arabs, with a rare exception for the caliphal house.

This lesson builds on the general concept of kafa'ah by focusing on lineage. The text provides a specific hadith that divides people into three categories for marriage suitability: Quraysh, Arabs, and non-Arabs (mawali). We will explore each category and note an intra-Hanafi difference regarding famous lineages.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule for Quraysh
Quraysh are equals of one another in lineage.
2
Identify the rule for Arabs
Arabs (non-Quraysh) are equals of one another.
3
Identify the rule for non-Arabs (mawali)
Non-Arabs are equals of one another.
4
Note the exception from Imam Muhammad
A famous lineage like the caliphal house among Quraysh may be considered superior.
5
Apply the rule to Banu Bahilah
They are not equal to common Arabs due to their low status.

عیوب ،عفت اور پیشہ میں ۔ امام احمد دین اور مذہب کا بھی اضافہ کرتے ہیں۔ مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ نسب ہیں کفاءت معتبر ہے۔ کیونکہ نسب کے ساتھ بھی آپس میں ایکدوسرے پر فخر کرتے ہیں۔ اور جو چیز ایسی ہو کہ اس ساتھ لوگ فخر کرتے ہیں کفاءت کا اعتبار کیا گیا ہے پس ایک قریشی دوسرے قریشی کا کفو ہو گا۔ اور قریش کے علاوہ ایک عرب دوسرے عرب کا کفو ہوگا۔ دلیل اس سلسلے میں فرمان رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم ہے کہ قریش آپس میں ایک دوسرے کا کفو ہیں ۔ ایک بطن دوسرے بطن کا اور عرب آپس میں ایک دوسرے کا کفو ہیں ایک قبیلہ دوسرے قبیلہ کا۔ اور غیر عرب اعاجم آپس میں ایک دوسرے کا کفو ہیں۔ ایک مرد دوسرے مرد کا۔ اور قریش میں باہم ایک دوسرے پر فضیلت معتبر نہیں۔ بیان کردہ حدیث کی وجہ سے۔ لہذا ہر قریشی دوسرے قریشی کا کفو بن جائے گا۔ کیونکہ حدیث الائمته من قریش کی وجہ سے ہر قریشی میں خلافت کی صلاحیت و اہلیت ہوتی ہے۔ البتہ قریش کے علاوہ دوسرے عرب قریش کا کفو نہیں بن سکتے۔ کیونکہ قریش کے علاوہ دوسرے عرب میں خلافت کی صلاحیت نہیں ہے۔ پس غیر قریش عرب قریش کے مساوی نہیں ہیں۔ لہذا کفو بھی نہیں بن سکتے ہیں۔ امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ قریش میں باہم ایک دوسرے پر فضیلت نہیں ہے۔ ہاں مگر کوئی نسب مشہور ہو۔ جیسے خاندان خلافت پس اس مشہور خاندان میں تفاضل معتبر ہوگا۔ چنانچہ قریش میں سے خاندان خلافت کی لڑکی
Chapter on Kafa'ah. Translation: The chapter on the explanation of kafa'ah. Kafa'ah is considered in marriage. He (the Prophet) said, 'Beware, do not marry women except through guardians, and do not marry except to equals.' And because the arrangement of interests usually occurs between two equals, because a noble woman refuses to be a bed for a base man. So it is necessary to consider kafa'ah, unlike the woman's side, because the husband is the one who makes the bed, so the lowness of the bed does not anger him. And if a woman marries herself to a non-eligant (ghayr kufu), then the guardians have the right to separate them to repel the harm of shame from themselves. Translation: The condition of kufu (equality) is considered in marriage. The Prophet said: 'Beware, do not marry women except through guardians, and do not marry except to equals.' And because the arrangement of interests can usually be achieved between two equals. Because a noble woman will refuse to be the bed of a base man. So it is necessary to consider kafa'ah, unlike the woman's side, because the husband is the one who makes the bed, so the lowness of the bed will not make him angry. And when a woman marries herself without kufu, the guardians have the right to separate them to repel the harm of shame from themselves. Explanation: The meaning of kafa'ah is equality, similarity, peer, equal. Kafa'ah in marriage is that the husband is equal to the woman in his lineage, nobility, religion, age, beauty, etc. The consideration of kafa'ah in marriage is so that the guardians' right of annulment is removed and the marriage becomes binding. The evidence for the validity of kufu in marriage is the statement of the Prophet: 'Beware, do not marry women except through guardians, and do not marry except to equals,' i.e., kufu. According to muhaddithun, this hadith is not of a level that can be used as evidence, because some narrators are accused of lying. The more authentic hadith is that of Ali, which al-Tirmidhi narrated. The translation of that hadith is: 'There are three things that should not be delayed: prayer when its time comes, the funeral when it is present, and an unmarried woman when a kufu is found for her.' The second rational proof is that marriage has six interests, and those interests can be fully achieved only when the marriage is contracted between equals. Therefore, we say that for achieving the interests of marriage, it is necessary that kufu exists. Hence, the consideration of kafa'ah is necessary. However, kafa'ah is not considered on the woman's side; if a man is of noble family and the woman is of lower family, there is no harm. Because the husband is the one who makes the bed, so the bed being low and inferior will not anger him. Now a branched example: if a woman marries herself without kufu, then her guardians have the right to obtain her for themselves to repel the harm of shame. But this right of annulment is before the woman gives birth to a child. After the child is born, the guardians do not retain the right of annulment. Kafa'ah will be considered in lineage. Then kafa'ah is considered in lineage, because it is by lineage that mutual pride occurs. So Quraysh are equals of one another, and Arabs are equals of one another. The basis for this is the statement of the Prophet: 'Quraysh are equals of one another, lineage by lineage; and Arabs are equals of one another, tribe by tribe; and the non-Arabs (mawali) are equals of one another, man by man.' And superiority among Quraysh is not considered because of what we have narrated. And it is narrated from Muhammad (Imam Muhammad) that unless it is a famous lineage like the family of the caliphate, as if he said to glorify the caliphate and calm the fitna. And Banu Bahilah are not equals of the common Arabs because they are known for lowliness. Translation: Then kafa'ah is considered in lineage because it is by lineage that mutual pride occurs. So Quraysh are equals of one another, and Arabs are equals of one another. The basis for this is the statement of the Prophet: 'Quraysh are equals of one another, lineage by lineage; and among Arabs, some tribes are equals of other tribes; and the non-Arabs are equals of one another, man by man.' And among Quraysh, superiority of one over another is not considered because of the hadith we narrated. And it is narrated from Imam Muhammad that unless it is a famous lineage like the family of the caliphate, as if he said to manifest the glory of the caliphate and to calm the fitna. And Banu Bahilah are not equals of the common Arabs because they are known for lowliness. Explanation: In al-Mabsut, it is stated that kafa'ah is considered for the man in lineage, freedom, wealth, profession, and social standing. And some have added piety, Islam, and intelligence. And in al-Minhaj, it is stated that Imam al-Shafi'i considers kafa'ah in freedom from defects, chastity, and profession. Imam Ahmad adds religion and school. The author says: That kafa'ah is considered in lineage. Because it is by lineage that people pride themselves on one another. And whatever thing is such that people take pride in it, kafa'ah is considered in it. So one Qurayshi is the kufu of another Qurayshi. And besides Quraysh, one Arab is the kufu of another Arab. The proof in this matter is the statement of the Messenger of God: 'Quraysh are equals of one another, one lineage equals another lineage; and Arabs are equals of one another, one tribe equals another tribe; and non-Arab foreigners (ajam) are equals of one another, one man equals another man.' And among Quraysh, superiority of one over another is not considered due to the mentioned hadith. Therefore, every Qurayshi becomes the kufu of another Qurayshi, because due to the hadith 'The leaders (imams) are from Quraysh', every Qurayshi has the potential and qualification for the caliphate. But besides Quraysh, other Arabs cannot become the kufu of Quraysh, because other Arabs besides Quraysh do not have the potential for the caliphate. Thus, non-Quraysh Arabs are not equal to Quraysh, therefore they cannot become kufu. Imam Muhammad says that among Quraysh, superiority of one over another is not present. Yes, unless there is a famous lineage, like the family of the caliphate, then in that famous lineage, superiority is considered. So, among Quraysh, the daughter of the caliphal family...
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive explanation of kafa'ah (suitability/equality) in marriage from the Hidayah commentary. It begins by defining kafa'ah and stating that it is considered in marriage. The proof includes a hadith (though noted as weak by muhaddithun) and a stronger hadith from Ali (ra) narrated by al-Tirmidhi, along with rational proof related to the six interests (masalih) of marriage. The text clarifies that kafa'ah is only required from the husband's side, not the wife's, as the husband is the one who 'makes the bed' and the lowness of the bed does not anger him. It then details that if a woman marries without kafa'ah, her guardians have the right to annul the marriage before the birth of a child. The second part focuses on kafa'ah in lineage. It states that Quraysh are equals of one another, Arabs are equals of one another, and non-Arabs (mawali or ajam) are equals of one another. No superiority is considered among Quraysh in general, except as per Imam Muhammad's view that notable lineages like the caliphal house are an exception where superiority is recognized. The Banu Bahilah are excluded from being kufu of common Arabs due to their low status. The tashrih (explanation) adds that kafa'ah is also considered in freedom, wealth, profession, and social standing, with some including piety, Islam, and intellect. It briefly mentions the differences with Shafi'i and Hanbali schools regarding the factors of kafa'ah.

Key Terms
کفاءت (kafa'ah): Equality between spouses in marriage, primarily in lineage, freedom, wealth, profession, and social standing.
نسب (nasab): Lineage or family descent.
موالی (mawali): Non-Arab freedmen or clients; considered equals among themselves for kafa'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Non-Arabs are equal to Quraysh.
B) Arabs are equal to Quraysh.
C) Quraysh are equal to one another.
D) All humans are equal regardless of lineage.

Key Takeaway
Kafa'ah in lineage follows a three-tier division: Quraysh, Arabs, and non-Arabs, each internal group equal, with a possible exception for famous lineages.

Kafa'ah in Lineage Among Quraysh, Arabs, and Mawali
Explains kafa'ah in lineage with hadith evidence and exception for famous nobility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on kafa'ah in lineage for Quraysh, Arabs, and mawali, and explain the exception for famous noble lineages.

Core Idea
Kafa'ah in lineage is defined by the Prophet's hadith: Quraysh, Arabs, and mawali each are kufu' among themselves, with an exception for famously noble families.

Kafa'ah (suitability) in marriage is a key condition in Hanafi fiqh, particularly in lineage (nasab). This lesson examines the ruling based on a prophetic hadith that classifies Quraysh, Arabs, and non-Arab converts (mawali) into separate suitability groups. We will also explore an intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding exceptions for famously noble lineages, such as the family of the Caliphate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its dalil
The passage states that kafa'ah is considered in lineage because it is a basis for boasting. The ruling is derived from the Prophet's hadith that defines mutual suitability within specific groups.
The hadith is the primary evidence; note its classification as ahad.
2
Analyze the hadith's classification
The hadith divides people into three categories: Quraysh are kufu' for each other clan for clan; Arabs are kufu' for each other tribe for tribe; mawali are kufu' for each other man for man. 'Superiority among Quraysh is not considered.'
This establishes a general rule of equivalence within each category.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi exception
Imam Muhammad states an exception: a family with a famously noble lineage, like the Caliphal house, is not considered kufu' for other Quraysh due to honor and prevention of fitna.
The majority view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) does not accept this exception.
4
Note the practical consequence
The exception means that a woman from a famous noble family could object to marrying a non-famous Qurayshi man based on lineage superiority.
The mufta bihi is the majority view, but the exception is cautionary.
5
Apply the ruling to another group
Banu Bahilah are not kufu' even for general Arabs due to their lowliness, showing that factors beyond lineage can affect suitability.
This demonstrates that 'urf (custom) and known character may also play a role.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الكفاءة تعتبر في النسب لانه يقع به التفاخر فقريش بعضهم اكفاء لبعض والعرب بعضهم اكفاء لبعض و الأصل فيه قوله عليه السلام قريش بعضهم اكفاء لبعض بطن ببطن والعرب بعضهم اكفاء لبعض قبيلة بقبيلة والموالي بعضهم اكفاء لبعض رجل برجل ولا يعتبر التفاضل فيما بين قريش لما روينا وعن محمد الا ان يكون نسبا مشهورا كاهل بيت الخلافة كانه قال تعظيما للخلافة و تسكينا للفتنة وبنو باهلة ليسوا باكفاء العامة العرب لانهم معروفون بالخساسة
Then kafa'ah is considered in lineage because boasting occurs with it. So Quraysh are kufu' for each other, and Arabs are kufu' for each other. The basis of this is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Quraysh are kufu' for each other, clan for clan; and Arabs are kufu' for each other, tribe for tribe; and the mawali are kufu' for each other, man for man.' And superiority is not considered among Quraysh due to what we have narrated. And from Muhammad: except if there is a famous lineage like the family of the Caliphate, as if he said to honor the Caliphate and to calm sedition. And Banu Bahilah are not kufu' for the general Arabs because they are known for lowliness.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah. The author establishes that suitability (kafa'ah) for marriage is considered in lineage (nasab) because it is a basis for boasting—a factor that can cause harm to the family. He then cites the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) to define the levels: within Quraysh, all are kufu' for each other regardless of branch; similarly, all Arabs are kufu' for each other, and non-Arab converts (mawali) are kufu' among themselves. Superiority within Quraysh is not considered, upholding the principle that all Quraysh are equal in eligibility to marry each other. However, Imam Muhammad makes an exception for a family of famously high lineage, such as the Caliphal house (Banu Hashim), to maintain honor and prevent fitna. Finally, the author notes that Banu Bahilah, known for vile practices, are not kufu' even for general Arabs.

Key Terms
كفاءة (kafa'ah): Equality in lineage, freedom, wealth, and profession between spouses for valid marriage.
نسب (nasab): Lineage or ancestry; the chain of forefathers.
قريش (Quraysh): The tribe of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him); all its clans are considered equal in kafa'ah.
موالي (mawali): Non-Arab converts to Islam; their kafa'ah is based on generations of Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited, which groups are kufu' for each other?
A) Quraysh are kufu' for all Arabs
B) Quraysh are kufu' for each other, Arabs for each other, and mawali for each other
C) All Muslims are kufu' regardless of lineage
D) Only Quraysh are kufu' for each other

Key Takeaway
Kafa'ah in lineage is based on the Prophet's hadith dividing people into groups, with an intra-Hanafi exception for famously noble families and a recognition that known lowliness can also affect suitability.

Kafa'ah Among Mawali: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Muslim Ancestors
Specifies rulings on kafa'ah for non-Arab converts based on their ancestors' Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on kafa'ah among mawali and explain the intra-madhhab difference between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding the number of Muslim ancestors required.

Core Idea
Among mawali, kafa'ah requires at least two Muslim ancestors; Abu Yusuf suffices with one.

In Hanafi fiqh, kafa'ah (compatibility) is a condition for valid marriage, especially regarding lineage. For non-Arab converts (mawali), the depth of family Islam matters. This passage from al-Hidayah presents the standard Hanafi view and a minority opinion from Abu Yusuf, giving us a window into how the school handles ikhtilaf within its own ranks.

Guided Path
1
State the majority Hanafi position
Identify the ruling for mawali: whoever has two Muslim ancestors (father and grandfather) is kufu' for those with more; a fresh convert or one with only one Muslim ancestor is not kufu' for two.
The ta'lil (reason) is that lineage completion requires both father and grandfather.
2
Identify Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf equates one Muslim ancestor with two, so a mawla with a Muslim father is kufu' for one with two.
He uses a different definition of lineage completion.
3
Follow Abu Yusuf's proof
His basis is that the father alone suffices for lineage; he attaches (yulhiq) the one to the two.
This is consistent with his methodology in other definitions.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The majority insists on two ancestors, because boasting among mawali is by generations of Islam, and lineage completeness requires both father and grandfather.
The response highlights the criterion of boasting (tafakhur) as the basis for grading.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: under the majority, a mawla with one Muslim father is not kufu' for one with two; under Abu Yusuf, he is. This affects the guardian's right to object.
The mufta bihi follows the majority, so the objection is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واما الموالي فمن كان له ابوان في الاسلام فصاعدا فهو من الاكفاء يعنى لمن له آباء فيه ومن اسلم بنفسه او له اب واحد في الاسلام لا يكون كفو لمن له ابوان في الاسلام لان تمام النسب بالاب والجد وابو يوسف الحق الواحد بالمثنى كما هو مذهبه في التعريف ومن اسلم بنفسه لا يكون كفو لمن له اب واحد في الاسلام لان التفاخر فيما بين الموالي بالاسلام والكفاءة في الحرية نظيرها في الاسلام في جميع ما ذكرنا لان الرق اثر الكفر وفيه معنى الذل فيعتبر في حكم الكفاءة
And as for the mawali, whoever has two fathers (i.e., father and grandfather) in Islam and above, he is among the kufu', meaning for one who has many ancestors in it. And whoever embraced Islam himself, or has one father in Islam, is not kufu' for one who has two fathers in Islam, because completion of lineage is by the father and grandfather. And Abu Yusuf attached the one to the two, as is his madhhab in definition. And whoever embraced Islam himself is not kufu' for one who has one father in Islam, because boasting among the mawali is through Islam. And kafa'ah in freedom is analogous to that in Islam in all that we have mentioned, because slavery is an effect of disbelief and it contains the meaning of humiliation, so it is considered in the ruling of kafa'ah.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage details intra-Hanafi differences regarding kafa'ah among non-Arab Muslims (mawali). The mainstream position (apparently Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) considers a mawla with two Muslim ancestors (father and grandfather) as kufu' for those with more ancestors. A mawla with only one Muslim father or a fresh convert is not kufu' for those with two ancestors, because lineage completeness requires both father and grandfather. Abu Yusuf, however, equates one Muslim ancestor (father) with two, thereby considering one ancestor sufficient for kafa'ah with those having two. His view is based on a different definition of lineage completion. The passage also draws an analogy with freedom: just as kafa'ah in freedom is graded (free vs. slave), kafa'ah in Islam is graded by generations of faith, because slavery stems from disbelief and humiliation.

Key Terms
ابوان (abawān): Two ancestors: father and grandfather (both Muslim).
الموالي (al-mawālī): Non-Arab Muslims, especially recent converts with limited Muslim ancestry.
حرية (ḥurriyyah): Freedom; being freeborn as opposed to a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A fresh convert
B) A mawla with one Muslim father
C) A mawla with two Muslim ancestors (father and grandfather)
D) No mawla is kufu' for one with three ancestors

Key Takeaway
The majority Hanafi view requires at least two Muslim ancestors for kafa'ah among mawali; Abu Yusuf's minority view considers one sufficient.

Kafa'ah among Quraysh and the Low Status of Banu Bahilah
Expansion of kafa'ah rulings for Arabs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kafa'ah between Qurayshi sub-groups and explain why Banu Bahilah are not considered equal to any Arab.

Core Idea
A Qurayshi woman from the ruling family is not equal to a Qurayshi man from a lower lineage; Banu Bahilah are too low for any Arab.

In Hanafi marriage law, kafa'ah (equality in lineage) is a right of guardians, not a condition of validity. This passage clarifies the nuanced gradations within Quraysh and introduces an extreme case: Banu Bahilah, a tribe so base that they cannot be kufu' to any Arab, not even the general masses. Understanding these distinctions helps you apply the guardian's right of objection in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the various Qurayshi lineages mentioned
Distinguish between Quraysh from the ruling family (khilafat) and other Quraysh. The text gives an example: a woman from the ruling family marries a man outside it.
The ruling family here refers to Banu Hashim, from which the caliphs came.
2
Determine the legal consequence of this disparity
The marriage is valid (sahih) but the guardians have the right to object (haqq al-i'tirad). Kafa'ah is not a condition for validity but a right that can void the marriage if challenged.
This is a key Hanafi distinction.
3
Analyze the case of Banu Bahilah
Banu Bahilah are considered so low due to their practice of boiling animal bones for grease that they are not equal to any Arab, even the general masses (ammat al-'arab).
This ruling is based on 'urf (custom) and known despicable behavior.
4
Explore the tribal hierarchy defined in the benefit (fa'idah)
The passage outlines six levels: Sha'b, Qabilah, 'Imarah, Batn, Fakhdh, Fasilah. Quraysh is at the 'Imarah level. This shows that lineage classification matters in kafa'ah.
This helps contextualize Quraysh's standing among Arab tribes.

دوسرے قریش کی جو خاندان خلافت سے نہیں ہے ۔ حتی کہ قریشیہ بالغہ جو خاندان خلافت سے ہے اس نے نکاح کر لیا کسی ایسے قریش سے جو خاندان خلافت سے نہیں تو اولیاء کو حق اعتراض ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ امام محمد کا نسب مشہور کا استثناء کرنا گویا ان کے پیش نظر خاندان خلافت کی تعظیم اور فتنہ کو دور کرتا ہے۔ آخر میں فرماتے ہیں کہ عرب میں ایک خاندان بنو باہلہ کا ہے۔ وہ عامتہ العرب کا کفو نہیں ہوں گے ۔ اس لئے کہ ان کے بارے میں مشہور ہے کہ وہ مردار کی ہڈیاں لیکر ان کو جوش دیتے ہیں اور ان کی چکنائی لیتے ہیں۔ پس یہ خاندان انتہائی پست اور دنی ہے اس لئے ان کو عام غرب کا کفو بھی نہیں بنایا جا سکتا ہے۔
فوائد قریش وہ لوگ کہلائیں گے جو نسر ابن کنانہ کی اولاد سے ہیں اور جونضر بن کنانہ کی اولاد سے نہیں وہ غیر قریش ہیں۔ زبیرا بن بکار نے بیان کیا کہ عرب کے چھ طبقات ہیں۔ شعب ، قبیہ ، عمارہ، بطن، فحد ، فصیلہ شعب سے اوپر ہے بہت سے قبیلوں کا جامع ہے اور قبیل با مع ہے عمارہ کو اور عماره لبطون کو اور بطن افخاذ کو اور فخذ فصائل کو پس مضر اور ربیعہ شعب ہیں اور کنانہ قبیلہ ہے اور قریش عمارہ اور قصی بطن اور ہاشم فید اور عباس فصیلہ ہے۔ مینی شرح بدایه )
Regarding other Quraysh who are not from the ruling family of the caliphate. Even if a mature Qurayshi woman who is from the ruling family marries a Qurayshi man who is not from the ruling family, the guardians will have the right to object. The author of Al-Hidayah says that Imam Muhammad's exception of the well-known lineage is, as it were, to honor the ruling family and to prevent fitna. Finally he says that there is a family in the Arabs called Banu Bahilah. They will not be equal (kufu) to the general Arabs. Because it is well-known about them that they take bones of dead animals, boil them, and extract their grease. So this family is extremely low and base; therefore they cannot even be considered equal to the general Arabs. Benefit: Quraysh are those who are from the descendants of al-Nadr ibn Kinanah, and those who are not from the descendants of al-Nadr ibn Kinanah are not Quraysh. Zubayr ibn Bakkar stated that the Arabs have six levels: Sha'b, Qabilah, 'Imarah, Batn, Fakhdh, Fasilah. Sha'b is above, encompassing many tribes; Qabilah includes 'Imarah; 'Imarah includes Batn; Batn includes Afkhadh; Fakhdh includes Fasa'il. So Mudar and Rabi'ah are Sha'b; Kinanah is Qabilah; Quraysh is 'Imarah; Qusayy is Batn; Hashim is Fakhdh; and 'Abbas is Fasilah. (From Sharh Bidayah)
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement elaborating on kafa'ah among Arabs, specifically within the Quraysh tribe and a despised sub-tribe. The author explains that a Qurayshi woman from the caliphal lineage (like Banu Hashim) cannot marry a Qurayshi man from a lesser lineage without the guardians' right to object. Sahib al-Hidayah notes that Imam Muhammad's mention of 'well-known lineage' aims to honor the ruling family and avoid discord. The example of Banu Bahilah shows that some tribes are so low that they are not equal to any Arab, not even the general Arabs, due to their repugnant practices. The benefit (fa'idah) defines Quraysh as descendants of al-Nadr ibn Kinanah and classifies Arab tribal levels, placing Quraysh at the 'Imarah level. This lesson clarifies that kafa'ah among Arabs considers lineage gradations, not just common Arab identity.

Key Terms
قریش (Quraysh): The tribe descended from al-Nadr ibn Kinanah, distinct from other Arab tribes. Within Quraysh, there are sub-groups like the ruling family (khilafat).
کفو (kufu'): Equality in marriage compatibility, considering lineage, religion, freedom, and profession.
عامتہ العرب (ammat al-'arab): The general masses of Arabs, as opposed to specific noble or low tribes.
بنو باہلہ (banu bahilah): A specific Arab tribe known for despicable practices, thus not equal to any Arab in kafa'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is Banu Bahilah not considered equal to the general Arabs?
A) They are not pure Arabs by lineage.
B) They engage in despicable practices like boiling dead animal bones for grease.
C) They are a very small tribe.
D) They are non-Muslims.

Key Takeaway
Kafa'ah among Arabs depends on detailed lineage gradations; even within Quraysh, the ruling family is distinct, and tribes like Banu Bahilah are considered too low to be equal to any Arab.

Kafa'ah among Non-Arabs: Lineage in Islam and Freedom
Ruling with proof: kafa'ah lineage requirements for non-Arabs and analogy for freedom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi requirements for kafa'ah among non-Arabs regarding lineage in Islam and freedom, and identify the intra-Hanafi difference with Abu Yusuf's view.

Core Idea
Kafa'ah among non-Arabs requires two Muslim ancestors; one is insufficient because Islam is the basis of honor.

In Hanafi law, marriage suitability (kafa'ah) depends on equality in lineage, Islam, freedom, and other factors. This passage focuses on how these criteria apply specifically to non-Arab Muslims (mawali), detailing the number of Muslim ancestors required and the treatment of freedom. Understanding this ruling helps you assess potential guardians' objections in marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The kafa'ah (equality) of a non-Arab man for a non-Arab woman based on lineage in Islam and freedom.
Kafa'ah is a condition affecting the right of guardians to object to a marriage.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited for the ruling on freedom? The text uses qiyas: slavery is an effect of disbelief and entails humiliation.
Dalil: 'لان الرق اثر الكفر وفيه معنى الذل'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the proof establish the ruling? Just as there is no kafa'ah between Muslim and disbeliever, there is none between free and slave because both pairs involve honor vs. humiliation.
Slavery is analogized to disbelief, so the same rule applies.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Which scholar differs? Abu Yusuf holds that one Muslim ancestor suffices, analogizing to witness identification where only the father's name is needed.
His reasoning is rejected by the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad).
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is relied upon and why? The majority view (two ancestors) is the mufta bihi because completeness of lineage requires both father and grandfather, and boasting among non-Arabs is through depth of Islam.
The text dismisses Abu Yusuf's analogy as inapplicable.

دوسری صورتوں کو اسی پر قیاس کر لیا جائے کفاء ت میں حریت کا اعتبار کرنے پر۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ مملوک ہونا کفر کا اثر ہے گویا کہ کفر ہے۔ پس جس طرح کفر اور اسلام میں کفارت نہیں اسی طرح حریت میں اور رقیت میں بھی کفارت نہیں ہوگی۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ رقیت میں ذلت کے معنی اور حریت میں عزت کے معنی ہیں اس وجہ سے حکم کفاءۃ میں ان کا بھی اعتبار کیا جائے گا۔
As for non-Arabs (mawali): Whoever has two fathers (i.e., father and grandfather) in Islam or more, then he is among the equals (akfa') for one who has many ancestors in Islam. And whoever accepted Islam himself or has only one father in Islam is not equal to one who has two fathers in Islam, because complete lineage (nasab) is through the father and grandfather. Abu Yusuf joined the one (single ancestor) to the two (as per his method in definition). And whoever accepted Islam himself is not equal to one who has one father in Islam, because boasting among non-Arabs is through Islam. And the ruling of kafa'ah in freedom is analogous to that in Islam in all the mentioned cases, because being a slave is an effect of disbelief and contains the meaning of humiliation, so it is considered in the ruling of kafa'ah. (Urdu translation and commentary follow with similar content.) In short: A person whose father and grandfather are both Muslim is equal to one whose father, grandfather, and great-grandfather are Muslim. A person who is Muslim himself but his father is not Muslim, or his father is Muslim but grandfather is not, is not equal to one with two Muslim ancestors. Abu Yusuf analogizes one to two; the original difference is in definition. Abu Yusuf says that in testimony etc., the definition of a witness is complete by mentioning the father's name, not requiring the grandfather; the other view requires both. Freedom's kafa'ah is like Islam: if a person is free and his father and grandfather are free, he is equal to one with many free ancestors. The proof: being a slave is an effect of kufr, so just as there is no kafa'ah between kufr and Islam, there is none between slavery and freedom. Another proof: slavery implies humiliation, freedom implies honor.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) explaining kafa'ah among non-Arabs (mawali) regarding Islam and freedom. The author states that for non-Arabs, the criterion in lineage for Islam is having at least two Muslim ancestors (father and grandfather). A person who converted himself or has only one Muslim ancestor is not equal to one with two. This is because completeness of lineage is achieved through father and grandfather. Abu Yusuf differs: he considers one Muslim ancestor sufficient, by analogy to witness identification where only the father's name is needed. However, the relied-upon view is that both are needed for boasting among non-Arabs occurs through Islam. For freedom, the ruling mirrors that of Islam: a free person with two free ancestors is equal to one with many free ancestors. The proof is that slavery is an effect of disbelief and implies humiliation, so there is no kafa'ah between free and slave, just as there is none between Muslim and disbeliever. This lesson clarifies that kafa'ah among non-Arabs considers not just immediate status but ancestral lineage in Islam and freedom.

Key Terms
موالی (mawali): Non-Arab Muslims, clients, or freedmen; in this context, non-Arabs as opposed to Arabs.
تمام النسب (tamam al-nasab): The completeness of lineage, achieved by mentioning both father and grandfather.
رق (raqq): Slavery; being owned as property.
حریت (hurriyyah): Freedom; being free-born or manumitted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), when is a non-Arab (mawla) considered an equal (kufu') for a non-Arab woman whose ancestors have been Muslim for several generations?
A) If he is a Muslim himself, regardless of his ancestors.
B) If his father was Muslim, even if his grandfather was not.
C) If both his father and grandfather were Muslim.
D) If he has at least one Muslim ancestor.

Key Takeaway
Kafa'ah among non-Arabs requires at least two Muslim ancestors and freedom status, because Islam and freedom are the bases of honor.
