عقد نکاح دو فضولیوں یا ایک فضولی اور ایک اصیل کے درمیان بالا جماع جائز ہے

ولوجرى العقد بين الفضوليين اوبين الفضولي والاصيل جاز بالاجماع هو يقول لو كان مامورا من الجانبين ينفذ فاذا كان فضوليا يتوقف وصار كالخلع والطلاق والاعتاق على مال ولهما ان الموجود شطر العقد لانه شطر حالة الحضرة فكذا عند الغيبة وشطر العقد لا يتوقف على ما وراء المجلس كمافى البيع بخلاف المامور من الجانبين لانه ينتقل كلامه الى العاقدين وماجرى بين الفضوليين عقدتام وكذا الخلع اختاه لانه تصرف يمين من جانبه حتى يلزم فيتم به

ترجمہ اور اگر عقد جاری ہوا دو فضولیوں کے درمیان یا ایک فضولی اور ایک اصیل کے درمیان تو بالا تفاق جائز ہے۔ ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر یہ شخص مامور من الجانبين (وکیل ) ہوتا تو نافذ کیا جاتا۔ پس فضولی ہے تو موقوف رہے گا اور ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ خلع ، طلاق اور اعتاق علی مال۔ اور طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ موجود جز وعقد ہے اس لئے کہ وہ جز ہے موجودگی کی حالت میں ۔ پس ایسا ہی عدم موجودگی میں اور جز عقد ماوراء مجلس پر موقوف نہیں رہتا جیسا کہ بیع میں۔ بخلاف مامور من الجانہین کے۔ اس لئے کہ اس کا کلام منتقل ہو گا عاقدین کی طرف اور جو دو فضولیوں کے درمیان جاری ہوا وہ عقد نام ہے اور ایسے ہی ضلع اور اس کی دونوں نظیر ہیں ۔ اس لئے کہ یہ تصرف یمین ہے مرد کی جانب سے یہاں تک کہ لازم ہوگا اور حالف کے ساتھ پورا ہو جائے گا۔ تشریح ماقبل میں بیان کیا گیا تھا کہ طرفین کے نزدیک آدمی جانبین سے فضولی نہیں بن سکتا ہے۔ البتہ ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ایک آدمی جانبین سے فضولی بننے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے۔ اس جگہ بیان کیا کہ اگر عقد نکاح دو فضولیوں یا ایک فضولی اور ایک اصیل کے درمیان جاری ہواتو بالاتفاق جائز ہے۔ مسئلہ سابق میں ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر یہ شخص دونوں جانب سے وکیل ہوتا تو نکاح نافذ ہو جاتا۔ پس اگر فضولی ہے تو نکاح موقوف رہے گا۔ لہذا ایک ہی شخص دونوں جانب سے فضولی ہو سکتا ہے اور یہ خلع طلاق کے مانند ہو گیا۔ مثلاً شوہر نے کہا کہ میں نے اپنی بیوی سے ہزار روپیہ پر ضلع کیا۔ اور بیوی موجود نہیں پھر اسکو خبر ملی بیوی نے قبول کر لیا تو یہ بالا تفاق جائز ہے۔ جس طرح یہاں صیغہ واحدہ سے عقد خلع درست ہو گیا اسی طرح فضولی واحد کے کلام سے بھی عقد نکاح درست ہونا چاہئے ۔ اسی طرح اگر شوہر نے کہا کہ میں نے اتنی مقدار پر طلاق دی یا مولیٰ نے کہا کہ میں نے اتنی مقدار پر آزاد کیا۔ پھر بیوی اور غلام کوخبر پہنچی اور جس مجلس میں خبر ملی اس میں قبول کر لیا تو بالا تفاق جائز ہے۔ پس اسی طرح عقد نکاح میں ہونا چاہئے کہ اجازت پر موقوف رہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ
فضولی من الجانبين کوضلع ، طلاق اور اعتاق پر قیاس کیا ہے اور جامع ان میں سے ہر ایک کا ایجاب وقبول کا محتاج ہونا ہے۔ طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عقد نکاح تام ہوتا ہے ایجاب اور قبول سے۔ اور متن کے مسئلہ میں اس شخص کا قول کہ گواہ رہو میں نے فلاں عورت سے نکاح کیا ہے۔ یہ قول عقد کا ایک جز ہے۔ یعنی ایجاب اور وجہ یہ ہے کہ اگر زوجین مجلس میں موجود ہوتے تب بھی یہ کلام عقد نکاح کا ایک ہی جز ہوتا۔ یعنی ایجاب۔ لہذا عدم موجودگی میں بھی یہ کلام جزو عقد ہوگا۔ یعنی ایجاب اور جز وعقد ماوراء مجلس پر موقوف
And if the contract occurred between two fudulis or between a fuduli and an asil, it is valid by consensus. He (Abu Yusuf) says: If he was an agent (ma'mur) from both sides, it would be effective; if he is a fuduli, it becomes suspended, and it becomes like khul', talaq, and 'itaq 'ala mal. And the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold: what is present is part of the contract (shatr al-'aqd) because it is part of the contract in the case of presence; so likewise in absence. And part of the contract does not depend on what is beyond the council, as in sale. Unlike the case of an agent from both sides, because his speech transfers to the two contracting parties. And what occurs between two fudulis is a complete contract (tamm). And likewise khul' and its like, because it is a disposition (tasarruf) of the husband on his side, such that it becomes binding and is fulfilled by the oath.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage establishes the consensus (ijma') that a marriage contract conducted between two fudulis (both acting without authority) or between a fuduli and an asil (principal) is valid. The dispute here is not over the validity of such contracts but over the reasoning. Abu Yusuf argues by qiyas (analogy) to khul', talaq, and 'itaq 'ala mal (emancipation for compensation): if a husband unilaterally pronounces khul' or talaq and the absent wife later accepts, it is valid by consensus. Similarly, a single fuduli acting on both sides should be able to contract a marriage that becomes suspended on approval. The two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) argue that what is present in such a case is only one part of the contract (shatr al-'aqd), i.e., the offer, not the acceptance. Since in the presence of both parties the speech would be only the offer, in absence it is also only the offer. A part of a contract does not depend on events beyond the council, as in sale (bay'); sale is not concluded by offer alone. However, when two fudulis act (one from each side), or one fuduli and one asil, the contract has both offer and acceptance from different persons, so it is a complete contract (tamm) requiring only the principals' approval. The commentary further clarifies that acting as agent (wakil) from both sides is permissible, but acting as fuduli from both sides is invalid according to the two, valid according to Abu Yusuf. The practical thamarah (result) is that in the second lesson's scenario, all agree the contract is valid but suspended.

Key Terms
فضولی (fuduli): A person who acts without prior authorization; the text discusses one acting on both sides or on one side.
شطر العقد (shatr al-'aqd): One part (offer or acceptance) of a contract; does not form a complete contract alone.
مامور من الجانبین (ma'mur min al-janibayn): A person appointed as agent (wakil) from both sides of the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, why is a marriage contract between two fudulis valid but the statement of one person saying 'I have married' invalid?
A) Because two fudulis provide a complete contract with both offer and acceptance
B) Because Abu Yusuf allows it
C) Because the marriage is not suspended
D) Because the woman's permission is not needed

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi consensus holds marriage between two fudulis valid but suspended; the authoritative view limits fuduli to one side per person, requiring separate parties for offer and acceptance.

Marriage by Two Fuduli or One Fuduli and One Asl: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on fuduli marriage contracts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a marriage contract by two fuduli and explain the intra-madhhab disagreement between Abu Yusuf and the majority on whether one person can be fuduli from both sides.

Core Idea
Two fuduli can marry: contract valid but suspended. Dispute: can one be fuduli from both sides?

This passage addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: while all agree that a marriage by two unauthorized agents is valid but suspended, the split is on whether a single person can act as fuduli from both sides. Abu Yusuf says yes, analogizing to khul' and talaq; the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) say no, insisting that the contract requires offer and acceptance as distinct parts.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم
یا ایک جانب سے ولی اور دوسری جانب سے اصیل یا ایک جانب سے ولی اور دوسری جانب سے وکیل یادونوں جانب سے وکیل بن سکتا ہے اور رہا یہ کہ ایک آدمی کا دونوں جانب سے اصیل بننا سو یہ امر محال ہے۔
عقد نکاح دو فضولیوں یا ایک فضولی اور ایک اصیل کے درمیان بالا جماع جائز ہے
ولوجرى العقد بين الفضوليين اوبين الفضولي والاصيل جاز بالاجماع هو يقول لو كان مامورا من الجانبين ينفذ فاذا كان فضوليا يتوقف وصار كالخلع والطلاق والاعتاق على مال ولهما ان الموجود شطر العقد لانه شطر حالة الحضرة فكذا عند الغيبة وشطر العقد لا يتوقف على ما وراء المجلس كمافى البيع بخلاف المامور من الجانبين لانه ينتقل كلامه الى العاقدين وماجرى بين الفضوليين عقدتام وكذا الخلع اختاه لانه تصرف يمين من جانبه حتى يلزم فيتم به
ترجمہ اور اگر عقد جاری ہوا دو فضولیوں کے درمیان یا ایک فضولی اور ایک اصیل کے درمیان تو بالا تفاق جائز ہے۔ ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر یہ شخص مامور من الجانبين (وکیل ) ہوتا تو نافذ کیا جاتا۔ پس فضولی ہے تو موقوف رہے گا اور ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ خلع ، طلاق اور اعتاق علی مال۔ اور طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ موجود جز وعقد ہے اس لئے کہ وہ جز ہے موجودگی کی حالت میں ۔ پس ایسا ہی عدم موجودگی میں اور جز عقد ماوراء مجلس پر موقوف نہیں رہتا جیسا کہ بیع میں۔ بخلاف مامور من الجانہین کے۔ اس لئے کہ اس کا کلام منتقل ہو گا عاقدین کی طرف اور جو دو فضولیوں کے درمیان جاری ہوا وہ عقد نام ہے اور ایسے ہی ضلع اور اس کی دونوں نظیر ہیں ۔ اس لئے کہ یہ تصرف یمین ہے مرد کی جانب سے یہاں تک کہ لازم ہوگا اور حالف کے ساتھ پورا ہو جائے گا۔ تشریح ماقبل میں بیان کیا گیا تھا کہ طرفین کے نزدیک آدمی جانبین سے فضولی نہیں بن سکتا ہے۔ البتہ ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ایک آدمی جانبین سے فضولی بننے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے۔ اس جگہ بیان کیا کہ اگر عقد نکاح دو فضولیوں یا ایک فضولی اور ایک اصیل کے درمیان جاری ہواتو بالاتفاق جائز ہے۔ مسئلہ سابق میں ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر یہ شخص دونوں جانب سے وکیل ہوتا تو نکاح نافذ ہو جاتا۔ پس اگر فضولی ہے تو نکاح موقوف رہے گا۔ لہذا ایک ہی شخص دونوں جانب سے فضولی ہو سکتا ہے اور یہ خلع طلاق کے مانند ہو گیا۔ مثلاً شوہر نے کہا کہ میں نے اپنی بیوی سے ہزار روپیہ پر ضلع کیا۔ اور بیوی موجود نہیں پھر اسکو خبر ملی بیوی نے قبول کر لیا تو یہ بالا تفاق جائز ہے۔ جس طرح یہاں صیغہ واحدہ سے عقد خلع درست ہو گیا اسی طرح فضولی واحد کے کلام سے بھی عقد نکاح درست ہونا چاہئے ۔ اسی طرح اگر شوہر نے کہا کہ میں نے اتنی مقدار پر طلاق دی یا مولیٰ نے کہا کہ میں نے اتنی مقدار پر آزاد کیا۔ پھر بیوی اور غلام کوخبر پہنچی اور جس مجلس میں خبر ملی اس میں قبول کر لیا تو بالا تفاق جائز ہے۔ پس اسی طرح عقد نکاح میں ہونا چاہئے کہ اجازت پر موقوف رہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ
فضولی من الجانبين کوضلع ، طلاق اور اعتاق پر قیاس کیا ہے اور جامع ان میں سے ہر ایک کا ایجاب وقبول کا محتاج ہونا ہے۔ طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عقد نکاح تام ہوتا ہے ایجاب اور قبول سے۔ اور متن کے مسئلہ میں اس شخص کا قول کہ گواہ رہو میں نے فلاں عورت سے نکاح کیا ہے۔ یہ قول عقد کا ایک جز ہے۔ یعنی ایجاب اور وجہ یہ ہے کہ اگر زوجین مجلس میں موجود ہوتے تب بھی یہ کلام عقد نکاح کا ایک ہی جز ہوتا۔ یعنی ایجاب۔ لہذا عدم موجودگی میں بھی یہ کلام جزو عقد ہوگا۔ یعنی ایجاب اور جز وعقد ماوراء مجلس پر موقوف نہیں ہوتا۔ جیسا کہ عقد بیع میں اگر کسی نے کہا کہ میں نے فلاں کے ہاتھ اپنا غلام بیچا اور مشتری کی جانب سے کسی نے قبول نہیں کیا تو یہ عقد بیع باطل ہوگا کیونکہ مجلس میں صرف عقد بیع کا ایک جز یعنی ایجاب پایا گیا۔ اور جز عقد ماوراء مجلس پر موقوف نہیں ہوتا۔ اسی طرح عقد نکاح میں بھی جز عقد ماوراء مجلس پر موقوف نہیں ہو گا۔ بخلاف مامور من الجانبین کے۔ اس لئے کہ وکیل جو جانبین سے مامور ہے اس کا کلام منتقل ہو جاتا ہے۔ عاقدین کی طرف تو گویا ایک کی جانب سے ایجاب ہوا۔ اور دوسرے کی جانب سے قبول ہوا۔ پس وکیل کا کلام ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ دو کا کلام اور جب دونوں عاقدین کا کلام یعنی ایجاب و قبول پایا گیا تو عقد تام ہوگا۔ اس کے برخلاف عقد بیع کہ اس میں ایک آدمی جانبین کا وکیل نہیں ہو سکتا ہے۔ اس کی تفصیل ماقبل میں گذر چکی اور وہ عقد جو فضولیین کے درمیان پایا گیا عقد نام ہے اس لئے کہ ایجاب قبول دونوں پائے گئے۔ ایسے ہی ضلع ، طلاق علی مال اور اعتاق علی مال بھی عقد نام ہیں۔ حاصل یہ کہ جب زوج نے کہا میں نے اپنی فلاں بیوی سے خلع کیا ایک ہزار پر اور بیوی موجود نہیں تو یہ ضلع صحیح ہوگا۔ لیکن اس لئے نہیں کہ یہ شوہر اپنی جانب سے اصیل اور عورت کی جانب سے فضولی ہے۔ بلکہ اس لئے کہ ضلع شوہر کی جانب سے یمین ہے چنانچہ اب اگر بیوی کے قبول کرنے سے پہلے رجوع کرنا چاہے تو رجوع نہیں کر سکتا ۔ اور یمین حالف کے ساتھ مکمل ہو جاتی ہے۔ لہذا شوہر کو عورت کی جانب سے فضولی بنانے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ خلع ، طلاق اور اعتاق میں ایجاب و قبول کا عقد نہیں بلکہ شرط ہے جو کہ وہ شوہر اور مولیٰ کے قول پر پوری ہو جاتی ہے۔ لہذا عقد نکاح کو ان تینوں پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔ اور یہ درست نہیں۔ ہاں البتہ خلع عورت کی جانب سے معاوضہ ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر عورت نے کہا کہ میں نے ضلع کیا اپنا فلاں مرد سے ایک ہزار کے بدلہ میں اور شوہر غائب ہے پھر اسکو خبر پہنچی اس نے جائز قرار دیا تو صحیح نہیں ہوگا اسلئے کہ ضلع عورت کی جانب سے معاوضہ ہے۔ لہذا ماوراء مجلس پر موقوف نہیں رہے گا۔ یہی تقریر طلاق علی مال اور اعتاق علی مال میں کر لی جائے ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
Book of Marriage. A man can be [authorized] from one side as a guardian and from the other side as an asl (principal), or from one side as a guardian and from the other side as a wakeel (agent), or from both sides as a wakeel. But for one person to be asl from both sides is impossible. The marriage contract between two fuduli (unauthorized agents) or between a fuduli and an asl is valid by consensus (ijma). [Arabic text:] And if the contract takes place between two fuduli or between a fuduli and an asl, it is valid by consensus. He (Abu Yusuf) says: If he was authorized from both sides, it would be binding, but if he is fuduli, it is suspended, and it becomes like khul', talaq, and itq 'ala maal. And for them (the two: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) the existing [statement] is a part of the contract, because it is a part in the state of presence, so likewise in absence. And a part of the contract does not depend on what is beyond the council, as in sale. Contrary to the one authorized from both sides, because his speech transfers to the two contractors. And what takes place between two fuduli is a complete contract, and likewise khul' and its two analogues, because it is an action of oath from his side, so it becomes binding and is completed by the oath. [Urdu translation and expansion:] Translation: If the contract takes place between two fuduli or between a fuduli and an asl, it is valid by consensus. Abu Yusuf says that if this person was authorized from both sides (wakeel), it would be binding. So if he is fuduli, it will be suspended, and it becomes like khul', talaq, and itq 'ala maal. The argument of the two sides is that the existing [statement] is a part of the contract, because it is a part in the state of presence, so likewise in absence. And a part of the contract does not depend on what is beyond the council, as in sale. Contrary to the one authorized from both sides, because his speech transfers to the two contractors. And what takes place between two fuduli is a complete contract, and likewise khul' and its two analogues, because it is an action of oath from his side, so it becomes binding and is completed by the oath. Explanation: Previously it was stated that according to the two sides, a man cannot be fuduli from both sides. However, according to Abu Yusuf, one man has the capacity to be fuduli from both sides. Here it is stated that if the marriage contract takes place between two fuduli or between a fuduli and an asl, it is valid by consensus. In the previous issue, Abu Yusuf's proof is that if this person was a wakeel from both sides, the marriage would be binding. So if he is fuduli, the marriage will be suspended. Therefore, one person can be fuduli from both sides, and this becomes like khul' and talaq. For example, the husband said, 'I made khul' with my wife for one thousand rupees,' and the wife is not present, then she heard the news and accepted. This is valid by consensus. Just as here a single phrase makes khul' valid, similarly from the speech of a single fuduli, the marriage contract should be valid. Similarly, if the husband said, 'I gave talaq for such amount,' or the master said, 'I freed [the slave] for such amount,' then the wife or slave heard the news and accepted in the same council, it is valid by consensus. So likewise in the marriage contract, it should depend on permission. The conclusion is that he analogized the fuduli from both sides to khul', talaq, and itq, and the commonality is that each requires offer and acceptance. The argument of the two sides is that the marriage contract is completed by offer and acceptance. In the issue of the text, this person's statement, 'Bear witness, I have married so-and-so woman,' is a part of the contract, i.e., the offer. The reason is that if the spouses were present in the council, this speech would be one part of the marriage contract, i.e., the offer. So in absence, this speech is also a part of the contract, i.e., the offer. And a part of the contract does not depend on what is beyond the council, as in the sale contract. If someone says, 'I sold my slave to so-and-so,' and no one from the buyer's side accepts, this sale contract is void because only one part of the sale contract (the offer) existed in the council. And a part of the contract does not depend on what is beyond the council. Similarly, in the marriage contract, a part of the contract does not depend on what is beyond the council. Contrary to the one authorized from both sides, because the wakeel who is authorized from both sides, his speech transfers to the two contractors, so it is as if the offer came from one side and acceptance from the other. So his speech becomes like the speech of two, and when the speech of both contractors (offer and acceptance) is found, the contract is complete. In contrast, in a sale contract, one person cannot be a wakeel from both sides; this detail has passed. The contract that takes place between two fuduli is a complete contract because both offer and acceptance are found. Likewise, khul', talaq 'ala maal, and itq 'ala maal are also complete contracts. The conclusion is that when the husband said, 'I made khul' with my wife for one thousand,' and the wife is not present, this khul' is valid. But not because the husband is asl from his side and fuduli from the woman's side; rather, because khul' is an oath from the husband's side, so if he wishes to revoke before the wife's acceptance, he cannot. And the oath is completed with the oath-taker. Therefore, there is no need for the husband to be fuduli from the woman's side. In summary, in khul', talaq, and itq, offer and acceptance are not a contract but a condition that is fulfilled by the husband's/master's statement. So analogizing the marriage contract to these three is qiyas ma'a al-fariq (analogy with a difference) and is not correct. However, khul' is a compensation from the woman's side. So if the woman said, 'I made khul' with so-and-so man for one thousand,' and the husband is absent, then he heard and permitted it, it is not valid because khul' is compensation from the woman's side, so it will not depend on what is beyond the council. The same reasoning applies to talaq 'ala maal and itq 'ala maal. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a marriage contract performed by two fuduli (unauthorized agents) or a fuduli and an asl (principal). The ruling itself is that such a contract is valid by consensus (ijma), but the reasoning differs between Abu Yusuf and the majority (the two: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The majority argue that the statement of the fuduli, e.g., 'I have married so-and-so woman,' constitutes a part of the contract (shart al-aqd), specifically the offer (ijab). Since a part of the contract does not require acceptance in the same council (majlis) to be valid—as evidenced by the analogy with sale where an offer without acceptance is void—the contract remains suspended (mawquf) upon the acceptance of the principal. Abu Yusuf analogizes the situation to khul', talaq, and itq 'ala maal, where a single statement from one side suffices because these are considered oaths (yamin) that become binding immediately. The text clarifies the distinction: in khul', talaq, and itq, the contract is not based on offer and acceptance in the usual sense; rather, the statement of the husband/master is an oath that completes the transaction. Therefore, analogizing the marriage contract to these is flawed (qiyas ma'a al-fariq). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the majority: the contract is valid but suspended until the principal approves, and one person cannot be fuduli from both sides unless he is a wakeel.

Key Terms
فضولی (fudūlī): A person who acts without authorization; an unauthorized agent who enters a contract without prior permission from the principal.
اصیل (aṣīl): The principal or the person on whose behalf the contract is made; the one who is directly a party to the contract.
شطر العقد (shaṭr al-ʿaqd): A part of the contract; specifically the offer (ijab) or acceptance (qabul) considered as a component of the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), what is the status of a marriage contract made by two fuduli (unauthorized agents)?
A) It is void (batil) from the outset.
B) It is valid and binding immediately.
C) It is valid but suspended (mawquf) on the approval of the principals.
D) It is only valid if the fuduli are also the guardians (awliya').

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a marriage by unauthorized agents is valid but suspended, and the majority holds that one person cannot act as fuduli from both sides.

Nikah — Marriage
beginner
6 min
Agent Exceeds Instructions: Two Marriages in One Contract
Ruling on an agent exceeding instructions by marrying two women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when an agent marries a man to two women in a single contract despite being instructed to marry one, and explain the legal reasoning behind the annulment.

Core Idea
An agent who exceeds instructions by marrying two women in one contract invalidates both marriages.

In this lesson, we examine a specific case from Hanafi nikah law: a principal instructs his agent to marry him to one woman, but the agent marries him to two in a single contract. The text establishes that neither marriage is binding. We will work through the three possible enforcement scenarios and understand why each fails, leading to the only viable outcome – annulment. This ruling underscores the strict limits of an agent's authority in marriage contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the violation
First, note the facts: the principal (commanding man) appoints an agent to marry him to one woman. The agent exceeds this limit by marrying him to two women in a single marriage contract (nikah). This is a clear violation of the agent's authority.
The principal's instruction is specific: 'marry me to a woman' (singular).
2
List the three theoretically possible outcomes
The author considers three options: (a) enforce both marriages, (b) enforce one unspecified marriage, or (c) specify and enforce one of the two. Each must be examined for legal validity.
These are the only logical possibilities given that the contract is executed.
3
Examine why enforcement of both marriages is impossible
The agent was instructed to marry one woman, so enforcing both directly contradicts (mukhalafah) the principal's order. Since the agent acts under authority, any act beyond the scope is non-binding.
This is based on the principle that an agent must stay within his mandate.
4
Examine why enforcement of one unspecified marriage is impossible
If we try to enforce only one marriage without specifying which one, there is ignorance (jahalah) about which woman the principal intended. Uncertainty in a marriage contract invalidates it, as the identity of the wife must be known.
Jahalah (uncertainty) is a defect that makes a contract invalid in Hanafi law.
5
Examine why specifying one of the two is impossible
There is no basis to prefer one woman over the other (la uluwiyyah). Both are equally valid candidates, and the agent had no authority to choose randomly. Thus, arbitrary selection would be unjust.
Since the principal did not specify which woman, and the agent exceeded authority, no preference can be made.
6
Conclude that annulment is the only option
Since all three possibilities are legally impossible, the only remaining outcome is tafriq (separation/annulment). Thus, neither marriage is binding (la yalzam).
Tafriq here means the marriages are void ab initio; no further action needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و من امر رجلا ان يزوجه امراة فزوجه انثنتين فى عقدة لم تلزمه واحدة منهما لانه لا وجه الى تنفيذ هما للمخالفة ولا الى التنفيذ فى احدهما غير عين للجهالة ولا الى التعيين لعدم الاولوية فتعين التفريق
ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے کسی مرد کو حکم دیا کہ نکاح کر دے اس کا کسی عورت سے۔ پس نکاح کیا اس کا دوعورتوں سے ایک عقد میں تو نہیں لازم ہو گا اس کو ان دونوں میں سے کسی کا نکاح۔ اس لئے کہ کوئی وجہ نہیں ان دونوں کے نکاح کو نافذ کرنے کی مخالفت کی وجہ سے اور نہ کوئی وجہ ہے ان دونوں میں سے ایک غیر معین میں نافذ کرنے کی جہالت کی وجہ سے اور نہ کوئی وجہ ہے متعین کرنے کی عدم اولویت کی وجہ سے پس تفریق متعین ہوگی۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک آدمی نے کسی کو وکیل بنایا کہ میرا ایک عورت سے نکاح کر دے وکیل نے عقد واحد میں دو عورتوں سے نکاح کر دیا ان دونوں میں سے کسی کا نکاح لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ تین صورتیں ہیں ایک یہ کہ دونوں میں عقد کو نافذ کر دیا جائے ۔ دوم یہ کہ ایک غیر معین میں نافذ کر دیا جائے۔ سوم یہ کہ ایک کو متعین کر کے نافذ کر دیا جائے۔ لیکن یہ تینوں صورتیں ممکن نہیں ۔ اول تو اس لئے کہ
And whoever ordered a man to marry him to one woman, and he married him to two women in one contract, neither of them is binding upon him. Because there is no way to implement both due to contradiction, nor to implement one unspecified due to ignorance (jahalah), nor to specify one due to lack of preference. So separation (tatreeq) is determined. Translation: And a person who ordered a man to marry him to one woman, and he married him to two women in one contract, then neither of these two marriages is binding upon him. Because there is no way to implement both due to contradiction, nor to implement one unspecified due to ignorance, nor to specify one due to lack of preference. So separation (tatreeq - annulment) is determined. Explanation: The issue is that a man appointed someone as wakeel (agent) to marry him to one woman. The agent married him to two women in a single contract. Neither marriage is binding. Because there are three possibilities: 1) Enforce both contracts, 2) Enforce one unspecified, 3) Specify one to enforce. But none of these is possible. The first is not possible because it contradicts the instruction to marry only one. The second is not possible because of ignorance (which woman?). The third is not possible because there is no preference. So the only option is to annul the marriage.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: if a man appoints an agent to marry him to one specific woman, and the agent marries him to two women in a single contract, neither marriage is binding (lazim). The agent has violated the instruction. The ruling is based on three possible outcomes being impossible: enforcing both contracts contradicts the instruction; enforcing one unspecified leads to uncertainty (jahalah); and arbitrarily specifying one is unjustified. Therefore, the only valid outcome is to annul the contract entirely. This is a straightforward ruling without proof, serving as a memorization anchor.

Key Terms
وکیل (wakīl): An agent appointed to perform a specific task, here to marry a man to one woman.
تفریق (tafrīq): Annulment or separation; here it means the marriage is nullified and not binding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man appoints an agent to marry him to one specific woman. The agent marries him to two women in a single contract. What is the ruling on these marriages?
A) Both marriages are valid and binding.
B) Only the first woman named in the contract is married.
C) The principal may choose one and it becomes binding.
D) Neither marriage is binding.

Key Takeaway
When an agent exceeds instructions by marrying a man to two women in one contract, both marriages are annulled due to the agent's violation and uncertainty.

Khula, Talaq on Payment, and Itaq on Payment: Oaths, Not Contracts
Distinguishing khula, talaq on payment, and itaq on payment from marriage contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that khula from the husband's side is an oath (yamin) and distinguish it from a bilateral contract requiring acceptance in the same council.

Core Idea
Khula from the husband is an oath, valid without acceptance; from the wife it is a compensation requiring acceptance.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies a key distinction: while a marriage contract requires offer and acceptance in the same council, acts like khula, talaq on payment, and manumission on payment when performed by the husband or master are oaths that are complete upon utterance. Understanding this prevents the error of analogizing them to marriage contracts and ensures correct fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key distinction
Recognize that a marriage contract requires both offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul) in the same council for validity. However, the author argues that khula, talaq on payment, and itaq on payment from the husband/master are different.
2
Analyze the proof: contract vs. oath
The author uses an analogy with a sales contract to show that a contract cannot be suspended beyond the council. Then he argues that khula from the husband's side is not a contract but an oath (yamin), which is complete upon utterance without need for acceptance.
3
Contrast the woman's side
When the woman initiates khula in the husband's absence, it is invalid because from her side it is a compensation contract (mu'awada) and cannot be suspended beyond the council.
4
Summarize the ruling
Thus, khula, talaq on payment, and itaq on payment from the husband/master are oaths, valid without acceptance. The marriage contract is fundamentally different and cannot be analogized to them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نہیں ہوتا۔ جیسا کہ عقد بیع میں اگر کسی نے کہا کہ میں نے فلاں کے ہاتھ اپنا غلام بیچا اور مشتری کی جانب سے کسی نے قبول نہیں کیا تو یہ عقد بیع باطل ہوگا کیونکہ مجلس میں صرف عقد بیع کا ایک جز یعنی ایجاب پایا گیا۔ اور جز عقد ماوراء مجلس پر موقوف نہیں ہوتا۔ اسی طرح عقد نکاح میں بھی جز عقد ماوراء مجلس پر موقوف نہیں ہو گا۔ بخلاف مامور من الجانبین کے۔ اس لئے کہ وکیل جو جانبین سے مامور ہے اس کا کلام منتقل ہو جاتا ہے۔ عاقدین کی طرف تو گویا ایک کی جانب سے ایجاب ہوا۔ اور دوسرے کی جانب سے قبول ہوا۔ پس وکیل کا کلام ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ دو کا کلام اور جب دونوں عاقدین کا کلام یعنی ایجاب و قبول پایا گیا تو عقد تام ہوگا۔ اس کے برخلاف عقد بیع کہ اس میں ایک آدمی جانبین کا وکیل نہیں ہو سکتا ہے۔ اس کی تفصیل ماقبل میں گذر چکی اور وہ عقد جو فضولیین کے درمیان پایا گیا عقد نام ہے اس لئے کہ ایجاب قبول دونوں پائے گئے۔ ایسے ہی ضلع ، طلاق علی مال اور اعتاق علی مال بھی عقد نام ہیں۔ حاصل یہ کہ جب زوج نے کہا میں نے اپنی فلاں بیوی سے خلع کیا ایک ہزار پر اور بیوی موجود نہیں تو یہ ضلع صحیح ہوگا۔ لیکن اس لئے نہیں کہ یہ شوہر اپنی جانب سے اصیل اور عورت کی جانب سے فضولی ہے۔ بلکہ اس لئے کہ ضلع شوہر کی جانب سے یمین ہے چنانچہ اب اگر بیوی کے قبول کرنے سے پہلے رجوع کرنا چاہے تو رجوع نہیں کر سکتا ۔ اور یمین حالف کے ساتھ مکمل ہو جاتی ہے۔ لہذا شوہر کو عورت کی جانب سے فضولی بنانے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ خلع ، طلاق اور اعتاق میں ایجاب و قبول کا عقد نہیں بلکہ شرط ہے جو کہ وہ شوہر اور مولیٰ کے قول پر پوری ہو جاتی ہے۔ لہذا عقد نکاح کو ان تینوں پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔ اور یہ درست نہیں۔ ہاں البتہ خلع عورت کی جانب سے معاوضہ ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر عورت نے کہا کہ میں نے ضلع کیا اپنا فلاں مرد سے ایک ہزار کے بدلہ میں اور شوہر غائب ہے پھر اسکو خبر پہنچی اس نے جائز قرار دیا تو صحیح نہیں ہوگا اسلئے کہ ضلع عورت کی جانب سے معاوضہ ہے۔ لہذا ماوراء مجلس پر موقوف نہیں رہے گا۔ یہی تقریر طلاق علی مال اور اعتاق علی مال میں کر لی جائے ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
It does not happen. As in a sales contract, if someone said, 'I sold my slave to so-and-so,' and no one from the buyer's side accepted, then this sales contract is void because only one part of the sale contract, namely the offer, occurred in the council. And a part of the contract cannot be suspended beyond the council. Similarly, in a marriage contract, a part of the contract cannot be suspended beyond the council. Unlike when one is commanded from both sides. Because the agent who is commanded from both sides, his speech is transferred to the two contracting parties, so it is as if there was an offer from one side and acceptance from the other. Thus, the agent's speech becomes like the speech of two, and when the speech of both contracting parties, i.e., offer and acceptance, are found, the contract is complete. In contrast, in a sales contract, one person cannot be an agent from both sides. This detail has passed before. And the contract that occurs between unauthorized agents is called a nominal contract because both offer and acceptance are found. Similarly, khula, talaq on payment, and manumission on payment are also nominal contracts. The result is that when the husband said, 'I have divorced my wife so-and-so for one thousand,' and the wife is not present, then this khula is valid. But not because the husband is principal on his own side and an unauthorized agent on the woman's side, but because khula from the husband's side is an oath. Therefore, if he wishes to revoke before the wife's acceptance, he cannot revoke. And an oath is completed with the one who swears. Hence, there is no need to make the husband an unauthorized agent on the woman's side. In summary, in khula, talaq, and manumission, there is no contract of offer and acceptance, but rather a condition that is fulfilled by the statement of the husband or master. Therefore, analogizing the marriage contract to these three is an analogy with a difference, and that is not correct. However, khula from the woman's side is a compensation. So, if the woman said, 'I have divorced my husband so-and-so for one thousand,' and the husband is absent, then later the news reached him and he approved it, it will not be valid because khula from the woman's side is a compensation, so it cannot be suspended beyond the council. This same reasoning should be applied to talaq on payment and manumission on payment. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary on Al-Hidayah. It distinguishes the nature of khula (divorce initiated by the wife with compensation), talaq 'ala mal (divorce in exchange for payment), and 'itaq 'ala mal (manumission in exchange for payment) from the marriage contract. The author explains that in a marriage contract, the offer and acceptance must be in the same council (majlis) for the contract to be valid; one part cannot be suspended beyond the council. However, in the acts of khula, talaq, and 'itaq, when performed by the husband or master, they are considered oaths (yamin) that are completed with the speaker's utterance, not bilateral contracts requiring acceptance in the same council. Therefore, if the husband says 'I have divorced my wife for one thousand' in her absence, it is valid and he cannot revoke it before her acceptance. On the other hand, if the woman initiates khula in the husband's absence, it is invalid because from her side it is a compensation contract that cannot be suspended beyond the council. The analogy between marriage and these acts is rejected as 'qiyas ma'a al-fariq' (analogy with a difference).

Key Terms
خلع (khul‘): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation, treated as an oath from the husband's side.
طلاق علی مال (talāq ʿalā māl): Divorce in exchange for payment, similar in ruling to khula from husband's side.
یمین (yamīn): Oath; in this context, a unilateral declaration that is valid upon utterance without acceptance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is khula from the husband's side valid without the wife's acceptance?
A) Because the husband can act as the wife's agent.
B) Because khula is an oath and oaths are complete upon utterance.
C) Because the wife's acceptance is automatic.
D) Because the husband pays compensation.

Key Takeaway
Khula from the husband is an oath, not a contract; from the wife it is a compensation contract requiring acceptance.

The Agent's Marriage to a Slave Woman: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on agency marriage validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding an agent's marriage to a slave woman, and explain their reasoning based on absolute wording, custom, and istihsan.

Core Idea
Absolute wording holds unless custom restricts, but practical custom cannot override verbal custom.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on the scope of agency in marriage. When a commander instructs his agent to marry him to a woman, and the agent marries him to a slave woman, does the marriage hold? The answer hinges on how absolute language interacts with customary practice. Abu Hanifa upholds the marriage; the Sahibayn require compatibility (kafa'ah). Understanding their arguments sharpens your ability to handle conflicts between textual absolutes and social custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Case and the Dispute
The commander says 'marry me to a woman'. The agent marries him to someone else's slave woman. Is the marriage valid? Abu Hanifa says yes; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say no, unless the woman is compatible (kufu').
The agency is absolute; no specification of free or slave.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position and Proof
Abu Hanifa argues that the word 'woman' (imra'ah) is absolute and includes both free and slave women. Also, there is no suspicion (tuhma) of the agent's partiality because the slave woman is not his own.
He relies on the literal meaning of the term.
3
State the Sahibayn's Position and Proof
The Sahibayn say the absolute term should be understood according to custom (urf). The customary marriage for a commander is to a free woman of equal status (kufu'). Hence the agent's act exceeds authority unless the slave woman is compatible.
They prioritize customary understanding over pure literalism.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response to the Sahibayn
The commentary provides a dual response: (1) The custom may be shared – nobles sometimes marry slave women, so no single custom restricts. (2) Even if the custom favors free women, it is a practical custom (urf 'amali) which cannot restrict a verbal custom (urf lafzi) because they are different domains. Additionally, the Sahibayn's view is based on istihsan, not a text, so it is a secondary consideration.
The distinction between verbal and practical custom is key to the rebuttal.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf and Tarjih
Under Abu Hanifa, the marriage is valid and binding; under the Sahibayn, it is invalid unless the woman is compatible. The commentary leans toward Abu Hanifa's view, which is from the zahir al-riwayah.
The practical consequence is whether the marriage stands or must be annulled.

Source Text

بالکفو میں مددطلب کرنا ( مراد ) ہوگا ۔ واللہ اعلم۔ تشریح حاکم نے کسی کو وکیل بنایا کہ کسی عورت کے ساتھ میرا نکاح کر دے اس نے اپنے غیر کی باندی سے نکاح کر دیا۔ امام صاحب کے نزدیک یہ نکاح جائز ہے اس کو فرماتے ہیں کہ جائز نہیں الا یہ کہ کفو میں نکاح کرے دلیل یہ کہ تو کیل مطلق ہے اور مطلق لوٹتا ہے متعارف کی طرف ۔ اور متعارف کفو میں نکاح کرنا ہے کنبہ غیر کفو میں ۔ ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ عرف مشترک سے نکاح کرتے ہیں اور اطلاق لفظ عرف لفظی ہے۔ پس عرف لفظی کے لئے عرف عملی مقید اور مخصص نہیں ہوسکتا۔ کیونکہ تقیید اطلاق کا مقابل ہے اور تقابل کیلئے اتحاد محل شرط ہے۔ اور اتحاد حل پایا نہیں گیا اس لئے کہ عرف لفظی اور عرف عملی میں کوئی اتحاد نہیں ہے۔ امام محمد نے مبسوط کی کتاب الوکالت میں ذکر کیا کہ صاحبین کے نزدیک اس صورت میں کفائت کا اعتبار استحسانا ہے اور وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ مطلق عورت کے ساتھ نکاح پر ہر شخص قادر ہے حاکم بھی غیر حاکم بھی ۔ لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ حاکم نے کفو میں نکاح پر مددطلب کی ہے۔
And whoever a commander ordered him to marry him to a woman, then he married him to someone else's slave woman, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa, turning to the absolute wording and the absence of suspicion. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: It is not permissible unless he marries him to one who is compatible (kufu'), because the absolute term turns to the customary, and that is marriage to equals. We reply: The custom is either shared or it is a practical custom, so it is not fit to restrict. And it is mentioned in the chapter of agency that considering compatibility in this is istihsan according to them, because everyone is capable of marrying an absolute woman, so the assistance is sought in marriage to a compatible partner. And Allah knows best. Translation: The person whom a commander ordered saying: 'Marry me to a woman,' then he married him to someone else's slave woman. According to Abu Hanifa, it is permissible, turning to the absolute wording and the absence of suspicion. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad said: It is not permissible, unless he marries him to a compatible woman. Because the absolute term returns to the customary, and that is marriage to equals. We will answer that the custom is shared, or it is a practical custom. So it is not capable of being a restrictor. And in the book of agency, it is mentioned that consideration of compatibility in this is istihsan according to the two, because no person is incapable of marrying an absolute woman, so the intended meaning is seeking help in marriage to a compatible partner. And Allah knows best. Explanation: The ruler appointed someone as agent to marry him to a woman. He married him to someone else's slave woman. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, this marriage is valid and will not be rejected. The proof is that in agency for marriage, the word 'woman' is absolute, including both free and slave women. And there is no suspicion because the slave woman is not the agent's own, so the agent is not suspected. The two (Sahibayn) said: It is not permissible unless he marries him to a compatible woman. The proof is that the agency is absolute, and absolute turns to the customary. And the customary is marriage to equals, not to non-equals. Our response is that the custom is shared, meaning that nobles marry both free women and slave women. And even if it is accepted that marrying free women is the custom, this is a practical custom. And absolute wording is a verbal custom. So a practical custom cannot restrict or specify a verbal custom, because restriction is opposite to absoluteness, and for opposition, unity of context is necessary, and that unity is not found here because there is no unity between verbal custom and practical custom. Imam Muhammad mentioned in al-Mabsut, in the book of agency, that according to the two, consideration of compatibility in this case is istihsan, and the reason for istihsan is that every person, whether a ruler or not, is capable of marrying an absolute woman, so it becomes known that the ruler sought assistance in marriage to a compatible partner.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The case: a ruler (amir) appoints an agent to marry him to a woman. The agent marries him to someone else's slave woman. Imam Abu Hanifa holds the marriage valid because the term 'woman' (imra'ah) in the agency is absolute, covering both free women and slave women. Additionally, there is no suspicion of partiality since the slave woman is not the agent's own. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (Sahibayn) hold that it is not valid unless the woman is compatible (kufu') in social status, because the absolute term is understood according to custom (urf), and the custom is to marry free women of equal status. The commentary provides a Hanafi response: the custom is shared (nobles sometimes marry slave women), and even if it is a custom, it is a practical custom (urf 'amali), which cannot restrict a verbal absolute (urf lafzi) because they belong to different domains. Furthermore, in the book of agency, Imam Muhammad notes that Sahibayn's view is based on istihsan, reasoning that since anyone can marry an absolute woman, the ruler's instruction is interpreted as seeking a compatible marriage. The mufta bihi is the position of Abu Hanifa, but the commentary presents both views.

Key Terms
کفو (kufu'): Compatibility in social status, lineage, and other factors considered in marriage.
عرف لفظی (‘urf lafẓī): Verbal custom: the conventional meaning of a word in a particular community.
عرف عملی (‘urf ‘amalī): Practical custom: the common practice of people, as opposed to linguistic usage.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; a source of law that allows departing from analogy for a stronger reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Abu Hanifa consider the marriage to a slave woman valid when the commander ordered marriage to a free woman?
A) Because the agent's act is always valid regardless of the principal's command.
B) Because the word 'woman' in the agency is absolute and includes both free and slave women.
C) Because the commander is a ruler and can marry anyone.
D) Because the agent had no choice.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the agent's marriage to a slave woman is valid under Abu Hanifa because the absolute term 'woman' includes her, and practical custom cannot override verbal absolutes.

Mahr: Not a Condition of Marriage, Minimum Ten Dirhams
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that marriage is valid without specifying or even stipulating no mahr, and that the minimum mahr is ten dirhams, citing the hadith and qiyas as proofs.

Core Idea
Mahr is wajib but not a condition; its minimum is ten dirhams, proven by hadith and analogy.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes two foundational rulings on mahr (dower). First, marriage is valid even if mahr is not mentioned or if the condition of no mahr is stipulated. Second, the minimum mahr is ten dirhams. These rulings are defended against objections from Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i using linguistic reasoning, a prophetic hadith, and qiyas (analogy) with the nisab of theft. Understanding these points clarifies the Hanafi view of mahr as a wajib (obligation) that does not affect contract validity.

Guided Path
1
Extract the two rulings
Read the passage carefully and identify the two main rulings: (1) marriage is valid without mentioning mahr or even with a stipulation of no mahr; (2) the minimum mahr is ten dirhams. Note that these are separate issues.
The first ruling is about the validity of the contract; the second is about the quantum of mahr.
2
Understand the linguistic basis for the first ruling
The author (Al-Marghinani) argues that marriage linguistically is a contract of joining (inghimam) and pairing (izdiwaj), perfected by the spouses alone. Mahr is a Sharia obligation added to honour the marital bond, but its mention is not a condition of validity. Trace this reasoning in the text.
This is a Hanafi principle: mahr is not a rukn or shart.
3
Identify the proofs for the second ruling
Two proofs are cited for the minimum of ten dirhams: (a) a hadith: 'There is no mahr less than ten dirhams,' and (b) qiyas with the nisab of theft (also ten dirhams). The underlying logic: mahr is a Sharia right that requires a significant amount; ten dirhams is the recognized threshold of significance.
The hadith is the primary proof; the qiyas reinforces it.
4
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute
The passage mentions Malik's disagreement on the first ruling (he may consider mahr a condition) and Shafi'i's disagreement on the second (he allows any price in sale as mahr, no minimum). Understand each position and the Hanafi response.
The practical consequence (thamarah) is whether a marriage contract with less than ten dirhams mahr is valid, and what the wife receives.

بابُ المهر
ترجمہ یہ باب مہر کے بیان میں ہے
مہر مقرر کئے بغیر بھی نکاح درست ہے، اسی طرح یہ شرط لگائی کہ مہر نہیں ہوگا تو بھی نکاح درست ہے

قال ويصح النكاح و ان لم يسم فيه مهر الان النكاح عقد انضمام و ازدواج لغة فيتم بالزوجين ثم المهر واجب شرعا ابانة لشرف المحل فلا يحتاج الى ذكره لصحة النكاح وكذا اذا تزوجها بشرط ان لامهر لها لما بينا وفيه خلاف مالك واقل المهر عشرة دراهم وقال الشافعى ما يجوزان يكون ثمنا في البيع يجوز ان يكون مهرالها لانه حقها فيكون التقدير اليها ولنا قوله عليه السلام ولا مهراقل من عشرة ولانه حق الشرع وجوبا اظهار الشرف المحل فيقدر بماله خطر و هو العشرة استدلالا بنصاب السرقة
ترجمہ اور صحیح ہے نکاح اگر چہ اس میں مہر ذکر نہیں کیا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ نکاح لغت میں عقد انضمام اور ازدواج ہے۔ پس زوجین کے ساتھ پورا ہو جائے گا۔ پھر مہر شرعاً واجب ہے شرافت محل کو ظاہر کرنے کے لئے ۔ پس مہر کے ذکر کی احتیاج نہیں صحت نکاح کے لئے اور ایسا ہی جب نکاح کیا عورت سے اس شرط کے ساتھ کہ اس کے لئے مہر نہیں۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی ۔ اور اس میں امام مالک کا اختلاف ہے۔ اور مہر کی کم از کم مقدار دس درھم ہے۔ امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ وہ چیز جس کو بیع میں شمن بنانا جائز ہے اس کو عورت کے لئے مہر بنانا جائز ہے۔ اس لئے کہ مہر عورت کا حق ہے پس اس کو مقدر کرنا بھی عورت ہی کا حق ہوگا ۔ ہماری دلیل حضور صلے اللہ علیہ وسلم کا فرمان ہے کہ دس درہم سے کم مہر نہیں ہے اور اس لئے کہ مہر شریعت کا حق ہے شرافت محل کو ظاہر کرنے کے لئے پس اندازہ لگایا جائے گا اس مقدار کے ساتھ جسکی کوئی عظمت ہو اور وہ دس ہے قیاس کرتے ہوئے نصاب سرقہ پر۔

قرآن میں دونوں نام مذکور ہیں و آتوا النساء صدقاتهن نحلة

Chapter of Mahr. Translation: This chapter is concerning mahr. Marriage is valid without specifying mahr; similarly, if the condition is set that there will be no mahr, then too the marriage is valid. Kitab al-Nikah: He said: The marriage is valid even if mahr is not mentioned in it, because marriage linguistically is a contract of joining and pairing; it is perfected by the spouses. Then mahr is obligatory by Sharia to show the honor of the place, so it is not needed for the validity of the marriage. Likewise, if he marries her with the condition that she has no mahr, due to what we have explained. And in this there is disagreement of Malik. The minimum mahr is ten dirhams. And al-Shafi'i said: Whatever is permissible to be a price in sale is permissible to be mahr for her, because it is her right, so the estimation is hers. And our proof is his saying (peace be upon him): 'There is no mahr less than ten.' And because it is a right of Sharia, its obligation is to show the honor of the place, so it is estimated by something that has significance, and that is ten, by analogy with the nisab of theft. Translation: And the marriage is valid even if mahr is not mentioned in it, because marriage linguistically is a contract of joining and pairing; it is perfected by the spouses. Then mahr is obligatory by Sharia to show the honor of the place, so mentioning mahr is not needed for the validity of the marriage. Similarly, when he marries her with the condition that she has no mahr, due to the proof we mentioned. And in this there is disagreement of Imam Malik. The minimum amount of mahr is ten dirhams. Imam al-Shafi'i said: Whatever thing is permissible to be a price in sale is permissible to be mahr for her, because mahr is her right, so its estimation is also her right. Our proof is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'There is no mahr less than ten dirhams.' And because mahr is a right of Sharia, to show the honor of the place, so it is estimated by an amount that has significance, and that is ten, by analogy with the nisab of theft. Elaboration: When the author of Hidayah finished describing the pillars and conditions of marriage, he wanted to describe the ruling of marriage, and the ruling of marriage is the obligation of mahr. Some say mahr is wealth, and some say mahr is sidaq, and sidaq is the name of the wealth mentioned in the marriage contract. Kaki said that mahr has seven names: (1) Sidaq, (2) Nihla, (3) [unclear: بن الله?], (4) Farida, (5) Mahr, (6) Ajr (this is also in the Quran: 'And give them their wages'), (7) [possibly another]. In the Quran both names are mentioned: 'And give the women their sadaqat as nihla.' This name is also present in the holy speech: 'And you have prescribed for them a farida.' This name is mentioned in hadith: 'For if he touches her, she gets the mahr for what he has made permissible.'
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter (Bab) on Mahr (dower). It establishes two fundamental rulings: (1) Marriage is valid without specifying the mahr at the time of contract, and even if the condition is stipulated that there is no mahr, the marriage remains valid. This is because marriage linguistically is a contract of joining (inghimam) and pairing; it is perfected by the spouses alone. The mahr is a Sharia obligation imposed to honor the marital tie, but its mention is not a condition of validity. (2) The minimum mahr is ten dirhams. This is disputed: Imam Malik disagreed with the first ruling (he held that mahr is a condition). Imam al-Shafi'i disagreed with the second: he held that any item permissible as a price in sale can be mahr, leaving its estimation to the woman's right. The Hanafi proof for the minimum is twofold: a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) stating 'There is no mahr less than ten dirhams' (or a variant meaning 'the least mahr is ten'), and a qiyas (analogy) with the nisab of theft (threshold for cutting the hand), which is also ten dirhams, indicating that ten is a legally recognized amount of significance. The commentary further lists various names for mahr found in Quran and Sunnah: sadaq, nihla, farida, ajr, etc., emphasizing its religious and legal nature.

Key Terms
مهر (mahr): The dower or bridal gift given by the husband to the wife, obligatory in marriage.
صداق (sidaq): Synonym for mahr; also used in Quran: 'And give the women their sadaqat.'
نحلة (nihlah): A gift or grant; another Quranic term for mahr: 'as a nihlah' (Quran 4:4).
فريضة (faridah): An ordained portion; used in Quran for prescribed mahr.
عشرة دراهم (ashratu darahim): Ten dirhams, the minimum mahr in Hanafi school.
نصاب السرقة (nisab al-sariqah): The minimum value of stolen property for which the hadd penalty (amputation) applies; set at ten dirhams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum mahr according to the Hanafi school?
A) Any amount agreed upon by the parties.
B) Ten dirhams.
C) Five dirhams.
D) One dirham.

Key Takeaway
Mahr is obligatory in marriage but not a condition of validity; its minimum is ten dirhams, established by hadith and analogy.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Rulings on Mahr: Validity Without Specification, Condition of No Mahr, and Minimum Amount
Establishes Hanafi rulings on mahr with proofs and inter-madhhab disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings that marriage is valid without mahr specification or with a condition of no mahr, and that the minimum mahr is ten dirhams, citing the textual proofs and the disputes with Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Mahr is wajib but not a pillar; marriage remains valid even if mahr is unspecified or denied, and its minimum is ten dirhams.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, the author establishes two key Hanafi rulings on mahr: the validity of a marriage contract even when no mahr is mentioned or even negated, and the minimum amount of mahr being ten dirhams. The text provides proofs from hadith and qiyas, and addresses the objections of Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i. Understanding these rulings clarifies that mahr is an obligation that honors the marriage, not a condition for its validity.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish between validity and obligation
The passage opens by stating that marriage is valid even without mahr. Understand that mahr is a wajib (obligation) imposed by Shariah, not a rukn (pillar) or shart (condition). The validity of nikah depends on consent and offer/acceptance, not on mahr.
This distinction is key to understanding the Hanafi position.
2
Analyse the proof for validity without mahr
The text argues that nikah linguistically means union (insidmam wa izdiwaj), completed by the spouses. The Quranic verse in al-Baqarah 236 allows divorce before fixing mahr, confirming validity. Note the Hanafi response to Malik's objection: omission of price invalidates sale, but omission of mahr does not invalidate marriage due to the difference in nature.
3
Examine the condition of no mahr
Even explicit negation of mahr does not invalidate the contract. Malik's view invalidates such a condition because he sees nikah as a contract of exchange. The Hanafi response highlights that consensus exists on validity when mahr is omitted, so explicit negation should not differ, unlike in sale where both omission and negation invalidate.
4
Determine the minimum mahr from the hadith and qiyas
The hadith 'No mahr less than ten dirhams' directly sets the minimum. The qiyas on nisab of theft (ten dirhams) reinforces that mahr must be a significant amount to honor the marriage. Compare with Shafi'i's view that any priceable item suffices, left to the woman's discretion.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of each dispute
For the condition of no mahr, Malik's view would invalidate the marriage; Hanafi keeps it valid with mahr al-mithl due. For minimum mahr, Shafi'i would allow one dirham; Hanafi requires at least ten, or else mahr al-mithl becomes wajib.
These differences affect real-life marriage contracts.

حدیث میں علایق سے مراد مہر ہے۔
حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا عفرنسا تھا کہ یہاں عقر سے مراد مہر ہے۔
ان سات ناموں میں چار قرآن میں اور تین احادیث میں مذکور ہیں۔
صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں نکاح صحیح ہوتا ہے اگر چہ آئمیں مہر مذکور نہ ہو۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ نکاح عقد انضمام اور عقد ازدواج کو کہتے ہیں۔ اور یہ معنی پورے ہو جاتے ہیں زوجین سے۔ لہذا صحت نکاح کیلئے مہر کا ذکر ضروری نہیں۔ دوسری دلیل یہ کہ قرآن میں ہے فانكحوا ما طاب لكم الآیة ۔ اب اگر ہم نے ذکر مہر کی شرط لگا دی تو نص پر زیادتی کرنالازم آئے گا جو درست نہیں۔ لیکن سوال یہ ہے کہ جب مہر شرعاً واجب ہے تو بغیر مہر کے نکاح کیسے درست ہوگا۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ وجوب مہر صحت نکاح کے لئے شرط نہیں بلکہ مہر واجب ہوا ہے شرافت محل یعنی بضع کی عظمت اور شرفت کو ظاہر کرنے کے لئے۔ لہذا صحت نکاح کے لئے مہر کے ذکر کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ اگر کوئی اشکال کرے کہ اس پر کیا دلیل ہے کہ صحت نکاح کے لئے مہر کے ذکر کی ضرورت نہیں ۔ جواب قرآن اس پر شاہد ہے، فرمایا گیا لا جناح عليكم ان طلقتم النساء مالم تمسوهن او تفرضوالهن فريضة ومتعواهن على الموسع قدره وعلى المقتر قدرہ ۔ (ترجمہ) کچھ گناہ نہیں تم پر اگر طلاق دو تم عورتوں کو اس وقت کہ ہاتھ بھی نہ لگایا ہو اور نہ مقرر کیا ہو ان کیلئے کچھ مہر اور ان کو خرچ دو مقدور والے پر اس کے موافق ہے اور تنگی والے پر اس کے موافق ۔
اس آیت میں بغیر تسمیہ مہر کے صحت طلاق کا حکم لگایا گیا ہے اور طلاق ہوتی ہے نکاح صحیح میں پس معلوم ہو گیا کہ ترک ذکر مہر صحت نکاح کے لئے مانع نہیں ہے۔ فرماتے ہیں کہ اسی طرح نکاح اس وقت بھی درست ہوگا جبکہ مہر کے نہ ہونے کی شرط لگا دی اسی سابقہ دلیل کی وجہ سے لیکن امام مالک کا اختلاف ہے۔ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ نفی مہر کی شرط سے نکاح درست نہیں ہوگا۔ اور دلیل یہ دیتے ہیں کہ نکاح عقد معاوضہ ہے۔ پس جس طرح بیچ میں اگر شمن کے نہ ہونے کی شرط لگادی تو بیع باطل ہوگی ۔ اسی طرح عدم مہر کی شرط کے ساتھ نکاح بھی درست نہیں ہوگا۔ لیکن ہم جوابدیں گے کہ اس پر سب کا اجماع ہے کہ اگر مہر کا ذکر ترک کر دیا جائے صراحتا نفی نہ کی جائے تو نکاح درست ہے۔ لہذا اسی طرح اگر مہر کی نفی کر دی جائے تب بھی درست ہونا چاہئے ۔ کیونکہ ترک ذکر میں حکم مختلف نہیں ہوتا مثلا بیع میں شمن کی نفی کی جائے یا شمن کا ذکر ترک کر دیا جائے دونوں صورتوں میں عقد بیع باطل ہوگا۔
مہر کی اکثر مقدار کی کوئی تحدید نہیں ۔ البتہ اقل مقدار مہر میں اختلاف ہے احناف کے نزدیک دس درہم ہے۔ امام مالک نے فرمایا کہ اقل مقدار مہر ربع دینار یا تین درہم ہیں ۔ ابن شبرمہ نے کہا کہ کم از کم پانچ درہم ہے۔ ابراہیم مخفی فرماتے ہیں کہ اقل مقدار مہر چالیس درہم ہے اور سعید ابن جبیر کے نزدیک کم از کم پچاس درہم ہونے چاہئیں ۔ حضرت امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ جس کو عقد بیع میں ثمن بنایا جا سکتا ہے اسکو عقد نکاح میں مہر بھی بنا سکتے ہیں۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مہر عورت کا حق ہے چنانچہ وصول کرنے اور ساقط کرنے میں عورت خود مختار ہے۔ معلوم ہوا کہ مہر عورت ہی کا حق ہے۔ لہذا اس کی مقدار معین کرنے کا حق بھی عورت ہی کو ہوگا۔ ہماری دلیل حدیث رسول لتی ہے۔ دس درہم سے کم مہر ہی نہیں ہے۔ دوسری عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مہر شریعت کا حق ہے بضع کی شرافت
Chapter of Mahr. Translation: This chapter is about mahr. Marriage is valid even if mahr is not specified, and similarly if one stipulates that there will be no mahr, the marriage is still valid. Book of Nikah. He said: Marriage is valid even if no mahr is mentioned in it, because nikah linguistically is a contract of joining and pairing, so it is completed by the spouses. Then mahr is wajib by shariah to manifest the honor of the place (buda'), so its mention is not needed for the validity of nikah. Similarly, if he marries her on condition that she has no mahr, due to what we have explained. In this there is a disagreement of Malik. And the minimum mahr is ten dirhams. Al-Shafi'i said: Whatever is permissible to be a price in sale is permissible to be mahr for her, because it is her right, so the determination is up to her. Our proof: the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) 'No mahr less than ten', and because it is a right of shariah, wajib to manifest the honor of the place, so it is determined by something significant, which is ten, analogically to the nisab of theft. (Urdu translation and commentary follow.)
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah covers the key rulings of mahr in the Hanafi school. The author begins by stating the chapter (Bab al-Mahr) and then presents the core ruling: a marriage is valid even if no mahr is specified at the time of contract, and even if the husband stipulates that no mahr will be given. The proof is that nikah is fundamentally a contract of union (causal insidmam wa izdiwaj), completed by the spouses' consent; mahr is an obligation imposed by Shariah to honor the marriage, not a condition for its validity. The author also mentions the dispute with Imam Malik, who holds that stipulating no mahr invalidates the marriage because nikah is a contract of exchange (mu'awada). The Hanafi response argues that since there is consensus that omitting mention of mahr (without explicit negation) does not invalidate, the same applies to explicit negation, as in sale where both omission and negation invalidate. Next, the minimum mahr is set at ten dirhams. Imam Shafi'i holds that any item valid as a price in sale can be mahr, leaving the amount to the woman. The Hanafi proof is the hadith 'No mahr less than ten dirhams' and a rational argument: mahr is a Shariah right to honor the private part (buda'), so it must be a significant amount, set at ten by analogy to the nisab for theft (ten dirhams). The commentary further elaborates, listing seven names of mahr from Quran and Hadith, providing additional proofs from Quranic verses (e.g., al-Baqarah 236-237) and addressing a potential objection that if mahr is wajib, how can marriage be valid without it? The answer is that the obligation of mahr is not a condition for validity but a consequence; the Quranic verse allowing divorce without fixing mahr confirms that marriage is valid without it.

Key Terms
مهر (mahr): The financial right (mal) that a husband must give to the wife as a wajib obligation upon marriage, to honor the marriage contract.
صداق (sadaq): A synonym for mahr, used in the Quran and referred to as the gift given to the wife.
نكاح (nikah): A contract of marriage, linguistically meaning union and pairing, legally a contract that permits intimacy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum amount for mahr (dowry) in a marriage?
A) Whatever the parties agree upon, with no minimum
B) Five dirhams
C) Ten dirhams
D) Forty dirhams

Key Takeaway
Mahr is an obligatory right of the wife, but its absence or insufficient amount does not invalidate the marriage; the minimum mahr is ten dirhams, and if not specified, mahr al-mithl is due.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
10 min
Validity of Nikah without Mahr and Dispute with Imam Malik
Ruling on nikah validity without mahr, with Quranic proof and Malik's objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of nikah without mahr, explain the Quranic proof, and evaluate Imam Malik's objection.

Core Idea
Nikah is valid even without mentioning mahr—mahr is wajib, not a condition of validity.

This passage addresses a common question: can a marriage contract be valid if no dower (mahr) is mentioned, or even if the husband explicitly stipulates no mahr? The Hanafi school affirms validity, relying on Quranic evidence and consensus, while Imam Malik analogizes nikah to a sale. We will explore the proofs and the analytical reasoning behind the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
The passage explicitly states that nikah is valid even if mahr is not mentioned. Note the distinction between mahr being wajib (obligatory) and being a shart (condition) of validity.
Omission of mahr does not affect the contract's validity.
2
Examine the Quranic proof
The verse (Surah al-Baqarah 2:236) permits divorce without specifying mahr, which implies that the nikah preceding it must be valid. This is the primary textual evidence.
Divorce is only valid in a valid marriage.
3
Extend to explicit negation
The same reasoning applies when the husband explicitly says 'no mahr'. The Hanafi school treats omission and negation the same, unlike in sale where both invalidate.
Consensus (ijma) on validity of omission supports this extension.
4
Compare with Imam Malik's objection
Malik argues by analogy to sale, which would make the contract invalid. The Hanafi response distinguishes nikah as a contract of union, not exchange, and cites the consensus.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Maliki invalidates, Hanafi validates.

کتاب النکاح
٢) عَلَيْقَةٌ
(۷) الْعَقْرُ
حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا اذو العلايق قيل يا رسول الله مالعلايق قال ماترضى الاهلون )
حدیث میں علایق سے مراد مہر ہے۔
حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا عفرنسا تھا کہ یہاں عقر سے مراد مہر ہے۔
ان سات ناموں میں چار قرآن میں اور تین احادیث میں مذکور ہیں۔
صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں نکاح صحیح ہوتا ہے اگر چہ آئمیں مہر مذکور نہ ہو۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ نکاح عقد انضمام اور عقد ازدواج کو کہتے ہیں۔ اور یہ معنی پورے ہو جاتے ہیں زوجین سے۔ لہذا صحت نکاح کیلئے مہر کا ذکر ضروری نہیں۔ دوسری دلیل یہ کہ قرآن میں ہے فانكحوا ما طاب لكم الآیة ۔ اب اگر ہم نے ذکر مہر کی شرط لگا دی تو نص پر زیادتی کرنالازم آئے گا جو درست نہیں۔ لیکن سوال یہ ہے کہ جب مہر شرعاً واجب ہے تو بغیر مہر کے نکاح کیسے درست ہوگا۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ وجوب مہر صحت نکاح کے لئے شرط نہیں بلکہ مہر واجب ہوا ہے شرافت محل یعنی بضع کی عظمت اور شرفت کو ظاہر کرنے کے لئے۔ لہذا صحت نکاح کے لئے مہر کے ذکر کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ اگر کوئی اشکال کرے کہ اس پر کیا دلیل ہے کہ صحت نکاح کے لئے مہر کے ذکر کی ضرورت نہیں ۔ جواب قرآن اس پر شاہد ہے، فرمایا گیا لا جناح عليكم ان طلقتم النساء مالم تمسوهن او تفرضوالهن فريضة ومتعواهن على الموسع قدره وعلى المقتر قدرہ ۔ (ترجمہ) کچھ گناہ نہیں تم پر اگر طلاق دو تم عورتوں کو اس وقت کہ ہاتھ بھی نہ لگایا ہو اور نہ مقرر کیا ہو ان کیلئے کچھ مہر اور ان کو خرچ دو مقدور والے پر اس کے موافق ہے اور تنگی والے پر اس کے موافق ۔
اس آیت میں بغیر تسمیہ مہر کے صحت طلاق کا حکم لگایا گیا ہے اور طلاق ہوتی ہے نکاح صحیح میں پس معلوم ہو گیا کہ ترک ذکر مہر صحت نکاح کے لئے مانع نہیں ہے۔ فرماتے ہیں کہ اسی طرح نکاح اس وقت بھی درست ہوگا جبکہ مہر کے نہ ہونے کی شرط لگا دی اسی سابقہ دلیل کی وجہ سے لیکن امام مالک کا اختلاف ہے۔ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ نفی مہر کی شرط سے نکاح درست نہیں ہوگا۔ اور دلیل یہ دیتے ہیں کہ نکاح عقد معاوضہ ہے۔ پس جس طرح بیچ میں اگر شمن کے نہ ہونے کی شرط لگادی تو بیع باطل ہوگی ۔ اسی طرح عدم مہر کی شرط کے ساتھ نکاح بھی درست نہیں ہوگا۔ لیکن ہم جوابدیں گے کہ اس پر سب کا اجماع ہے کہ اگر مہر کا ذکر ترک کر دیا جائے صراحتا نفی نہ کی جائے تو نکاح درست ہے۔ لہذا اسی طرح اگر مہر کی نفی کر دی جائے تب بھی درست ہونا چاہئے ۔ کیونکہ ترک ذکر میں حکم مختلف نہیں ہوتا مثلا بیع میں شمن کی نفی کی جائے یا شمن کا ذکر ترک کر دیا جائے دونوں صورتوں میں عقد بیع باطل ہوگا۔
Book of Nikah. 2) 'Aliqah. 7) al-'Aqr. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Those with 'ala'iq.' It was said: O Messenger of Allah, what are 'ala'iq? He said: 'What the family is pleased with.' In the hadith, 'ala'iq means mahr. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'He made 'aqr' as a slave woman'? Here 'aqr means mahr. Among these seven names, four are mentioned in the Quran and three in hadith. Sahib al-Quduri says: Nikah is valid even if mahr is not mentioned. The proof is that nikah is called a contract of union and a contract of marriage. And these meanings are fulfilled by the spouses. Therefore, mentioning mahr is not necessary for the validity of nikah. A second proof is that in the Quran it says: 'Then marry what is lawful for you' (4:3). If we impose the condition of mentioning mahr, then it would necessitate adding to the text, which is not correct. But the question is: when mahr is legally obligatory, how can nikah be valid without it? The answer is: the obligation of mahr is not a condition for the validity of nikah; rather, mahr is obligatory to manifest the honor of the place, i.e., the esteem and honor of the private part. Therefore, mentioning mahr is not necessary for the validity of nikah. If someone objects: what is the proof that mentioning mahr is not necessary for the validity of nikah? The answer is that the Quran bears witness to this: 'There is no blame upon you if you divorce women while you have not touched them or specified a right (mahr) for them, but give them a provision—the wealthy according to his capacity and the poor according to his capacity' (2:236). In this verse, the validity of divorce without specifying mahr is established, and divorce occurs only in a valid nikah. Thus it became known that omitting the mention of mahr is not an impediment to the validity of nikah. He says: Similarly, nikah will also be valid when the condition of no mahr is stipulated, based on the same previous proof, but Imam Malik differs. He says that nikah will not be valid with the condition of negating mahr. He gives the proof that nikah is a contract of exchange. So just as in sale, if the condition of no price is made, the sale becomes invalid, similarly nikah with the condition of no mahr will not be valid. But we will respond that there is consensus that if the mention of mahr is omitted explicitly without negation, nikah is valid. Therefore, similarly if mahr is negated, it should also be valid, because in omitting mention the ruling does not differ. For example, in sale, whether the price is negated or its mention is omitted, in both cases the sale contract is invalid.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya begins the Book of Nikah by listing seven names for mahr (dower), mentioning that four appear in the Quran and three in hadith. The author then presents the ruling from Quduri's matn: a nikah contract is valid even if no mahr is mentioned. The reasoning is that nikah is fundamentally a contract of union and companionship, not an exchange, so mahr is not a condition of validity. Two proofs are given: first, the linguistic meaning of nikah; second, the general command to marry without requiring mahr specification. An objection is raised: if mahr is obligatory, how can a contract without it be valid? The response distinguishes between wujub (obligation) and shart (condition); mahr is wajib but not a condition of validity. Its purpose is to honor the woman, not to validate the contract. The Quranic verse 2:236 is cited as evidence, where divorce is permitted before consummation and without specification of mahr—showing that nikah without mahr is valid. The passage then extends this to an explicit condition of no mahr, which is also valid in the Hanafi school. However, Imam Malik objects, analogizing nikah to sale: if no price is stipulated, the sale is invalid. The Hanafi response uses consensus (ijma) that omitting mahr is valid, and notes that the same applies to explicit negation, as the ruling on omission and negation does not differ in sale (both invalidate sale). Thus, the Hanafi position stands: mahr is not a condition for validity, and its negation does not invalidate the contract.

Key Terms
مهر (mahr): The dower given by the husband to the wife as a mandatory gift, obligatory upon marriage.
عقد معاوضہ (aqd mu'awadah): A commutative contract involving exchange of consideration, like sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on the validity of nikah when the husband explicitly stipulates that there will be no mahr?
A) The nikah is invalid because mahr is a condition for validity.
B) The nikah is valid and the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl.
C) The nikah is valid and the wife gets 10 dirhams.
D) The nikah is valid and the wife gets nothing.

Key Takeaway
Nikah is valid without mahr; mahr is obligatory separately and its absence or explicit negation does not invalidate the contract.

Nikah — Marriage

Minimum Mahr: Ten Dirhams and Dispute with Zufar
Establishes 10 dirhams as minimum mahr; discusses ruling when less is named, with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on minimum mahr, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Zufar, and explain the Hanafi response to Zufar's qiyas.

Core Idea
A mahr less than 10 dirhams is invalid; the wife gets 10 dirhams, not mahr al-mithl.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on the minimum mahr. The passage establishes 10 dirhams as the minimum and addresses the dispute with Imam Zufar. You will learn the proofs and the reasoning behind the Hanafi ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: the minimum mahr is 10 dirhams; if less is named, the wife receives 10 dirhams.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Zufar (within the Hanafi school) holds that mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory.
3
Examine Zufar's proof
Zufar uses qiyas: specifying an invalid amount is like no specification, which triggers mahr al-mithl.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes between the right of the Lawgiver (shar') and the right of the wife. The shar' right is fulfilled by 10; the wife's consent to less implies consent to 10. The analogy to no specification fails because a woman may forgo all but not accept a small amount.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi fixes payment at 10 dirhams; Zufar's view leads to mahr al-mithl, which may be more or less.
