مہر کی اکثر مقدار کی کوئی تحدید نہیں ۔ البتہ اقل مقدار مہر میں اختلاف ہے احناف کے نزدیک دس درہم ہے۔ امام مالک نے فرمایا کہ اقل مقدار مہر ربع دینار یا تین درہم ہیں ۔ ابن شبرمہ نے کہا کہ کم از کم پانچ درہم ہے۔ ابراہیم مخفی فرماتے ہیں کہ اقل مقدار مہر چالیس درہم ہے اور سعید ابن جبیر کے نزدیک کم از کم پچاس درہم ہونے چاہئیں ۔ حضرت امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ جس کو عقد بیع میں ثمن بنایا جا سکتا ہے اسکو عقد نکاح میں مہر بھی بنا سکتے ہیں۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مہر عورت کا حق ہے چنانچہ وصول کرنے اور ساقط کرنے میں عورت خود مختار ہے۔ معلوم ہوا کہ مہر عورت ہی کا حق ہے۔ لہذا اس کی مقدار معین کرنے کا حق بھی عورت ہی کو ہوگا۔ ہماری دلیل حدیث رسول لتی ہے۔ دس درہم سے کم مہر ہی نہیں ہے۔ دوسری عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مہر شریعت کا حق ہے بضع کی شرافت کو ظاہر کرنے کے لئے ۔ لہذا اتنی مقدار معین کی جائے جس سے شرافت محل اور شرافت بضع ظاہر ہو سکے۔ ہم نے دیکھا کہ نصاب سرقہ دس در ہم ہے تو گویا دس درہم چوری کرنے پر ہاتھ کاٹ دیا جاتا ہے۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ انسان کے ایک عضو یعنی ہاتھ کی کم از کم قیمت دس درہم ہے۔ چنانچہ اس پر قیاس کر کے نکاح میں بھی ملک بضع کی قیمت کم از کم دس درہم مقرر کی گئی ہے۔
دس در اہم سے کم مہر مقرر کیا تو دس دراہم مہر ہوں گے
و لو سمى اقل من عشرة فلها العشرة عندنا وقال زفر مهر المثل لان تسمية مالا يصلح مهرا كعدمها ولنا ان فساد هذه التسمية لحق الشرع وقدصار مقضيا بالعشرة فاما ما يرجع الى حقها فقد رضيت بالعشرة لرضاها بمادونها ولا معتبر بعدم التسمية لانها قد ترضى بالتمليك من غير عوض تكرما ولا ترضى فيه بالعوض اليسير ترجمہ اور اگر ذ کر کیا دس درہم سے کم تو عورت کے لئے دس درہم ہوں گے ہمارے نزدیک ۔ اور فر مایا امام زفر نے کہ مہر مثل ہے۔ اس لئے کہ اس چیز کا تسمیہ جو ہر بنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا ایسا ہی ہے جیسا کہ عدم تسمیہ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس تسمیہ کا فسادحق شرع کی وجہ سے ہے اور وہ پورا ہو گیا دس سے ۔ بہر حال وہ جو وٹے گا عورت کے حق کی طرف تو عورت راضی ہوگئی دس پر اس کے دس سے کم پر راضی ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ اور عدم تسمیہ معتبر ہیں اسلئے کہ کبھی راضی ہو جاتی ہے بغیر عوض مالک بنانے پر تکر نما اور نہیں راضی ہوتی اس میں تھوڑے عوض پر۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ انعقاد نکاح کے وقت دس درہم سے کم مہر ذکر کیا گیا تو اس صورت میں ہمارے نزدیک عورت کے لئے دس درہم ہوں گے۔ اور امام زفر کے نزدیک مہر مثل واجب ہوگا۔ امام زفر کی دلیل قیاس ہے۔ حاصل قیاس یہ ہے کہ ایسی چیز کو ہر بنانا جومہر بنے کی صلاحیت نہ رکھتی ہو وہ عدم تسمیہ کے مانند ہے۔ اور عدم تسمیہ کی صورت میں مہرمشکل واجب ہوتا ہے لہذا اس صورت میں بھی مہر مثل واجب ہوگا۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ دس درہم سے کم کے تسمیہ کا فساد حق شرع کی وجہ سے ہے۔ اور حق شرع پورا ہو جاتا ہے دس درہم سے ۔ لہذا دس درہم پورے کر دیے جائیں ، زیادہ کی ضرورت نہیں۔ اب رہی یہ بات کہ دس درہم پر عورت بھی راضی ہے یا نہیں تو ہم کہتے ہیں کہ جب وہ بھلی مانس دس سے کم پر راضی ہو گئی تو دس درہم پر بدرجہ اولیٰ راضی ہوگی حاصل یہ کہ مہر میں شارع اور زوجہ دونوں کا حق ہے لہذا ان دونوں کی رعایت ضروری ہوگی۔ اور دس درہم میں دونوں کی رعایت ہو جاتی ہے۔ کیونکہ شارع کا تو حق ہی دس درہم تک ہے اور زائد میں .
اگر چہ عورت کا حق ہے لیکن وہ دس سے کم پر راضی ہونے کی وجہ سے زائد میں اپنا حق ساقط کر چکی ، جس کا اس کو پورا پورا اختیار ہے۔ امام زفر کے قیاس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ دس سے کم کے تسمیہ کو عدم تسمیہ پر قیاس کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ انسان کبھی اپنے پورے حق کو ساقط کر دینے پر راضی ہو جاتا ہے فکر ما اور تفصل تناسل جمیل کو طلب کرنے کے لئے۔ اور شی قلیل پر راضی نہیں ہوتا۔ اسی طرح یہاں ہے کہ عورت بلاعوض تملیک پر راضی ہو سکتی ہے اپنے تکرم اور تفضل کو ظاہر کرنے کے لئے لیکن ترفعاً عوض قلیل اور معمولی چیز پر بھی راضی نہیں ہو سکتی ہے۔ پس اس سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا ہے کہ اگر عورت بالکل مہر نہ لینے پر راضی ہو جائے تو دس سے کم پر بھی راضی ہو جائیگی ۔ لہذا یہ قیاس غلط ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
There is no limit on the maximum amount of mahr. However, there is a difference of opinion on the minimum amount of mahr. According to the Hanafis, it is ten dirhams. Imam Malik said that the minimum mahr is a quarter dinar or three dirhams. Ibn Shubrumah said the minimum is five dirhams. Ibrahim al-Makhifi said the minimum mahr is forty dirhams, and Sa'id ibn Jubayr held that it should be at least fifty dirhams. Imam al-Shafi'i said that whatever can be made a price in a sale contract can be made mahr in a marriage contract. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that mahr is the right of the woman; thus she is independent in receiving and remitting it. This indicates that mahr is solely the woman's right. Therefore, the right to determine its amount also belongs to her. Our (Hanafi) proof is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'There is no mahr less than ten dirhams.' The second rational proof is that mahr is a legal right to manifest the honor of the private part. Therefore, an amount should be fixed that can manifest the honor of the place and the honor of the private part. We observe that the nisab (minimum threshold) for theft (sariqa) is ten dirhams, meaning that for stealing ten dirhams, the hand is cut off. Thus it is known that the minimum value of a human limb—the hand—is ten dirhams. By analogy (qiyas) to this, the price of ownership of the private part in marriage is set at a minimum of ten dirhams.
If he specifies less than ten dirhams as mahr, she will get ten dirhams according to us. Zufar said (she gets) mahr al-mithl (proper dower), because specifying something that is not fit to be mahr is like not specifying it at all. Our proof is that the invalidity of this specification is due to the right of the Lawgiver, and that (right) is fulfilled by ten. As for what reverts to her right, she is pleased with ten because she is pleased with less than ten. And the case of no specification is not comparable, because sometimes she agrees to be made owner without any consideration out of generosity, but she does not agree to a small consideration. Explanation of the issue: At the time of contracting the marriage, if mahr of less than ten dirhams is mentioned, then according to us the wife will get ten dirhams. According to Imam Zufar, mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory. Imam Zufar's proof is analogy (qiyas): making something that is not fit to be mahr as mahr is like no specification, and in the case of no specification, mahr al-mithl is obligatory, so here too mahr al-mithl is obligatory. Our proof is that the invalidity of specifying less than ten dirhams is due to the right of the Lawgiver, and that right is fulfilled by ten dirhams. So ten dirhams should be completed; more is not needed. As for whether the wife is pleased with ten, we say that since she was voluntarily pleased with less than ten, she would a fortiori be pleased with ten. The conclusion is that both the Lawgiver and the wife have a right in mahr; therefore, both must be considered. And in ten dirhams, both are considered because the Lawgiver's right is only up to ten dirhams, and as for the excess, although it is the wife's right, she has waived her right to the excess by being pleased with less than ten, and she has full authority to do so. The response to Imam Zufar's analogy is that it is not correct to analogize specifying less than ten to no specification, because a person may be pleased to relinquish his entire right out of magnanimity and seeking beautiful conduct, but he is not pleased with a small amount. Similarly, here the wife may agree to being given ownership without any consideration to show her generosity and favor, but out of dignity she cannot be pleased with a small and insignificant consideration. Therefore, it does not follow that if the wife agrees to take no mahr at all, she would also agree to less than ten. So this analogy is incorrect. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya addresses the minimum amount of mahr. It begins by stating that there is no maximum limit, but the minimum is disputed. The Hanafi position is ten dirhams, supported by a hadith (though not directly quoted in this text) and rational proof based on qiyas (analogy) to the nisab of theft (sariqa). The reasoning is that if stealing ten dirhams warrants cutting off the hand (a limb), then the minimum value of a limb is ten dirhams; by analogy, the value of ownership of the private part in marriage should be at least ten dirhams. The text then presents the ruling: if a husband specifies a mahr less than ten dirhams, the wife is entitled to ten dirhams, not mahr al-mithl. This is the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi). Imam Zufar, a Hanafi jurist, disagrees, arguing that since the specified amount is invalid, it is as if no mahr was specified, so mahr al-mithl is due. The Hanafi response distinguishes between two rights in mahr: the right of the Lawgiver (shar') and the right of the wife. The Shar' requires a minimum of ten dirhams, so that deficiency is corrected by raising it to ten. The wife, by agreeing to less, has implicitly waived any right to more, but since the Shar' requires ten, she gets ten. The analogy to no specification fails because a woman may forgo mahr entirely out of generosity but would not accept a negligible amount. Thus, the Hanafi position stands: naming less than ten dirhams obligates ten dirhams, not mahr al-mithl.

Key Terms
اقل مهر (aqall mahr): The minimum legally permissible amount of mahr, which is 10 dirhams in the Hanafi school.
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower equivalent to the mahr given to women of similar status (family, beauty, etc.).
نصاب سرقہ (nisab al-sariqa): The minimum value of stolen goods (10 dirhams) that triggers the hadd punishment of hand amputation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a husband specifies a mahr of 5 dirhams at the time of nikah, what is the wife entitled to?
A) 5 dirhams as specified.
B) Mahr al-mithl (proper dower).
C) 10 dirhams.
D) The marriage is invalid and she gets nothing.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the minimum mahr is 10 dirhams; if less is named, the wife receives 10 dirhams, not mahr al-mithl.

Nikah — Marriage

Half of Specified Mahr on Divorce Before Consummation
Ruling on half mahr with intra-Hanafi dispute and conflicting qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr when divorce occurs before consummation, distinguish the position of Imam Zufar, and explain why conflicting qiyas are set aside for the nass.

Core Idea
When conflicting analogies yield opposite results, the clear Quranic text prevails: half the specified mahr is wajib.

In this lesson, we examine a key ruling in Hanafi nikah: the obligation of half the specified mahr upon divorce before consummation. The passage presents the school's position, an intra-Hanafi dissent by Imam Zufar, and a fascinating legal reasoning involving two conflicting analogies. Understanding this ruling sharpens your ability to prioritize nass over qiyas when analogy is inconclusive.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is divorce before consummation where a mahr was specified. The ruling: half of the specified mahr is wajib upon the husband.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is Quran 2:237, which explicitly commands giving half of the specified mahr when divorce occurs before touching.
The verse is qati' al-thubut and qati' al-dalalah in Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Zufar holds that mut'ah (a consolation gift) is wajib instead, because he considers the specified mahr to revert to mahr al-mithl before consummation, and for mahr al-mithl, mut'ah is due.
Zufar's view is rejected (marjuh) in the madhhab; the three imams' view is mufta bihi.
4
Analyze the conflicting qiyas
First qiyas: likening to a buyer destroying goods before delivery, which would require full mahr. Second qiyas: likening to rescission of sale, which would require nothing. Both analogies conflict.
Because the qiyas are contradictory, they cannot determine the ruling.
5
Conclude with tarjih
The text (nass) is decisive over conflicting qiyas. The Quran commands half, so half is wajib. The condition 'before seclusion' is added because valid seclusion (khalwah) is equivalent to consummation in Hanafi law.
Thus, if seclusion occurred, the full mahr is due.

ترجمہ اور اگر طلاق دی اس عورت کے ساتھ دخول سے پہلے تو پانچ درہم واجب ہوں گے ہمارے علماء ثالثہ کے نزدیک اور امام زفر کے نزدیک متعہ واجب ہوگا جیسا کہ جب کچھ ذکر نہیں کیا تھا۔

دس در اہم یا زیادہ مقرر کئے گئے تو مقررہ مہر لازم ہوگا
ومن سمى مهرا عشرة فمازاد فعليه المسمى ان دخل بها اومات عنها لانه بالدخول يتحقق تسليم المبدل و به يتاكد البدل وبالموت ينتهى النكاح نهايته والشيء بانتهائه يتقرر ويتاكد فيتقرر بجميع مواجبه وان طلقها قبل الدخول والخلوة فلها نصف المسمى لقوله تعالى وان طلقتموهن من قبل ان تمسوهن الآية والاقيسة متعارضة ففيه تفويت الزوج الملك على نفسه باختياره وفيه عود المعقود عليه اليها سالما فكان المرجع فيه النص وشرط ان يكون قبل الخلوة لانها كالدخول عندنا على مانبينه ان شاء الله تعالى
ترجمہ اور وہ شخص کہ مقرر کیا مہر دس درہم یا زیادہ تو شوہر پر سمی ہے۔ اگر اس نے بیوی کے ساتھ دخول کیا یا مر گیا اس سے (اس کو چھوڑ کر ) اس لئے کہ دخول کی وجہ سے مبدل کو سپرد کرنا متفق ہوگا اور اس بضع کی سپردگی سے بدل مؤکد ہوتا ہے۔ اور موت سے نکاح اپنی انتہا کو پہنچ جاتا ہے۔ اور شی اپنی انتہا سے منتقررا اور مؤکد ہو جاتی ہے پس نکاح مقر ر ہو گا اپنے تمام احکام کے ساتھ ۔ اور اگر طلاق دی اسکو دخول اور خلوت سے پہلے تو اس عورت کے لئے نصف مسمی ہے باری تعالیٰ کے قول وان طلقتموهن الآيه كى وجہ سے یعنی اگر طلاق دیدی تم نے ان عورتوں کو چھونے سے پہلے اور مقرر کیا ان کے لئے مہر تو مقرر کئے ہوئے کا نصف ہوگا۔ اور قیاس متعارض ہیں۔ پس طلاق قبل الدخول اور قبل الخلوت میں زوج کا اپنے اختیار سے اپنے حق میں ملک کو فوت کر دیتا ہے۔ اور اسی طلاق قبل الدخول والخلوت میں معقود عالیہ کا عورت کی طرف صحیح سالم لوٹ آتا ہے۔ پس مدار اس میں نص ہوگی۔ اور قدوری نے شرط لگائی ہے کہ طلاق قبل الفلوت ہو۔ اس لئے کہ خلوت دخول کے مانند ہے ہمارے نزدیک اسی تفصیل پر جسکو ہم انشاء اللہ بیان کریں گے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ شوہر نے بیوی کا مہر مقرر کر دیا دس درہم یا زیادہ۔ پھر اس کے بعد دخول پایا گیا۔ یا احد الزوجین کا انتقال ہو گیا تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں شوہر پر کل مسمی واجب ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ دخول کی وجہ سے بدل یعنی بضع کا سپر ذکر نا متفق ہوگیا اور مبدل کے سپرد کرنے سے بدل واجب ہو جاتا ہے۔ لہذا شوہر پر بدل یعنی مہر واجب ہوگا۔ اور موت کی وجہ سے شئی اپنی انتہاء کو پہنچ جاتی ہے۔ اس
کے بعد کوئی چیز باقی نہیں رہتی۔ اور شئی اپنی انتہاء کو پہنچ کر متقر اور مؤکد ہو جاتی ہے یعنی نا قابل تغیر ۔ پس نکاح اپنے تمام احکام و مواجب کے ساتھ ثابت ہوگا اور حکم نکاح مہر بھی ہے۔ لہذا موت کی وجہ سے یہ بھی ثابت ہوگا۔
دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ اس عورت کو دخول اور خلوت سے پہلے طلاق دیدی تو شوہر پر عورت کے لئے نصف مسمی واجب ہوگا۔ دلیل میں صاحب ہدایہ نے آیت پیش کی ہے، یعنی جماع سے پہلے اگر تم نے طلاق دیدی اور مہر مقرر کر رکھا ہے تو مقرر کردہ میں سے نصف دیدو۔ آیت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ طلاق قبل الدخول سے نصف مہر واجب ہو گا۔ طلاق قبل الدخول میں دو قیاس باہم متعارض ہیں ، چنانچہ ایک قیاس کا تقاضا تو یہ ہے کہ شوہر پر کل سمی واجب ہو کیونکہ شوہر نے اپنے اختیار سے اپنے حق میں ملک بضع کو فوت کر دیا۔ یہ ایسا ہو گیا کہ مشتری نے مبیع کو ہلاک کر دیا بائع کے سپرد کرنے سے پہلے تو مشتری پر کل شمن واجب ہوگا۔ پس ایسا ہی یہاں بھی ہوگا ، دوسرے قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ شوہر پر کچھ بھی واجب نہ ہو۔ نہ کل مسمی نہ نصف مسمی۔ کیونکہ طلاق قبل الدخول کی صورت میں معقود علیہ یعنی بضع صحیح سالم عورت کی طرف لوٹ آیا۔ پس جب مبدل عورت کو پورے کا پورا واپس مل گیا تو شوہر پر بدل واجب نہیں ہوگا، جیسا کہ عقد بیع کو فتح کر دینے کی صورت میں جب مبیع بائع کی طرف لوٹ آئی تو مشتری پرشن واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ اسی طرح یہاں بھی شوہر پر کچھ واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ پس جب دونوں قیاس متعارض ہیں تو نص کی طرف رجوع کریں گے اور نص میں نصف مسمی واجب کیا گیا ہے۔ لہذا نص کے مطابق شوہر پر اس صورت میں نصف مسمی واجب ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قدوری نے کہا قبل الفلوت یعنی خلوت سے پہلے کی شرط لگائی اس لئے کہ ہمارے نزدیک خلوت دخول کے مرتبہ میں ہے لہذا جو حکم دخول کا ہو گا وہی خلوت کا ہوگا۔
Before consummation, in divorce, five dirhams become obligatory when mahr was not specified. And if he divorces her before consummation, five are obligatory according to our three imams; according to Imam Zufar, mut'ah is obligatory as when nothing was named. Explanation: In the aforementioned issue, if divorce before consummation occurred, according to us five dirhams are obligatory. According to Imam Zufar, mut'ah is obligatory for the woman because in his view mahr al-mithl was obligatory, and in case of mahr al-mithl, if divorce before consummation occurs, mut'ah is obligatory. So here mut'ah is obligatory. According to us, ten dirhams were specified, so in case of divorce before consummation, half of the specified amount is obligatory, which is five dirhams. He who specifies a mahr of ten or more, upon him is the specified amount if he consummates with her or dies from her, because by consummation delivery of the subject matter is realized and by it the compensation is confirmed, and by death the marriage reaches its end, and something by its end becomes established and confirmed, so it is established with all its obligations. And if he divorces her before consummation and seclusion, she gets half of the specified mahr due to the saying of Allah: 'And if you divorce them before you have touched them...' and the analogies are conflicting: in it the husband forfeits ownership of himself by choice, and in it the subject of contract returns to her intact, so the reference in it is to the text. And a condition is that it be before seclusion because seclusion is like consummation according to us, as we will explain if Allah wills. Translation: And the person who specified a mahr of ten dirhams or more, upon him is the specified amount. If he consummated with the wife or died from her, because by consummation delivery of the subject matter is realized, and by that delivery the compensation is confirmed. And by death the marriage reaches its end, and something by its end becomes established and confirmed, so the marriage is established with all its rulings. And if he divorced her before consummation and seclusion, then for her is half of the specified amount due to the verse 'And if you divorce them...' meaning if you divorce them before touching and you have specified a mahr, then half of what you specified. And the analogies are conflicting: in divorce before consummation and seclusion, the husband forfeits ownership in his right by his choice, and in it the subject of contract returns to the wife intact. So the reference in this is the text. And al-Quduri conditioned that the divorce be before seclusion, because seclusion is like consummation according to us on the detail we will explain if Allah wills. Explanation: The case is that the husband specified a mahr of ten dirhams or more. Then consummation occurred, or one of the spouses died. In both cases, the full specified amount is obligatory on the husband. The proof is that by consummation the compensation, i.e., the subject matter, is delivered, and by delivery of the subject matter the compensation becomes obligatory. Therefore the husband owes the mahr. And by death, the thing reaches its end, after which nothing remains. And a thing reaching its end becomes established and confirmed, i.e., unchangeable. So the marriage is established with all its rulings and obligations, and one of the rulings of marriage is the mahr. Therefore it is also established by death. The second case is that he divorced her before consummation and seclusion, then the husband owes her half of the specified mahr. The author of Hidayah presented the verse as proof, meaning if you divorce before intercourse and you have specified a mahr, then give half of what was specified. The verse indicates that divorce before consummation makes half of the mahr obligatory. In divorce before consummation, two analogies conflict with each other. One analogy requires that the husband owes the full specified amount because the husband by his own choice forfeited ownership of the subject matter (budge). This is like a buyer destroying the sold item before delivery by the seller, in which case the buyer owes the full price. So here too. The second analogy requires that the husband owes nothing, neither full nor half, because in divorce before consummation, the subject matter (budge) returns to the woman intact. When the subject matter is returned to the woman in full, the husband does not owe compensation, just as in the case of cancellation of a sale when the sold item returns to the seller, the buyer does not owe the price. So here too the husband owes nothing. When the two analogies conflict, we resort to the text, and in the text half of the specified amount is made obligatory. Therefore according to the text, the husband owes half the specified amount in this case. The author of Hidayah says: al-Quduri stated the condition that it be before seclusion, because according to us seclusion has the status of consummation, so the same ruling as for consummation applies to seclusion.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on mahr when a husband divorces his wife before consummation, but after specifying a mahr. The Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad) holds that the wife is entitled to half of the specified mahr. Imam Zufar among the Hanafis differs, arguing that here mahr al-mithl applies (since the specified mahr was not confirmed?), and thus mut'ah (a consolation gift) is obligatory instead. The author then explains that when a mahr is specified (ten dirhams or more), it becomes fully obligatory upon consummation or death of either spouse, as these events confirm the marriage and the mahr. If divorce occurs before consummation and valid seclusion (khalwah), the wife receives half the specified mahr, based on the Quranic verse (2:237) which explicitly states this. The text highlights a conflict between two analogies: one analogy (like sale with destruction) would demand full mahr, another (like rescission of sale) would demand nothing. Since these analogies conflict, the text (nass) is decisive, giving half. Additionally, al-Quduri's condition of 'before seclusion' is noted because Hanafis consider valid seclusion equivalent to actual consummation in confirming the full mahr. Thus, if divorce occurs after seclusion, the full mahr is due.

Key Terms
متعہ (mut'ah): A consolation gift given to a divorced woman, not part of the mahr.
مہر مسمی (mahr musamma): The mahr explicitly specified in the marriage contract.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning used to derive rulings; here two conflicting analogies are presented.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if a husband specifies a mahr of 10 dirhams and then divorces his wife before consummation and before valid seclusion, what is the wife entitled to?
A) Half of the specified mahr (5 dirhams)
B) The full specified mahr (10 dirhams)
C) A consolation gift (mut'ah) only
D) Nothing, because she did not permit consummation

Key Takeaway
When conflicting analogies give opposite results, the explicit Quranic text prevails and determines the ruling: half the specified mahr.

Mahr al-Mithl and Mut'ah: When No Mahr Is Specified
Ruling on mithl mahr and mut’ah with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr al-mithl and mut'ah, and compare it with the Shafi'i and Maliki positions.

Core Idea
Mahr is a shari'ah obligation that cannot be negated initially; only remission after establishment is valid.

When a marriage contract is made without specifying mahr, what are the wife's rights? The Hanafi school holds that mahr al-mithl becomes due upon consummation or death, and mut'ah upon divorce before consummation. This lesson examines the evidence and the disagreements with the Shafi'i and Maliki schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Scenarios
Recognize the two cases: when no mahr is mentioned in the contract, and when the contract explicitly states 'no mahr'.
Both lead to the same Hanafi ruling.
2
State the Hanafi Ruling for Each
For consummation or death: mahr al-mithl is wajib. For divorce before consummation: mut'ah is wajib.
Mahr al-mithl is determined by peers' mahr; mut'ah is a consolation gift.
3
Compare with Shafi'i and Maliki Positions
Shafi'i: no mahr upon death (only upon consummation). Maliki: mut'ah is mustahabb, not wajib.
Focus on the practical difference: Hanafi gives mahr al-mithl to heirs on death; Shafi'i gives nothing.
4
Analyze the Quranic Dalil and Usul Principle
The imperative 'متعوهن' in 2:236 is taken by Hanafis as indicating obligation (wajib). The opposing schools interpret it differently.
Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-wujub unless there is a contrary indicator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مہر مقرر کئے بغیر نکاح کیا یا اس شرط پر نکاح کیا کہ مہر نہیں ہوگا تو مہر مثل لازم ہے
قال وان تزوجها ولم يسم لها مهرا او تزوجها على ان لامهر لها فلها مهر مثلها ان دخل بها اومات عنها وقال الشافعى لا يجب شىء فى الموت واكثرهم على انه يجب فى الدخول له ان المهر خالص حقها فتتمكن من نفيه ابتداء كما تتمكن من اسقاطه انتهاء ولنا ان المهروجوبا حق الشرع على ما مر وانما يصير حقا لها في حالة البقاء فتملك الابراء دون النفى ولو طلقها قبل الدخول بها فلها المتعة لقوله تعالى ومتعوهن على الموسع قدره الأية ثم هذه المتعة واجبة رجوعا الى الامر وفيه خلاف مالک
ترجمہ اور اگر نکاح کیا عورت سے اور اس کے لیئے مہر ذکر نہیں کیا یا نکاح کیا اس سے اس شرط پر کہ اس کیلئے مہر نہیں تو اس عورت کیلئے مہر مثل ہوگا۔ اگر اس سے دخول کیا یا اس کو چھوڑ کر مر گیا۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ موت کی صورت میں کوئی چیز واجب نہیں ہوتی ہے اور اکثر شوافع اس مسلک پر ہیں کہ دخول کی صورت میں واجب ہوگا ، امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مہر خالص عورت کا حق ہے پس وہ قادر ہوگی اس کی نفی کر دینے پر ابتداء جس طرح قادر ہے اس کو ساقط کر دینے پر انتہاء ۔ اور ہمارے مسلک پر استدلال یہ ہے کہ مہر و جو با حق شرع ہے اور عورت کا حق ہوگا حالت بقاء میں ، پس وہ عورت بری کر دینے کی مالک تو ہوگی لیکن نفی کر دینے کی مالک نہیں ہو سکتی ہے اور اگر طلاق دی اس کو قبل الدخول تو اس عورت کیلئے متعہ ہے باری تعالیٰ کے قول و متعومن “ کی وجہ سے یعنی متعہ دو اُن کو مقدور والے پر اس
کی وسعت کے مطابق ، پھر یہ متعہ واجب ہے امر کی طرف رجوع کرتے ہوئے اور اسمیں امام مالک کا اختلاف ہے۔
If he marries a woman and does not specify a mahr for her, or marries her on the condition that she has no mahr, then she has her mahr al-mithl if he consummates with her or dies from her. Al-Shafi'i said: Nothing is obligatory in the case of death, and most of his followers hold that it is obligatory in the case of consummation. His proof is that mahr is her pure right, so she has the power to negate it initially just as she has the power to drop it finally. Our proof is that mahr is obligatory as a right of shari'ah as mentioned earlier, and it becomes her right only in the state of survival; thus she has the power to remit (ibra') but not to negate it. And if he divorces her before consummation, then she has mut'ah due to the saying of Allah: 'And give them a provision (mut'ah) - the wealthy according to his means...' Then this mut'ah is obligatory by referring to the command, and there is a difference of opinion with Malik.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage deals with two scenarios when no mahr is specified in the marriage contract. First, if the husband consummates the marriage or dies, the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the mahr of her peers), according to the Hanafi school. Imam al-Shafi'i differs, arguing that mahr is purely the woman's right, so she can negate it initially (by agreeing to no mahr) just as she can waive it later. Hence, in his view, no mahr is obligatory upon death, though most Shafi'is require it upon consummation. The Hanafi response is that mahr is an obligation imposed by shari'ah; it becomes the woman's right only in the sense of survival (i.e., after the contract is effective), so she can remit it after it is established but cannot negate it from the start. Second, if the husband divorces before consummation, the wife receives mut'ah (a consolation gift), based on the Quranic command (2:236). Hanafis consider this mut'ah obligatory (wajib) because the imperative form indicates obligation, although Imam Malik regards it as recommended (mustahabb) rather than obligatory. The passage thus presents the Hanafi position on mahr al-mithl and mut'ah, with inter-madhhab disagreements with Shafi'i and Malik.

Key Terms
مہر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The mahr equivalent to that of women similar to the wife in status, used when no mahr is specified.
متعہ (mut'ah): A provision given to a divorced woman as consolation; here it is wajib on divorce before consummation when no mahr specified.
ابراء (ibra'): Remission or waiver of a right after it is established.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a man marries a woman without specifying any mahr and later divorces her before consummation, what is she entitled to?
A) Half of mahr al-mithl
B) Full mahr al-mithl
C) Mut'ah only
D) Nothing, because she agreed to no mahr

Key Takeaway
Mahr al-mithl is wajib upon consummation or death; mut'ah is wajib upon divorce before consummation; mahr cannot be initially negated, only remitted after establishment.

Mahr and Mut'ah in Cases of Silence or Negation of Mahr
Explains ruling on mahr when not specified or negated, inter-madhhab dispute with Shafi'i, and obligation of mut'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr al-mithl when mahr is not specified or negated, explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i and Maliki proofs regarding mahr and mut'ah, and apply the Hanafi position on mut'ah's amount and conditions.

Core Idea
Mahr is a Sharī'ah right that the wife cannot forgo until it is established; mut'ah is wajib as a command.

When a marriage is contracted without specifying a mahr or even with a condition of no mahr, what does Sharī'ah require? This lesson explores the Hanafi position that mahr al-mithl becomes wajib upon consummation or death, and that the wife cannot negate mahr at the outset. It also examines the obligatory mut'ah for a woman divorced before consummation when no mahr was fixed. We will engage with the proofs of opposing schools and see how Hanafi usul resolves these disputes.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on mahr when silent or negated
Identify the two scenarios (silence and negation) and the condition that triggers wajib mahr al-mithl: consummation or death of the husband.
Remember that in Hanafi fiqh, mahr is a right of both Sharī'ah and the guardians, not solely the woman's.
2
Examine the Shafi'i objection and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that since mahr is the woman's right, she can waive it at inception, citing a hadith about inheritance without dower.
The hadith involves a specific case (a wife who died after a defective marriage).
3
Analyze the Hanafi response using the three rights framework
Mahr comprises a right of Sharī'ah (minimum 10 dirhams), a right of guardians (to protect dignity), and the woman's right. The first two cannot be negated initially; the woman's right only operates after its establishment.
This distinction is key to understanding why initial negation is invalid.
4
State the Hanafi ruling on mut'ah and the Maliki objection
Mut'ah is wajib upon divorce before consummation when no mahr was specified. The imperative 'amti'ū' and words 'haqqan' and 'alā' prove obligation. Imam Malik considers it mustahabb, citing the term 'muhsin'.
Hanafi response: 'muhsin' refers to those who fulfill obligations, not only volunteers.
5
Apply the rules on mut'ah's amount and conditions
Mut'ah consists of three garments. The correct opinion considers the husband's financial status (based on 'alā al-mūsi' and 'alā al-muqtir'). It must not exceed half of mahr al-mithl and not be less than five dirhams.
The lower limit comes from the substitute for the vulva being at least ten dirhams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چهارم کتاب النکاح تشریح مصنف نے دو صورتیں بیان کی ہیں، اول یہ کہ نکاح کیا اور مہر کے بارے میں سکوت کیا نہ ذکر کیا اور نہ نفی کی ، دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ نکاح کیا اور مہر کے نہ ہونے کی شرط گادی ان دونوں صورتوں میں ہمارے نزدیک مہر مثل واجب ہوگا بشرطیکہ بیوی سے دخول کیا یا زوج کا انتقال ہوگا۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ موت قبل الدخول کی صورت میں شوہر پر کچھ واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ اور اکثر شوافع کہتے ہیں کہ دخول کی صورت میں مہر مثل واجب ہوگا، جیسا کہ ہمارا مذہب ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مہر خالصہ عورت کا حق ہے پس جس طرح وہ انتہاء ساقط کرنے پر قدرت رکھتی ہے اسی طرح ابتداء بھی نفی کرنے پر قدرت حاصل ہے۔ امام شافعی ایک حدیث سے بھی استدلال کرے ہیں جو حضرت علی ، زید بن ثابت ، ابن عباس اور ابن عمرؓ سے مروی ہے، الفاظ حدیث یہ ہیں "قالوا لها الميراث ولا صداق لها و عليها العدة" یعنی اس عورت کیلئے میراث ہے اور مہر نہیں اور اس پر عدت ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مہر جو و جو با شریعت کا حق ہے، آیت ان تبتغوا باموالکم اور آیت " قد علمنا ما فرضنا‘ کی وجہ سے۔ دونوں آیات کی تفصیل اصول فقہ کی کتابوں میں موجود ہے، دیکھ لیا جائے ۔ بعض لوگوں نے کہا کہ مہر میں تین حق ہیں: (۱) حق شرع ... حق شرع تو یہ ہے کہ دس درہم سے کم نہ ہو۔ اور (۲) اولیاء کا حق اولیاء کا حق یہ ہے کہ مہر مشکل سے کم نہ ہو۔ (۳) تیسرے عورت کا حق عورت کا حق یہ ہے کہ مہر اس کی ملک ہے لیکن حق شرع اور حق اولیاء صرف ابتداء نکاح کے وقت معتبر ہیں اور عورت کا حق حالت بقاء میں ہے لہذا عورت انتہا تو ساقط کر سکتی ہے ابتداء نفی نہیں کر سکتی ۔ پس امام شافعی کا یہ کہنا ابتداء نفی کر دینے پر قادر ہے اپنے حق سے تجاوز کرنا ہے جس کی شرعاً اجازت نہیں۔ اور اگر اس عورت کو طلاق قبل الدخول دی تو اس کیلئے متعہ واجب ہوگا۔ دلیل آیت ہے " لا جناح عليكم ان طلقتموا النساء ما لم تمسوهن او تفرضو لهن فريضة و متعوهن " آیت میں "او" معنی " و " ہے یعنی تم پر کوئی حرج نہیں اگر تم نے طلاق دیدی عورتوں کو جبتک کہ ان کو مس نہیں کیا اور نہیں مقرر کیا متطوع کو کہتے ہیں، یعنی نفل کام کرنے والا ۔ ہماری دلیل اور امام مالک کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ستعوا امر کا صیغہ ہے جو وجوب کیلئے آتا ہے، دوسرا لفظ " حقا ہے یہ بھی وجوب پر دلالت کرتا ہے۔ تیسر الفظ ”علی“ جو الزام کیلئے آتا ہے اور رہا لفظ "محسن" تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ وہ لوگ جو واجب کو ادا کرتے ہیں اور اپنی طرف سے احسان کے طو پر زیادہ کرتے ہیں۔ لہذا اب لفظ "محسنین امام مالک کا مستدل نہیں ہو سکتا۔ متعہ تین کپڑے ہیں والمتعة ثلثة اثواب من كسوة مثلها وهى درع وخمار و ملحفة وهذا التقدير مروى عن عائشة وابن عباس وقوله من كسوة مثلها اشارة الى انها يعتبر حالها وهو قول الكرخى فى المتعة الواجبة لقيامها مقام مهر المثل والصحيح انه يعتبر حاله عملا بالنص وهو قوله تعالى على الموسع قدره و على المقتر قدره ثم هي لاتزاد على نصف مهر مثلها ولاتنقص عن خمسة دراهم ويعرف ذلك في الاصل تشریح متعہ کی حقیقت یہ ہے کہ وہ تین کپڑے ہیں کرتہ، اوڑھنی ، چادر۔ یہ تین کپڑوں کی تعیین و تقدیر حضرت عائشہ اور ابن عباس رضی اللہ عنہما سے منقول ہے۔ صاحب قدوری کی عبارت " من كسوة مثلها “ سے اشارہ اس طرف ہے کہ متعہ میں عورت کے حال کا اعتبار ہوگا ۔ متعہ واجبہ میں امام کرختی کا یہی قول ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ متعہ مہر مثل کے قائم مقام ہے اور مہر مثل میں عورتوں کا حال معتبر ہے، لہذا جو اس کا قائم مقام ہے اس میں بھی عورت ہی کے حال کا اعتبار ہوگا ۔ اور صحیح قول یہ ہے کہ مرد کے حال کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ ان کی دلیل قرآن کی آیت ”على الموسع قدره وعلى المقتر قدرہ “اللہ تعالیٰ نے مرد کے حال کا اعتبار کیا نہ کہ عورت کے حال کا ۔ متعہ تین طرح کا ہے: ادنی ، اوسط ، اعلیٰ ۔ ادنی تو یہ ہے کہ یہ تین کپڑے سوتی ہوں۔ اوسط یہ کہ ٹر کے ہوں ۔ ٹسر ایک کپڑا جو ریشم سے کمتر ہے اور سوت سے اچھا ہے۔ اور اعلیٰ درجہ کا متعہ یہ ہے کہ یہ تین کپڑے ریشم کے ہوں۔ پھر صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ متعہ میں عورت کا حال معتبر ہو یا مرد کا نصف مہر مثل سے زائد اور پانچ درہم سے کم نہ ہونا چاہئے ۔ نصف مہر مثل سے زائد تو اس لئے نہیں ہو گا کہ مہر سمی اقومی ہے مہر مثل سے، کیونکہ مہر مسمی کا وجوب عقد اور تسمیہ سے ہوا ہے اور مہر مثل کا وجوب فقط عقد سے ہوا ہے۔ اب اگر ایسے نکاح میں مہرتی ہر جس میں تسمیہ پایا گیا طلاق قبل الدخول دے دی تو نصف مسمی پر زیادتی نہیں ہوگی۔ پس ایسا نکاح جس میں تسمیہ نہیں پایا گیا نصف مہر مثل پر بدرجہ اولی زیادتی نہ ہونی چاہئے ۔ اور پانچ درہم سے کم اس لئے نہ ہو کہ متعہ واجب ہوا بضع کا عوض بن کر اور کوئی عوض دس درہم سے کم نہیں ہوتا۔ لہذ انصف عوض پانچ سے کم نہ ہونا چاہئے ۔
Ashraf al-Bidaya Urdu commentary of Hidaya volume 4, Book of Nikah. Explanation: The author mentioned two scenarios: first, marriage was performed and silence was observed regarding mahr – neither mentioned nor negated; second, marriage was performed and a condition of no mahr was stipulated. In both scenarios, according to us, mahr al-mithl is obligatory provided that the husband consummated the marriage or the husband died. Imam al-Shafi'i says: in case of death before consummation, nothing is obligatory upon the husband. And most Shafi'is say: in case of consummation, mahr al-mithl is obligatory, as is our madhhab. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that mahr is exclusively the woman's right; just as she has the power to drop it at the end, similarly she has the power to negate it at the beginning. Imam al-Shafi'i also argues with a hadith narrated from 'Ali, Zayd ibn Thabit, Ibn 'Abbas, and Ibn 'Umar: 'They said: She has inheritance and no dower for her, and she must observe the waiting period.' That is, this woman has inheritance and no mahr, and she must observe 'iddah. Our proof is that mahr is a right established by Sharī'ah, due to the verses 'that you may seek them with your wealth' and 'We have known what We have prescribed'. Details of both verses are in books of Usul al-Fiqh. Some have said that mahr involves three rights: (1) the right of Sharī'ah – that it should not be less than ten dirhams; (2) the right of the guardians – that mahr should not be less than a certain amount; (3) the woman's right – that mahr is her property. However, the right of Sharī'ah and the right of guardians are only valid at the time of marriage, whereas the woman's right persists. Hence the woman can drop it at the end but cannot negate it at the beginning. So Imam al-Shafi'i's saying that she is capable of negating at the beginning is a transgression of her right, which is not permitted by Sharī'ah. And if this woman is divorced before consummation, then mut'ah is obligatory for her. The proof is the verse: 'There is no sin upon you if you divorce women while you have not yet touched them nor specified for them an obligation, but provide for them.' In the verse, 'aw' means 'waw', i.e., you have no sin if you have divorced women before you have touched them and not fixed a mahr for them, but give them mut'ah. There is difference of opinion on the obligation or non-obligation of mut'ah. Imam Malik holds it as recommended, while the Hanafis hold it as obligatory. Imam Malik's proof is that in the Qur'an, the one who gives mut'ah is called 'muhsin', and 'muhsin' refers to a volunteer, i.e., one who does supererogatory acts. Our proof and reply to Imam Malik is that 'amti'ū' is a command form which indicates obligation, second the word 'haqqan' also indicates obligation, third the word 'alā' which indicates compulsion. As for the word 'muhsin', it means those who perform the obligatory and do extra as beneficence. Therefore, the word 'muhsinīn' cannot be used as proof by Imam Malik. Mut'ah is three garments: 'And mut'ah is three garments from clothing similar to hers, and they are a chemise, a headcover, and a wrap. This estimation is narrated from 'A'isha and Ibn 'Abbas. His statement 'from clothing similar to hers' indicates that her status is considered. This is the saying of al-Karkhi concerning obligatory mut'ah because it stands in place of mahr al-mithl. The correct view is that his (husband's) status is considered, acting upon the text: the saying of Allah Most High: 'Upon the wealthy in accordance with his means and upon the straitened in accordance with his means.' Then it (mut'ah) does not exceed half of her mahr al-mithl and is not less than five dirhams. This is known in al-Asl. Explanation: The reality of mut'ah is that it is three garments: a chemise, a headcover, and a wrap. This specification and estimation is transmitted from 'A'isha and Ibn 'Abbas. The statement of al-Quduri 'from clothing similar to hers' indicates that in mut'ah, the woman's status is considered. This is the saying of Imam al-Karkhi regarding obligatory mut'ah. The proof is that mut'ah stands in the place of mahr al-mithl, and in mahr al-mithl, the woman's status is considered; therefore, its replacement also considers the woman's status. The correct saying is that the man's status is considered. Their proof is the verse 'Upon the wealthy...' Allah considered the man's status, not the woman's. Mut'ah is three types: lowest, middle, highest. The lowest is that these three garments are cotton. The middle is that they are of a cloth called 'tassar', which is inferior to silk and better than cotton. The highest grade is that these three garments are silk. Then the author of al-Hidayah says: whether the woman's status or the man's status is considered, mut'ah should not exceed half of mahr al-mithl and should not be less than five dirhams. It does not exceed half of mahr al-mithl because mahr al-musamma is analogous to mahr al-mithl; because wajub of mahr al-musamma is through the contract and specification, while wajub of mahr al-mithl is through the contract alone. Now if in a marriage where specification existed, divorce before consummation is given, there will be no excess over half of the specified mahr. So in a marriage where specification is not present, there should, with greater reason, be no excess over half of mahr al-mithl. And it is not less than five dirhams because mut'ah is wajib as a substitute for the vulva, and no substitute is less than ten dirhams; hence half of the substitute should not be less than five.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute and ruling statement. The author, commenting on al-Hidayah, presents two scenarios where no mahr was specified or it was negated. According to the Hanafi school, in both cases mahr al-mithl (the mahr appropriate for a woman of her status) becomes wajib if consummation occurs or the husband dies. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees in case of death before consummation, arguing that the woman can forgo her right even initially. He also cites a hadith. The Hanafi response distinguishes between three rights in mahr: the right of Sharī'ah (minimum 10 dirhams), right of guardians (to ensure dignity), and the woman's right. The woman can only drop her right after it is established, not before. Thus the initial negation is invalid. The passage then discusses mut'ah (consolatory gift) given to a woman divorced before consummation when no mahr was specified. Hanafis hold mut'ah as wajib, based on the imperative 'amti'ū' and the words 'haqqan' and 'alā'. Imam Malik views it as mustahabb. The correct opinion in the Hanafi school is that the husband's financial status is considered, not the woman's, as per the verse. Mut'ah consists of three garments (chemise, headcover, wrap) and must be between half of mahr al-mithl and five dirhams.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The mahr appropriate for a woman of similar status (family, beauty, etc.) as determined by custom.
متعہ (mut'ah): A consolatory gift given to a woman divorced before consummation when no mahr was specified.
صداق (sadaq): Synonym for mahr (dower).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum amount of mut'ah?
A) 5 dirhams
B) 10 dirhams
C) Half of mahr al-mithl
D) Three garments only, no monetary minimum

Key Takeaway
Mahr is a Sharī'ah and guardians' right that cannot be negated by the wife at the outset; mut'ah is wajib upon divorce before consummation when no mahr is specified, and its amount is based on the husband's status, between half of mahr al-mithl and five dirhams.

Post-Nuptial Mahr Agreement: Halving or Mut'ah?
Rules on mahr when spouses later agree on a mahr after marriage without initial specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi majority view from Abu Yusuf's first opinion on halving a post-nuptially agreed mahr and apply the rule that such an agreement is a determination of mahr al-mithl.

Core Idea
A post-nuptial mahr is a determination of mahr al-mithl, not a fresh stipulation, so it is not halved.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario: a marriage was contracted without specifying a mahr, and later the spouses agree on a mahr. If the husband divorces before consummation, a dispute arises: does the wife get half of the agreed mahr or only mut'ah? The Hanafi majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold that it is not halved, while Abu Yusuf's first opinion (and al-Shafi'i) holds that it is. We will examine the proofs and the basis of this disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and two outcomes
Recognize the two sub-scenarios: if consummation or death occurs, the full agreed mahr is due; if divorce before consummation, the dispute arises over what is due.
Consummation or death makes the full mahr wajib under all views.
2
State the dispute on divorce before consummation
The majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad) says only mut'ah is due. Abu Yusuf's first opinion (and al-Shafi'i) says half of the agreed mahr is due.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the amount the wife receives.
3
Analyze the majority's proof
The post-nuptial agreement is a determination of mahr al-mithl, which is not halved. The verse on halving (Quran 2:237) applies only to mahr stipulated at the contract, not to later determinations.
The analogy (qiyas) is to mahr al-mithl, which by definition is not halved.
4
Analyze the opposing proof and Hanafi response
Abu Yusuf and Shafi'i argue that the agreed mahr is a 'mafrud' (stipulated) and thus falls under the general rule of halving. The Hanafi response distinguishes: the verse refers to 'mafrud' in the contract, not a later determination.
The key is the timing of the stipulation: at contract vs post-nuptial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مہر کے بغیر نکاح کیا پھر باہمی رضامندی سے مہر مقرر کیا تو عورت کیلئے یہ مہر کب ہوگا ؟ وان تزوجها ولم يسم لهامهر اثم تراضيا على تسميته فهى لها ان دخل بها اومات عنها وان طلقها قبل الدخول بها فلها المتعة وعلى قول ابى يوسف الاول نصف هذا المفروض وهو قول الشافعي لانه مفروض فيتنصف بالنص ولنا ان هذا الفرض تعيين للواجب بالعقد وهو مهرالمثل وذلك لا يتنصف فكذا مانزل منزلته والمراد بما تلا الفرض فى العقد اذ هو الفرض المتعارف ترجمہ اور اگر نکاح کیا عورت سے اور اس کیلئے مہر ذکر نہیں کیا۔ پھر دونوں رضامند ہو گئے ( اس مہر) کے تسمیہ پر تو یہ متعین کردہ مقدار اس کیلئے ہوگی۔ اگر اس کے ساتھ دخول کیا یا اس کو چھوڑ کر مر گیا۔ اور اگر اس کو طلاق قبل الدخول دی تو اس کیلئے متعہ ہوگا۔ اور ابو یوسف کے قول اول پر اس مفروض کا نصف ہوگا ۔ اور یہ قول امام شافعی کا بھی ہے اسلئے کہ یہ مفروض ہے پس تنصیف ہوگی نص سے ۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ فرض متعین کرنا ہے اس کا جو واجب ہوا عقد کی وجہ سے۔ اور وہ مہر شل ہے۔ اور مہر مثل کی تنصیف نہیں ہوتی ۔ پس ایسے ہی اس کی بھی جو اس کے مرتبہ میں اتار لیا گیا اور مراد اس سے جو تلاوت کیا ابو یوسف نے فرض فی العقد ہے۔ اسلئے کہ وہ فرض متعارف ہے۔
If a man married a woman without specifying a mahr for her, then they mutually agreed on specifying it (a mahr), then this (specified amount) is for her if he consummated with her or died. And if he divorced her before consummation, then for her is mut'ah. According to the first saying of Abu Yusuf, half of this stipulated (mahr) (is due), and this is the saying of al-Shafi'i, because it is a stipulated (mahr) and thus it is halved by the text. And our proof is that this stipulation is a determination of what became wajib by the contract, and that is mahr al-mithl, and that (mahr al-mithl) is not halved. So likewise what is placed in its position (i.e., this post-nuptial stipulation). And the meaning of what Abu Yusuf recited [؟] is 'the stipulated (mahr) in the contract', because it is the commonly known stipulation. Translation: And if a man married a woman and did not mention a mahr for her, then both agreed on specifying (a mahr), then this specified amount will be for her if he consummated or died. And if he divorced her before consummation, then for her is mut'ah. And according to the first saying of Abu Yusuf, half of this specified (mahr) will be due. And this is also the saying of Imam al-Shafi'i, because it is specified, so it is halved by the text. And our proof is that this specification is a determination of what became wajib by the contract, and that is mahr al-mithl, and mahr al-mithl is not halved. So likewise whatever is placed in its position. And the meaning of what Abu Yusuf recited (i.e., the verse or text) is 'the stipulated (mahr) in the contract', because it is the commonly known stipulation.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and a ruling statement. It addresses the scenario where a marriage was contracted without specifying a mahr, and later the spouses mutually agree on a specific mahr amount. According to the majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani), if the husband consummates the marriage or dies, the agreed mahr becomes due in full. If he divorces before consummation, the wife is entitled only to mut'ah (consolatory gift), not half of the agreed mahr. Abu Yusuf's first opinion (also held by al-Shafi'i) is that if divorce occurs before consummation, the wife gets half of the stipulated mahr, just like in a normal marriage with specified mahr, because it is a 'mafrud' (stipulated amount) and the Qur'an says half of what is stipulated. The Hanafi majority respond that this post-nuptial agreement is not an independent stipulation; it is merely a determination of what was already wajib by the contract, i.e., mahr al-mithl. Since mahr al-mithl is not halved by divorce before consummation (because it is based on status, not agreement), this determination also should not be halved. They argue that the 'mafrud' referred to in the verse is the mahr stipulated at the time of the contract, not a later agreement.

Key Terms
مفروض (mafrud): A stipulated/agreed mahr, whether at the time of marriage or later.
تسمیہ (tasmiyah): The act of specifying/naming a mahr.
متعہ (mut'ah): Consolatory gift for divorced woman without mahr specification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, what does a woman get if she is divorced before consummation after a post-nuptial agreement on mahr?
A) Half of the agreed mahr
B) The full agreed mahr
C) Mut'ah only
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
A post-nuptial mahr agreement is treated as a determination of mahr al-mithl, not a fresh stipulation, so it is not halved upon divorce before consummation; only mut'ah is due.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Mut'ah: Definition, Amount, and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Defines mut'ah and rules on its amount based on husband's status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of mut'ah, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whose status is considered, and apply the limits of half mahr al-mithl and five dirhams.

Core Idea
Mut'ah is wajib; amount based on husband's means, max half mahr al-mithl, min five dirhams.

This lesson focuses on mut'ah, the consolatory gift given to a woman divorced before consummation when no dower was specified. The Hanafi school considers it wajib, but there is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the husband's or the wife's status determines the amount. The text resolves this using the Quranic verse and sets clear upper and lower limits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what mut'ah is and when it is wajib: a gift given to a woman divorced before consummation when no mahr was specified in the marriage contract. The ruling is wajib in the Hanafi school.
Mut'ah is not temporary marriage; it is post-divorce compensation.
2
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute
Two views: Imam al-Karakhi says the wife's status (based on qiyas to mahr al-mithl), and the relied-upon view says the husband's status (based on the Quranic verse). Understand the reasoning behind each.
The author declares the husband's status as 'sahih' (correct).
3
Locate the dalil and its wajh al-dalalah
The Quranic verse (2:236) 'upon the wealthy according to his means and upon the poor according to his means' is the proof. It directly ties the gift to the husband's ability, not the wife's status. This nass overrides the qiyas.
The verse is zanni in dalala because it implies the criterion indirectly, but it is qati' in thubut.
4
Determine the limits: maximum and minimum
Maximum: half of mahr al-mithl. This is because if mahr were specified, the maximum given upon pre-consummation divorce is half of that specified amount; so by analogy, when no mahr is specified, it should not exceed half of what would have been specified (mahr al-mithl). Minimum: five dirhams, because the entire substitute (badal al-bud') is ten dirhams, so half is five.
These limits apply regardless of which status is considered.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a man of moderate means divorcing before consummation with no mahr specified, and the wife's mahr al-mithl is known, determine the mut'ah range. Use the husband's financial ability within the limits.
Practice applying the two limits to ensure correct calculation.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم کتاب النکاح عائشہ اور ( حضرت ) ابن عباس سے۔ اور قدوری کا قول " من کسوۃ مثلھا اشارہ ہے اس طرف کہ اعتبار کیا جائیگا عورت کے حال کا اور وہ قول ہے امام کرخی کا متعہ واجبہ میں متعہ کے قائم مقام ہونے کی وجہ سے مہر مثل کے۔ اور صحیح یہ ہے کہ اعتبار کیا جائے گا مرد کے حال کا عمل کرتے ہوئے نص پر اور وہ قول ہے باری تعالیٰ کا " علی الموسع قدره وعلی المقتر قدرہ پھر یہ متعہ نہ زیادہ کیا جائے گا نصف مہر مثل پر اور نہ پانچ درہم سے کم ہوگا اور یہ مسئلہ معلوم ہو گا مبسوط میں ۔
تشریح متعہ کی حقیقت یہ ہے کہ وہ تین کپڑے ہیں کرتہ، اوڑھنی ، چادر۔ یہ تین کپڑوں کی تعیین و تقدیر حضرت عائشہ اور ابن عباس رضی اللہ عنہما سے منقول ہے۔ صاحب قدوری کی عبارت " من كسوة مثلها “ سے اشارہ اس طرف ہے کہ متعہ میں عورت کے حال کا اعتبار ہوگا ۔ متعہ واجبہ میں امام کرختی کا یہی قول ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ متعہ مہر مثل کے قائم مقام ہے اور مہر مثل میں عورتوں کا حال معتبر ہے، لہذا جو اس کا قائم مقام ہے اس میں بھی عورت ہی کے حال کا اعتبار ہوگا ۔ اور صحیح قول یہ ہے کہ مرد کے حال کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ ان کی دلیل قرآن کی آیت ”على الموسع قدره وعلى المقتر قدرہ“ اللہ تعالیٰ نے مرد کے حال کا اعتبار کیا نہ کہ عورت کے حال کا ۔ متعہ تین طرح کا ہے: ادنی ، اوسط ، اعلیٰ ۔ ادنی تو یہ ہے کہ یہ تین کپڑے سوتی ہوں۔ اوسط یہ کہ ٹر کے ہوں ۔ ٹسر ایک کپڑا جو ریشم سے کمتر ہے اور سوت سے اچھا ہے۔ اور اعلیٰ درجہ کا متعہ یہ ہے کہ یہ تین کپڑے ریشم کے ہوں۔ پھر صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ متعہ میں عورت کا حال معتبر ہو یا مرد کا نصف مہر مثل سے زائد اور پانچ درہم سے کم نہ ہونا چاہئے ۔ نصف مہر مثل سے زائد تو اس لئے نہیں ہو گا کہ مہر سمی اقومی ہے مہر مثل سے، کیونکہ مہر مسمی کا وجوب عقد اور تسمیہ سے ہوا ہے اور مہر مثل کا وجوب فقط عقد سے ہوا ہے۔ اب اگر ایسے نکاح میں مہرتی ہر جس میں تسمیہ پایا گیا طلاق قبل الدخول دے دی تو نصف مسمی پر زیادتی نہیں ہوگی۔ پس ایسا نکاح جس میں تسمیہ نہیں پایا گیا نصف مہر مثل پر بدرجہ اولی زیادتی نہ ہونی چاہئے ۔ اور پانچ درہم سے کم اس لئے نہ ہو کہ متعہ واجب ہوا بضع کا عوض بن کر اور کوئی عوض دس درہم سے کم نہیں ہوتا۔ لہذ انصف عوض پانچ سے کم نہ ہونا چاہئے ۔
From Ashraf al-Bidaya, Urdu commentary on Hidayah, Volume 4, Kitab al-Nikah. (Narrated) from Aisha and (Hadrat) Ibn Abbas. And al-Quduri's statement 'from clothing like hers' indicates that consideration is given to the condition of the woman. And that is the statement of Imam al-Karakhi in obligatory mut'ah because mut'ah stands in place of mahr al-mithl. And the correct (view) is that consideration will be given to the condition of the man, acting upon the text, and that is the statement of Allah Most High: 'Upon the wealthy according to his means and upon the poor according to his means.' Then this mut'ah will neither exceed half of mahr al-mithl nor be less than five dirhams. And this issue will be known in al-Mabsut.
Explanation: The reality of mut'ah is that it consists of three garments: a shirt (kurta), a head-covering (odhni), and a wrapper (chadar). This determination and specification of three garments is transmitted from Hadrat Aisha and Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them). The phrase of al-Quduri 'from clothing like hers' indicates that in mut'ah the condition of the woman is considered. This is the statement of Imam al-Karakhi in wajib mut'ah. The proof is that mut'ah stands in place of mahr al-mithl, and in mahr al-mithl the condition of women is considered; therefore what stands in its place (i.e., mut'ah) will also consider the condition of the woman. And the correct statement is that the condition of the man will be considered. Their proof is the Quranic verse 'Upon the wealthy according to his means and upon the poor according to his means.' Allah Most High considered the condition of the man, not the condition of the woman. Mut'ah is of three types: low (adna), middle (awsat), high (a'la). Low is that these three garments are cotton. Middle is that they are of tasar (a type of silk-blend). Tasar is a cloth lower than silk and better than cotton. And high-grade mut'ah is that these three garments are silk. Then the author of al-Hidayah says: In mut'ah, whether the condition of the woman is considered or that of the man, it should not exceed half of mahr al-mithl and should not be less than five dirhams. It should not exceed half of mahr al-mithl because mahr al-musamma (specified dower) is superior to mahr al-mithl, because the obligation of mahr al-musamma arises from the contract and specification, while the obligation of mahr al-mithl arises from the contract alone. Now if in a marriage where specification occurred, talaq before consummation is given, there is no excess over half of the specified amount. Therefore a marriage where no specification occurred should, a fortiori, not have excess over half of mahr al-mithl. And it should not be less than five dirhams because mut'ah is wajib as a substitute for the bridal due (badal al-bud'), and no substitute is less than ten dirhams. Hence half of the substitute should not be less than five.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling regarding mut'ah, the consolatory gift given to a woman divorced before consummation when no mahr was specified in the marriage contract. The author first quotes a difference of opinion: Imam al-Karakhi considers the woman's status (her social standing) based on Quduri's phrase 'from clothing like hers,' analogizing to mahr al-mithl. But the correct view, supported by the Quranic verse, is that the man's financial capacity is considered. The verse 'upon the wealthy according to his means and upon the poor according to his means' directly addresses the man's ability. Then mut'ah is defined as three specific garments (kurta, odhni, chadar) with three quality levels: cotton, tasar (a medium fabric), and silk. The maximum amount is half of the woman's mahr al-mithl, because mahr al-musamma takes precedence and even in cases where mahr was specified, the maximum given is half of that. If no specification existed, it is a fortiori not to exceed half of mahr al-mithl. The minimum is five dirhams, as the full substitute (mahr) for the act of marriage is at least ten dirhams, so half is five. These limits ensure fairness.

Key Terms
متعہ (mut'ah): A consolatory gift given to a woman divorced before consummation when no mahr was specified.
مہر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The standard dower for a woman of similar family and status in her locality.
مہر مسمی (mahr al-musamma): The dower explicitly agreed upon in the marriage contract.

Mut'ah is wajib for pre-consummation divorce without specified mahr; amount based on husband's means but capped at half the woman's mahr al-mithl and floored at five dirhams.

Post-Contract Mahr Agreement and Talaq Before Consummation
Dispute on whether a post-contract mahr agreement is halved in talaq before consummation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rules that a post-contract mahr agreement is not halved in talaq before consummation, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A post-contract mahr agreement determines mahr al-mithl, not a new specification, so it is not halved in talaq before consummation.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario: a marriage contracted without mahr, followed by a mutual agreement on an amount, and then talaq before consummation. The Hanafi school distinguishes between mahr specified at the contract and later determination, leading to different rulings on whether the wife gets half or mut'ah. Understanding this distinction is key to correctly applying the Quranic verse on halving.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and legal issue
Recognize that the marriage was contracted without mahr, then a mutual agreement on mahr occurred, followed by talaq before consummation. The issue is whether the wife is entitled to half of the agreed amount or mut'ah.
2
State the Hanafi position and its basis
The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that the wife gets mut'ah, not half. Their basis: the post-contract agreement is a determination (ta'yin) of the mahr al-mithl that became wajib by the contract, and mahr al-mithl is not halved.
3
State the opposing position and its proof
Abu Yusuf (first opinion) and al-Shafi'i hold that the wife gets half of the agreed amount. Their proof: the Quranic verse 'half of what you specified' applies to any specification, whether at contract or later.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes: the verse's 'specification' (fard) refers to the customary practice at the time of contract, not post-contract. Post-contract agreement is a determination of an existing obligation, not a fresh specification.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under the opposing view, wife gets half the agreed sum (e.g., 5,000 if 10,000 was agreed). Under Hanafi, she gets mut'ah (valued between 5 dirhams and half mahr al-mithl).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وان تزوجها ولم يسم لهامهر اثم تراضيا على تسميته فهى لها ان دخل بها اومات عنها وان طلقها قبل الدخول بها فلها المتعة وعلى قول ابى يوسف الاول نصف هذا المفروض وهو قول الشافعي لانه مفروض فيتنصف بالنص ولنا ان هذا الفرض تعيين للواجب بالعقد وهو مهرالمثل وذلك لا يتنصف فكذا مانزل منزلته والمراد بما تلا الفرض فى العقد اذ هو الفرض المتعارف
ترجمہ اور اگر نکاح کیا عورت سے اور اس کیلئے مہر ذکر نہیں کیا۔ پھر دونوں رضامند ہو گئے ( اس مہر) کے تسمیہ پر تو یہ متعین کردہ مقدار اس کیلئے ہوگی۔ اگر اس کے ساتھ دخول کیا یا اس کو چھوڑ کر مر گیا۔ اور اگر اس کو طلاق قبل الدخول دی تو اس کیلئے متعہ ہوگا۔ اور ابو یوسف کے قول اول پر اس مفروض کا نصف ہوگا ۔ اور یہ قول امام شافعی کا بھی ہے اسلئے کہ یہ مفروض ہے پس تنصیف ہوگی نص سے ۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ فرض متعین کرنا ہے اس کا جو واجب ہوا عقد کی وجہ سے۔ اور وہ مہر شل ہے۔ اور مہر مثل کی تنصیف نہیں ہوتی ۔ پس ایسے ہی اس کی بھی جو اس کے مرتبہ میں اتار لیا گیا اور مراد اس سے جو تلاوت کیا ابو یوسف نے فرض فی العقد ہے۔ اسلئے کہ وہ فرض متعارف ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ نکاح کے وقت مہر ذکر نہیں کیا پھر دونوں شوہر بیوی نے ایک مقدار مقرر کر لی تو اب اگر شوہر نے بیوی کے ساتھ دخول کیا یا مر گیا تو دونوں صورتوں میں یہ متعین کردہ مقدار واجب ہوگی۔ اور اگر طلاق قبل الدخول ہے تو طرفین کے نزدیک عورت کیلئے متعہ واجب ہوگا ۔ اور ابو یوسف کا قول اول یہ ہے کہ اس متعین کردہ مقدار کا نصف واجب ہوگا ۔ اور یہی قول امام شافعی کا ہے۔ ابو یوسف کا دوسرا قول طرفین کے ساتھ ہے۔ امام شافعی اور ابو یوسف کے قول اول کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ زوجین نے باہمی اتفاق سے جو مقدار مقرر کی ہے یہ مفروض ( مقدور و معین) ہے۔ اور آیت فنصف ما فرضتم سے مفروض کی تنصیف ثابت ہے۔ مفروض فی حالت العقد ہو یا مفروض بعد العقد ۔ لہذا اس صورت میں بھی اگر طلاق قبل الدخول پائی گئی تو نصف مفروض واجب ہوگا متعہ واجب نہیں ہوگا۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ عقد نکاح کے وقت اگر مہر ذکر نہ کیا جائے تو مہر مثل واجب ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس اس صورت میں بھی نکاح کے وقت مہر یذکور نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے مہر مثل واجب ہو گیا۔ بعد میں زوجین نے ایک مقدار پر اتفاق کر لیا تو یہ بعد میں متعین کردہ مقدار در حقیقت تعیین ہے اس کی جو عقد کی وجہ سے واجب ہوا تھا اور عقد کی وجہ سے مہر مثل واجب ہوا تھا۔ اور مہر مثل کی تنصیف نہیں ہوتی ۔ لہذا جو اس کے مرتبہ میں ہے اس کی بھی تنصیف نہیں ہوگی۔ حاصل دلیل یہ کہ مفروض بعد العقد تعیین ہے مہر مثل کی اور مہر مثل کی تنصیف نہیں ہوتی ہے لہذا جو ا سکے قائم مقام ہے یعنی مفروض بعد العقد اسکی بھی تنصیف نہیں ہوگی۔ اور جب تنصیف نہیں ہوسکتی تو متعہ واجب ہوگا۔ اور ابو یوسف نے جو آیت تلاوت کی یعنی فنصف ما فرضتم تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ آیت میں فرض فی العقد مراد ہے نہ کہ فرض بعد العقد ۔ اور وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ آیت مطلق ہے اور مطلق بولا جاتا ہے تو اس سے متعارف مراد ہوتا ہے اور متعارف مفروض فی العقد ہے نہ کہ مفروض بعد العقد ۔ پس مفروض فی العقد کی تنصیف ہوگی مفروض بعد العقد کی نہیں۔
If he married her without specifying a mahr for her, then they mutually agree on specifying it, then it (the specified amount) is for her if he has consummated with her or died. And if he divorced her before consummation, then she gets mut'ah. According to the first opinion of Abu Yusuf, half of this specified (amount) is due, and it is the opinion of al-Shafi'i because it is a specified (mufarrad) amount, so it is halved by the text (Quran). And our proof is that this specification is a determination of what became obligatory by the contract, which is mahr al-mithl, and that (mahr al-mithl) is not halved; so likewise what is placed in its position. And what Abu Yusuf recited (the verse) refers to specification in the contract, because that is the customary specification.
Translation: ...
Explanation: The scenario is that at the time of marriage no mahr was mentioned, then both husband and wife agreed on an amount. Now if the husband consummated or died, in both cases this specified amount becomes wajib. And if talaq before consummation occurs, according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) mut'ah is wajib for the woman. And Abu Yusuf's first opinion is that half of this specified amount is wajib, and this is also the opinion of Imam al-Shafi'i. Abu Yusuf's second opinion aligns with the two. The proof of Imam al-Shafi'i and Abu Yusuf's first opinion is that the amount mutually agreed upon is a specified (mufarrad) amount, and the verse 'half of what you specified' establishes halving of a specified amount, whether the specification occurred at the time of contract or after the contract. Therefore in this case, if talaq before consummation occurs, half of the specified amount is wajib, not mut'ah.
Our proof is that if at the time of marriage no mahr is mentioned, then mahr al-mithl becomes wajib. So in this case too, due to not mentioning mahr at the time of marriage, mahr al-mithl became wajib. Later the couple agreed on an amount; this later specified amount is in reality a determination of what became wajib by the contract, and that was mahr al-mithl. And mahr al-mithl is not halved. Therefore what is in its position (i.e., the later specification) is also not halved. The conclusion is that the post-contract specification is a determination of mahr al-mithl, and mahr al-mithl is not halved; hence what stands in its place, i.e., the post-contract specification, is also not halved. And when it cannot be halved, then mut'ah becomes wajib. As for the verse recited by Abu Yusuf, i.e., 'half of what you specified', the answer is that the verse refers to specification in the contract, not specification after the contract. The reason is that the verse is absolute (mutlaq), and when an absolute expression is used, the customary meaning is intended, and the customary specification is that at the time of the contract, not post-contract. So the specification in the contract is halved, not the post-contract specification.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage deals with a scenario where a marriage is contracted without specifying a mahr, and later the spouses mutually agree on a specific mahr amount. The Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad) is that this later agreement is considered a determination (ta'yin) of the mahr al-mithl that automatically became wajib by the contract. Since mahr al-mithl is not halved in case of talaq before consummation (because it was not explicitly specified at the time of contract), this determination also is not halved. Therefore, if talaq occurs before consummation, the wife is entitled to mut'ah (a consolatory gift), not half of the agreed amount. Abu Yusuf (in his first opinion) and Imam al-Shafi'i argue that the agreed amount is a new specified dower (mufarrad) at the time of agreement, and the Quranic verse 'half of what you specified' applies to any specification regardless of when it occurs, so half is due. The Hanafi response distinguishes: the verse refers to the customary specification, which is at the time of the contract. The post-contract agreement is a determination of an already existing obligation (mahr al-mithl), not a fresh specification. The practical difference: the wife gets mut'ah (between 5 dirhams and half mahr al-mithl) rather than half the agreed amount (which could be larger or smaller). The relied-upon position is the Hanafi one, as indicated by the text.

Key Terms
مفروض (mufarrad): A specified amount of mahr agreed upon by the spouses, either at the time of contract or later.
تنصیف (tansif): Halving of the mahr when talaq occurs before consummation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if a couple marries without specifying mahr and later agrees on a sum, then divorces before consummation, the wife is entitled to:
A) Half of the agreed sum
B) The full agreed sum
C) Mut'ah
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
A post-contract mahr agreement is a determination of mahr al-mithl, not a fresh specification; hence it is not halved in talaq before consummation under Hanafi fiqh.

Increase and Decrease in Mahr After the Marriage Contract
Rulings on post-contract mahr modifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on post-contract increase in mahr, distinguish between the majority view and Abu Yusuf's first opinion regarding its fate in talaq before consummation, and explain the validity of the wife's reduction of her mahr.

Core Idea
A voluntary increase in mahr after the contract is binding, but cancelled by talaq before consummation, while the wife's reduction is always valid.

This passage from a Hanafi fiqh text addresses three important rulings regarding modifications to the mahr after the marriage contract. First, if the husband voluntarily increases the mahr after the contract is concluded, that increase is binding upon him, contrary to the view of Imam Zufar. Second, if talaq occurs before consummation, the increase is cancelled entirely, though Abu Yusuf's first opinion holds it is halved. Third, if the wife voluntarily reduces or forgives part of her mahr, that reduction is valid and effective because the mahr is her exclusive right. These rulings illustrate how the Hanafi school treats post-contract changes in mahr distinctly from the original obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings in the passage
Read the Arabic passage and list the three distinct rulings it covers: (1) increase in mahr after contract, (2) fate of that increase in talaq before consummation, (3) reduction of mahr by the wife.
These rulings are all modifications of the mahr after the nikah contract.
2
Analyze the ruling on increase
Note that the increase is binding (lazim) upon the husband, contrary to Imam Zufar's view. The text refers to an analogy with increase in price in a sale (to be mentioned later).
The binding nature is immediate upon acceptance by the wife.
3
Examine the fate of the increase in talaq before consummation
The basic ruling is that a valid increase is cancelled by talaq before consummation. However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold it falls entirely, while Abu Yusuf's first opinion holds it is halved along with the original mahr.
The text uses the phrase 'tasqut' (falls/cancelled) and then contrasts Abu Yusuf's view.
4
Understand the wife's reduction
The passage states that if the wife reduces from her mahr (i.e., forgives part of it), the reduction is valid and binding. The reason given is that the mahr is her right, and she may waive it during the continuance of the marriage.
This is a straightforward application of the principle that a right-holder can waive their right.
5
Summarize the inter- and intra-madhhab differences
Imam Zufar (outside the Hanafi school) holds that the increase is not binding. Within the Hanafi school, Abu Yusuf's first opinion differs from the majority on the treatment of the increase in talaq before consummation. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the majority view: the increase is binding and cancelled entirely.
These differences have practical consequences for how much is owed after divorce.

Source Text

If he increases (her mahr) after the contract, the increase is binding upon him, contrary to Zufar. And we will mention it in the section on increase in price and the priced item, if Allah wills. And when the increase is valid, it falls (i.e., is cancelled) by talaq before consummation. And according to the first opinion of Abu Yusuf, it is halved along with the original, because half, according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), is specific to what was specified in the contract. And according to him (Abu Yusuf), the post-contract specification is like the specification in the contract as passed. And if she reduces from her mahr (i.e., forgives part of it), the reduction is valid, because the mahr is her right, and the reduction meets it in a state of survival (during the marriage).
Explanation: After the marriage contract, if the husband adds to the agreed mahr and the woman accepts in that same session, then according to us (the Hanafis) it is binding upon the husband...

Commentary
This passage covers three rulings regarding mahr after the marriage contract. First: if the husband voluntarily increases the mahr after the contract, that increase is binding (lazim) on him, contrary to Imam Zufar who argued it is not binding. This is analogous to increasing the price in a sale. Second: if talaq before consummation occurs, this increase is cancelled (falls) because it is treated like a gift that is not yet completed. However, Abu Yusuf's first opinion holds that the increase is halved along with the original mahr, because he considers post-contract specification as equivalent to contract-time specification. Third: if the wife voluntarily reduces or forgives part of her mahr, that reduction is valid and binding because the mahr is her exclusive right and she may waive it during the marriage. The passage ends mid-commentary on the conditions of increase acceptance, likely continuing on the next page. The relied-upon position is that the increase is binding and is cancelled entirely in talaq before consummation, not halved.

Key Terms
زیادتی (ziyada): An increase in the mahr amount voluntarily given by the husband after the marriage contract.
حط (hatt): A reduction or forgiveness of part of the mahr by the wife, which is valid and effective immediately.

A husband's voluntary increase in mahr after the contract is binding, but it is entirely cancelled by talaq before consummation, while any reduction by the wife is valid and effective immediately.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
