Post-Marriage Mahr Agreement: Half or Mut'ah?
Dispute on effect of post-marriage mahr agreement with divorce before consummation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on mahr agreed after marriage and distinguish it from the Shafi'i view, stating the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
The later fixing of mahr is a determination of mahr al-mithl, which is never halved – only mut'ah is given.

When mahr is not specified at the marriage contract but is later agreed upon, and divorce occurs before consummation, a critical dispute arises: should the wife receive half of the agreed amount or a gift (mut'ah)? This lesson examines the Hanafi position (supported by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) against the Shafi'i position (and Abu Yusuf's first opinion), analyzing their proofs and the underlying usul principles. By the end, you will understand why the Hanafi mufta bihi rules mut'ah, not half.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): the wife is entitled to mut'ah, not half of the agreed amount.
The later-fixed amount is a determination of mahr al-mithl.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
State the positions of Imam al-Shafi'i and Abu Yusuf's first opinion: they hold that half of the agreed amount is due.
They consider the later agreement as an independent fixing (mafrud).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the opponent's dalil: Quran 2:237 (fa-nisfu ma faradtum) applied to any mafrud, regardless of timing.
The verse seems general: 'half of what you fixed'.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal: the verse's 'faradtum' conventionally means fixing at the time of contract, not after. Also, the later agreement is a determination of mahr al-mithl, which is not halved.
The Hanafis distinguish between mafrud fi al-aqd and mafrud ba'd al-aqd.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: in the given scenario, the wife receives mut'ah under Hanafi law, but half the agreed amount under Shafi'i law.
Abu Yusuf later reverted to the Sahibayn's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ نکاح کے وقت مہر ذکر نہیں کیا پھر دونوں شوہر بیوی نے ایک مقدار مقرر کر لی تو اب اگر شوہر نے بیوی کے ساتھ دخول کیا یا مر گیا تو دونوں صورتوں میں یہ متعین کردہ مقدار واجب ہوگی۔ اور اگر طلاق قبل الدخول ہے تو طرفین کے نزدیک عورت کیلئے متعہ واجب ہوگا ۔ اور ابو یوسف کا قول اول یہ ہے کہ اس متعین کردہ مقدار کا نصف واجب ہوگا ۔ اور یہی قول امام شافعی کا ہے۔ ابو یوسف کا دوسرا قول طرفین کے ساتھ ہے۔ امام شافعی اور ابو یوسف کے قول اول کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ زوجین نے باہمی اتفاق سے جو مقدار مقرر کی ہے یہ مفروض ( مقدور و معین) ہے۔ اور آیت فنصف ما فرضتم سے مفروض کی تنصیف ثابت ہے۔ مفروض فی حالت العقد ہو یا مفروض بعد العقد ۔ لہذا اس صورت میں بھی اگر طلاق قبل الدخول پائی گئی تو نصف مفروض واجب ہوگا متعہ واجب نہیں ہوگا۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ عقد نکاح کے وقت اگر مہر ذکر نہ کیا جائے تو مہر مثل واجب ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس اس صورت میں بھی نکاح کے وقت مہر یذکور نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے مہر مثل واجب ہو گیا۔ بعد میں زوجین نے ایک مقدار پر اتفاق کر لیا تو یہ بعد میں متعین کردہ مقدار در حقیقت تعیین ہے اس کی جو عقد کی وجہ سے واجب ہوا تھا اور عقد کی وجہ سے مہر مثل واجب ہوا تھا۔ اور مہر مثل کی تنصیف نہیں ہوتی ۔ لہذا جو اس کے مرتبہ میں ہے اس کی بھی تنصیف نہیں ہوگی۔ حاصل دلیل یہ کہ مفروض بعد العقد تعیین ہے مہر مثل کی اور مہر مثل کی تنصیف نہیں ہوتی ہے لہذا جو ا سکے قائم مقام ہے یعنی مفروض بعد العقد اسکی بھی تنصیف نہیں ہوگی۔ اور جب تنصیف نہیں ہوسکتی تو متعہ واجب ہوگا۔ اور ابو یوسف نے جو آیت تلاوت کی یعنی فنصف ما فرضتم تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ آیت میں فرض فی العقد مراد ہے نہ کہ فرض بعد العقد ۔ اور وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ آیت مطلق ہے اور مطلق بولا جاتا ہے تو اس سے متعارف مراد ہوتا ہے اور متعارف مفروض فی العقد ہے نہ کہ مفروض بعد العقد ۔ پس مفروض فی العقد کی تنصیف ہوگی مفروض بعد العقد کی نہیں۔
Explanation: The scenario is that at the time of marriage, the mahr was not mentioned. Then both husband and wife agreed upon an amount. Now, if the husband has consummated with the wife or died, in both cases this agreed amount becomes obligatory. If divorce occurs before consummation, according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) mut'ah is obligatory for the woman. Abu Yusuf's first opinion is that half of this agreed amount is obligatory. This is also the opinion of Imam Shafi'i. Abu Yusuf's second opinion aligns with the two. The proof of Imam Shafi'i and Abu Yusuf's first opinion is that the amount agreed upon by mutual consent is mafrud (fixed/ determined). The verse 'fa-nisfu ma faradtum' (half of what you fixed) establishes the half of the mafrud, whether the fixing occurred at the time of contract or after the contract. Therefore, in this case too, if divorce before consummation occurs, half of the mafrud is obligatory, not mut'ah. Our proof is that if mahr is not mentioned at the time of marriage, then mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory. So in this case too, due to mahr not being mentioned at the time of marriage, mahr al-mithl became obligatory. Later, when the couple agreed on an amount, this later-fixed amount is in fact a determination of what was already obligatory due to the contract, and due to the contract, mahr al-mithl was obligatory. Mahr al-mithl is not halved. So that which stands in its place (the later-fixed amount) will also not be halved. The summary of the proof is that the later-fixed amount is a determination of mahr al-mithl, and mahr al-mithl is not halved, so the later-fixed amount, which stands in its place, will also not be halved. When half cannot be applied, mut'ah becomes obligatory. As for the verse recited by Abu Yusuf, 'fa-nisfu ma faradtum', the response is that in the verse, 'faradtum' refers to fixing at the time of contract, not fixing after the contract. The reason is that the verse is absolute, and when absolute is used, the understood (conventional) meaning is intended. The conventional meaning is fixing at the time of contract, not after. So half applies to mafrud at the time of contract, not to mafrud after the contract.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) on one side, and Imam al-Shafi'i and Abu Yusuf's first opinion on the other. The issue is: if mahr is not specified at the nikah contract, the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl (proper mahr). If the couple later agrees on a specific amount, and then divorce occurs before consummation, what is due? The Hanafi position (Sahibayn) is that the fixed amount is only a determination of mahr al-mithl, which is never halved, so mut'ah (a gift) is due instead of half. Abu Yusuf's first view, also held by Shafi'i, considers the later agreement as an independent fixing (farad) analogous to that at the contract, thus half is due (Quran 2:237). The Hanafi rebuttal focuses on the term 'faradtum' in the verse, arguing via conventional usage that it only applies to fixing at the time of contract. The passage shows the Hanafi reliance on istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas: while qiyas would equate the two fixings, istihsan distinguishes them based on the nature of mahr al-mithl. Note that Abu Yusuf later reverted to the Sahibayn's view (his second opinion). The practical result is that in this scenario, the Hanafi mufta bihi position is mut'ah, not half.

Key Terms
متعہ (mut'ah): A gift given by the husband to the wife upon divorce before consummation when mahr was not specified.
مفروض (mafrud): The amount fixed by mutual agreement after the marriage contract.
مہر مثل (mahr al-mithl): Proper mahr equivalent to what women of similar status receive, due when mahr is unspecified.
تنصیف (tansif): Halving of the mahr upon divorce before consummation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If mahr is not specified at marriage, the couple later agrees on 500 dirhams, then divorce occurs before consummation. According to the Sahibayn, what is the wife entitled to?
A) Half of 500 dirhams
B) 500 dirhams
C) Mut'ah (a gift)
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a post-marriage mahr agreement is a determination of mahr al-mithl, which is never halved; only mut'ah is due upon divorce before consummation.

Nikah — Marriage

Addition and Reduction of Mahr After Marriage
Rulings on husband's addition and wife's reduction of mahr post-contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on post-contract addition and reduction of mahr, explain the inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi disputes, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Post-contract additions to mahr are binding only if accepted in session; reduction by wife is valid anytime during marriage.

After the marriage contract is concluded, the mahr is fixed. But what if the husband wants to increase it or the wife wants to reduce it? The Hanafi school provides detailed rules for such modifications, with notable disagreements between madhhabs and even within the school itself. This lesson unpacks the rulings, proofs, and practical consequences for both scenarios.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on husband's addition
Identify the basic rule: the addition is binding on the husband if the wife accepts it in the same session. Understand the opposing view of Imam Zufar and Shafi'i.
The text explicitly contrasts the Hanafi position with Zufar's.
2
Analyze the proofs for and against the addition
The Hanafi proof is the Quranic verse allowing mutual agreement after fixation (Quran 4:24). Zufar and Shafi'i analogize the addition to an independent gift (hibah) requiring possession.
The `dalil_block` details the Quranic proof.
3
Determine the effect of divorce before consummation on the addition
The Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold that only the original mahr is halved, not the addition. Abu Yusuf's first view was that the addition is also halved.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the mufta bihi is the Sahibayn view.
4
Explain the validity of the wife's reduction (hatt)
The wife may reduce her mahr after the contract, as long as she does so willingly and the husband accepts in the session. At the time of contract, she cannot reduce below ten dirhams or mahr al-mithl due to Shariah and guardian rights.
The reduction takes effect upon mutual agreement in the session.
5
Summarize the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequences)
For the addition: Hanafis require acceptance for binding; Shafi'is require possession. For halving: only original mahr halved per mufta bihi. For reduction: valid without possession.
These differences affect how mahr disputes are resolved in practice.

Source Text

کسی بات پر راضی ہو جائیں۔ مثلاً عورت اپنی خوشی سے مہر میں سے کچھ کم کر دے یا وہ اپنی رضا سے مہر مقرر سے کچھ زیادہ دے تو وہ مختار ہے اس میں کچھ گناہ نہیں ۔ بہر حال زیادہ کرے یا کم باہمی رضا ضروری ہے۔ ائمہ ثلثہ اور امام زفر کا اصل اختلاف زیادتی شمن اور مثمن میں ہے جو باب المرابحہ اور تولیہ کے بعد ایک فصل میں مذکور ہے اختلاف یہ ہے کہ احناف کے نزدیک مشتری شمن میں اور بائع مبیع میں زیادتی کر سکتا ہے اور امام زفر و شافعی کے نزدیک نہیں کر سکتا ہے۔ بہر حال جب ہمارے نزدیک مہر میں زیادتی کرنا درست ہے تو طلاق قبل الدخول کی صورت میں اصل کے ساتھ زیادتی کی بھی تنصیف ہوگی یا نہیں سو اس بارے میں ابو یوسف کا قول اول یہ ہے کہ اصل مہر کے ساتھ زیادتی کی بھی تنصیف ہوگی اور طرفین کے نزدیک اصل مہر کی تنصیف تو ہوگی زیادتی کی نہیں۔ دلیل ابو یوسف کی وہی ہے جو ماقبل میں گذر چکی کہ مفروض بعد العقد ایسا ہے جیسا کہ مفروض فی حالت العقد ۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ کہ تنصیف مخصوص ہے مفروض فی حالتہ العقد کے ساتھ ۔ لہذا اصل مہر جو حالت عقد میں مقرر ہوا تھا اس کی تنصیف تو ہوگی بعد میں جو زیادہ کیا گیا ہے اس کی تنصیف نہیں ہوگی۔ اور اگر عورت نے اپنے مہر میں سے کچھ کم کر دیا تو کم کردینا درست ہے اسلئے کہ مہر عورت کا حق ہے اور کم کر نالاحق ہوا حالت بقا میں جو عورت کے حدود اختیار میں ہے۔ خلاصہ یہ ہوا کہ ابتداء عقد میں دس درہم سے کم نہیں کر سکتی حق شرع کی وجہ سے اور مہر مثل سے کم نہیں کر سکتی اولیاء کے حق کی وجہ سے اور عقد نکاح کے بعد جب تک نکاح قائم ہے کم کرنا نافذ ہوگا اپنے حق کی وجہ سے بشرطیکہ مجلس میں مرد اس کمی کو قبول بھی کر لے۔
If he increased for her in the mahr after the contract, the increase becomes binding upon him, contrary to Zufar. We will mention it in the increase of price and commodity, insha'Allah. When the increase is valid, it is dropped by divorce before consummation. According to Abu Yusuf's first opinion, it is halved along with the original, because half according to the two is specific to what was fixed at the contract. According to him, what is fixed after is like what is fixed at the contract, as passed. If she reduces from her mahr for him, the reduction is valid, because mahr is her right, and reduction affects it in the state of continuance.
Translation: So if the husband increased for his wife in her mahr after the contract, the increase becomes binding on the husband. Contrary to Imam Zufar. And we will soon mention it in the increase of price and commodity, insha'Allah. When the increase is valid, it becomes dropped by divorce before consummation. According to Abu Yusuf's first opinion, it is halved along with the original, because half according to the two is specific to what was fixed at the contract, and according to him, what is fixed after is like what is fixed at the contract, as passed. If the woman reduces from her mahr for the husband, this reduction is valid, because mahr is her right, and reduction affects it in the state of continuance.
Explanation: If after the marriage contract, the husband increases on the fixed mahr and the woman accepts in the same session, then according to us, this increase becomes binding on the husband. Imam Zufar says the increase is not valid, and Imam Shafi'i agrees with him. Imam Zufar's proof is that the increase is an independent gift, so it does not attach to the original contract. If the wife takes possession, she owns it, otherwise not. Our proof is the Quranic verse: 'There is no sin upon you in what you mutually agree after the fixation.' In its commentary, Maulana Shabbir Ahmad wrote that if the spouses agree on something after fixing mahr, e.g., the woman voluntarily reduces some of the mahr or the man gives more from the fixed mahr, he has option, there is no sin. Anyway, whether increase or decrease, mutual consent is necessary. The original disagreement between the three Imams and Imam Zufar is in the increase of price and commodity, which is mentioned in a chapter after Bab al-Murabahah and Tawliyah. The disagreement is that according to the Hanafis, the buyer can increase in the price and the seller can increase in the commodity, while Imam Zufar and Shafi'i do not allow it. Anyway, when according to us increasing in mahr is valid, then in case of divorce before consummation, will the increase also be halved along with the original? Regarding this, Abu Yusuf's first opinion is that the increase will also be halved along with the original mahr. According to the two, the original mahr will be halved, but not the increase. Abu Yusuf's proof is the same as passed previously, that what is fixed after the contract is like what is fixed at the time of contract. Our proof is that half is specific to what is fixed at the time of contract. So the original mahr fixed at the contract will be halved, but the increase made later will not be halved. If the woman reduces some of her mahr, the reduction is valid, because mahr is the woman's right, and reduction affects it in the state of continuance, which is within the woman's scope of authority. Summary: At the beginning of the contract, she cannot reduce it below ten dirhams due to the right of Shari'ah, and cannot reduce it below mahr al-mithl due to the right of the guardians. After the marriage contract, as long as the marriage exists, reduction is effective due to her own right, provided that the man accepts the reduction in the session.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding post-marriage modifications to mahr. The first part discusses the husband's addition: the Hanafi school (Imam Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) holds that if the husband increases the mahr after the contract and the wife accepts in the same session, the increase is binding. Imam Zufar and Shafi'i disagree, viewing it as an independent gift requiring possession. The Hanafi proof is Quran 4:24 (or similar) allowing mutual agreement after fixation. Then the passage addresses the effect of divorce before consummation on the increase. There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Yusuf's first view is that the increase is halved along with the original mahr, while the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold that only the original mahr is halved, not the increase. The reasoning mirrors the earlier dispute: Abu Yusuf considers post-contract fixation equivalent to contract fixation, while the Sahibayn restrict half to contract fixation. The passage then discusses the wife's reduction (hatt): it is valid after marriage because mahr is her right and she is exercising it during the continuance of the marriage, provided the husband accepts in the session. However, certain limits apply at the time of contract (minimum ten dirhams and mahr al-mithl). This passage shows the Hanafi position on the binding nature of post-contract agreements regarding mahr.

Key Terms
زیادتی (ziyadah): Addition to the mahr made by the husband after the contract.
حط (hatt): Reduction of the mahr by the wife for the husband.
مفروض بعد العقد (mafrud ba'd al-'aqd): Amount fixed after the marriage contract, either by determination or increase.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (Sahibayn), if the husband adds 200 dirhams to the mahr after the contract and then divorces before consummation, what happens to the addition?
A) The addition is halved along with the original mahr
B) The addition is not halved; only the original mahr is halved
C) The addition is void because it was added after the contract
D) The addition becomes the full mahr

Key Takeaway
Post-contract additions to mahr are binding only if accepted in session, and only the original mahr is halved upon divorce before consummation; the wife's reduction is valid anytime during marriage with consent.

Valid Seclusion (Khalwah Sahihah) and Full Mahr
Inter-madhhab dispute with qiyas reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on khalwah sahihah and mahr, apply the qiyas with sale, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Valid seclusion makes full mahr due — delivery of availability suffices, just as in sale.

This passage presents the Hanafi view that if a man secludes with his wife privately with no impediment and then divorces her, she gets full mahr. The Shafi'i school disagrees, requiring actual intercourse. The Hanafi proof uses an analogy to sale to argue that the wife's delivery of the 'substitute' (mubdal) by removing impediments is sufficient to confirm the full mahr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Dispute
What does the text rule for the wife's mahr after valid seclusion and divorce? Which school opposes?
Hanafi: full mahr; Shafi'i: half mahr.
2
Understand the Shafi'i Proof
Why does Shafi'i say half? Focus on the claim that the subject matter (manafi' bud') is only fully taken by actual intercourse.
Shafi'i argues that mahr is confirmed only upon actual use of the right.
3
Follow the Hanafi Qiyas
How does the Hanafi school analogize to a sale? What is the asl (original case), far' (new case), and illa (effective cause)?
Asl: sale; far': nikah; illa: delivery of the substitute (mubdal) by making the object available.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi Response
How does the Hanafi school rebut Shafi'i's objection that sale requires actual receipt?
In sale, mere enabling (takliya) suffices for price confirmation; similarly here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عورت سے خلوت صحیحہ کی اور کوئی مانع ولی نہیں تھا، پھر طلاق دے دی ... مکمل مہر لازم ہے
واذا خلا الرجل بامرأته وليس هناك مانع من الوطى ثم طلقها فلها كمال المهر وقال الشافعي لها نصف المهر لان المعقود عليه انما يصير مستوفى بالوطى فلايتاكد المهردونه ولنا انها سلمت المبدل حيث رفعت الموانع وذلك وسعها فيتاكد حقها في البدل اعتبارا بالبيع
ترجمہ اور جب خلوت کی مرد نے اپنی بیوی کے ساتھ اور وہاں کوئی مانع قطی بھی نہیں ہے پھر طلاق دی اس عورت کو تو اس کیلئے کامل مہر ہوگا۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ عورت کیلئے نصف مہر ہو گا اسلئے کہ معقود علیہ یعنی منافع بضع پوری طور پر وصول ہوتے ہیں دہلی سے لہذا بغیر ولی کے مہر مؤکد نہیں ہوگا اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت نے مبدل سپرد کر دیا کیونکہ اس نے مواقع کو اٹھا دیا اور یہی اس کی وسعت میں تھا پس اس کا حق مؤکد ہو گا بدل میں قیاس کرتے ہوئے بیچ میں۔
And if a man secludes with his wife and there is no impediment to intercourse, then he divorces her, she gets the full mahr. Imam Shafi'i said she gets half the mahr, because the subject of the contract (usufruct of vulva) is only fully taken by actual intercourse, so mahr is not confirmed without it. Our proof is that she handed over the substitute (mubdal) by removing the impediments, and that is within her capacity, so her right to the substitute is confirmed, by analogy to sale.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the effect of valid seclusion (khalwah sahihah) on mahr when divorce occurs before actual consummation. The Hanafi position is that if a man secludes with his wife in private with no legal or physical impediment to intercourse (e.g., no menstruation, no fasting, no travel, no third person present), then divorces her, she is entitled to the full mahr, not half. Imam Shafi'i argues that half is due because the subject matter of the contract (the right to intercourse) is only fully realized by actual intercourse, so seclusion alone does not confirm the full mahr. The Hanafi proof is based on qiyas with a sale: just as in a sale, if the seller delivers the goods (makes them available) and the buyer takes possession, the price is confirmed; here the wife has delivered her part by removing impediments and making herself available for intercourse. Since full availability is within her capacity (she cannot force actual intercourse), that is sufficient to confirm the entire substitute (mahr). The ruling is that full mahr becomes due upon valid seclusion followed by divorce, even without actual intercourse.

Key Terms
خلوت صحیحہ (khalwah sahihah): Valid seclusion: husband and wife alone in a place where intercourse is physically possible and no legal or natural impediment exists.
مانع وطی (mani' wat'i): Impediment to intercourse, e.g., menstruation, ritual fasting, travel, illness, or presence of a third person.
مبدل (mubdal): The substitute: the wife's availability and submission in the marital relationship, analogous to goods in a sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man concludes a valid nikah, takes his wife to a private room with no witnesses or impediments, then divorces her before any physical contact. According to the Hanafi school, what is the wife entitled to?
A) Half of the mahr
B) Full mahr
C) Mut'ah only
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
Valid seclusion (khalwah sahihah) with no impediment obligates full mahr upon subsequent divorce, by Hanafi analogy to sale.

Increasing or Decreasing Mahr After the Contract
Ruling on increasing or decreasing mahr after contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on increasing and decreasing mahr after the marriage contract, explain the inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi disputes, and apply the rule that tanseef applies only to the originally fixed mahr.

Core Idea
Increasing mahr after contract is valid per Hanafi; it becomes part of the mahr but is not subject to tanseef upon divorce before consummation.

This lesson examines one of the practical issues in marriage contracts: can the spouses change the mahr after the contract is concluded? The Hanafi school permits both increase and decrease by mutual consent, while other schools restrict this. You will learn the proof, the intra-Hanafi disagreement on the effect of divorce before consummation, and the conditions under which the wife may reduce her mahr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and Hanafi position
State that the Hanafi school (three imams) holds that increasing mahr after the contract is valid and becomes part of the mahr.
This applies to any addition agreed upon after the original fixation.
2
Analyze the opposing view (Shafi'i/Zufar)
Explain that Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i consider the increase an independent gift (hibah) that does not attach to the original contract, requiring separate possession.
Their proof: increase is a separate contract, not a modification of the original.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof and response
Recite the Hanafi proof from Quran 4:24, which permits mutual agreement after the obligation. Show how this verse supports the validity of increase as an addition to the mahr, not a separate gift.
The Hanafi response uses qiyas on sales where increasing the price after agreement is allowed.
4
Resolve the intra-Hanafi dispute on tanseef
Identify that Abu Yusuf initially held the increase is halved upon divorce before consummation, while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad held it is not. The relied-upon position is the latter.
Key principle: tanseef applies only to mahr fixed at the time of contract, not to later increases.
5
Understand the wife's right to decrease mahr
The wife may decrease her mahr after the contract within her authority, but cannot go below ten dirhams or mahr al-mithl at the time of contract due to rights of shariah and guardians. Acceptance by the husband in the same session is required.
Decrease is her right as owner of the mahr, but limited by prior obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
زیادتی لازم ہوگی۔ اور امام زفر فر ماتے ہیں کہ زیادتی صحیح نہیں۔ اور اسی کے قائل ہیں امام شافعی امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ زیادتی مستقلاً ہبہ ہے۔ لہذا اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں ہو گا۔ اگر بیوی نے قبضہ کر لیا تو مالک ہو گی ورنہ نہیں۔ ہماری دلیل آیت قرآن ہے "ولا جناح عليكم فيما تراضيتم به من بعد الفريضة" اور گناہ نہیں تم کو اس بات میں کہ ٹھہر الو تم دونوں آپس کی رضامندی سے مقرر کیئے ہوئے کے بعد۔ آیت کی تفسیر میں مولانا شبیر احمد نے لکھا ہے کہ اگر زوجین مہر مقرر کر لینے کے بعد کسی بات پر راضی ہو جائیں۔ مثلاً عورت اپنی خوشی سے مہر میں سے کچھ کم کر دے یا وہ اپنی رضا سے مہر مقرر سے کچھ زیادہ دے تو وہ مختار ہے اس میں کچھ گناہ نہیں ۔ بہر حال زیادہ کرے یا کم باہمی رضا ضروری ہے۔ ائمہ ثلثہ اور امام زفر کا اصل اختلاف زیادتی شمن اور مثمن میں ہے جو باب المرابحہ اور تولیہ کے بعد ایک فصل میں مذکور ہے اختلاف یہ ہے کہ احناف کے نزدیک مشتری شمن میں اور بائع مبیع میں زیادتی کر سکتا ہے اور امام زفر و شافعی کے نزدیک نہیں کر سکتا ہے۔ بہر حال جب ہمارے نزدیک مہر میں زیادتی کرنا درست ہے تو طلاق قبل الدخول کی صورت میں اصل کے ساتھ زیادتی کی بھی تنصیف ہوگی یا نہیں سو اس بارے میں ابو یوسف کا قول اول یہ ہے کہ اصل مہر کے ساتھ زیادتی کی بھی تنصیف ہوگی اور طرفین کے نزدیک اصل مہر کی تنصیف تو ہوگی زیادتی کی نہیں۔ دلیل ابو یوسف کی وہی ہے جو ماقبل میں گذر چکی کہ مفروض بعد العقد ایسا ہے جیسا کہ مفروض فی حالت العقد ۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ کہ تنصیف مخصوص ہے مفروض فی حالتہ العقد کے ساتھ ۔ لہذا اصل مہر جو حالت عقد میں مقرر ہوا تھا اس کی تنصیف تو ہوگی بعد میں جو زیادہ کیا گیا ہے اس کی تنصیف نہیں ہوگی۔ اور اگر عورت نے اپنے مہر میں سے کچھ کم کر دیا تو کم کردینا درست ہے اسلئے کہ مہر عورت کا حق ہے اور کم کر نالاحق ہوا حالت بقا میں جو عورت کے حدود اختیار میں ہے۔ خلاصہ یہ ہوا کہ ابتداء عقد میں دس درہم سے کم نہیں کر سکتی حق شرع کی وجہ سے اور مہر مثل سے کم نہیں کر سکتی اولیاء کے حق کی وجہ سے اور عقد نکاح کے بعد جب تک نکاح قائم ہے کم کرنا نافذ ہوگا اپنے حق کی وجہ سے بشرطیکہ مجلس میں مرد اس کمی کو قبول بھی کر لے۔
Increase will be necessary. Imam Zufar says that increase is not valid. Imam Shafi'i agrees with him. Imam Zufar's proof is that the increase is an independent gift, therefore it does not attach to the original contract. If the wife takes possession, she becomes owner; otherwise not. Our proof is the Quranic verse: 'There is no sin upon you concerning what you mutually agree after the obligation.' And there is no sin upon you in that you both agree by mutual consent after the fixed [mahr]. In the interpretation of the verse, Maulana Shabir Ahmad wrote that if the spouses agree on something after fixing the mahr, for example, the woman reduces some of the mahr willingly, or the man gives more than the fixed mahr willingly, then he is free, there is no sin. Anyhow, whether increase or decrease, mutual consent is necessary. The main difference between the three Imams and Imam Zufar concerns increase in the price and the commodity, which is mentioned in a chapter after the chapter on Murabahah and Tawliyah. The difference is that according to the Hanafis, the buyer can increase the price and the seller can increase the commodity, while according to Imam Zufar and Shafi'i, they cannot. Anyway, when in our view increasing the mahr is valid, then in the case of divorce before consummation, will the increase be halved along with the original or not? Regarding this, Abu Yusuf's first opinion is that the increase will be halved along with the original mahr, while the two sides (i.e., Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold that the original mahr is halved but not the increase. Abu Yusuf's proof is what has passed previously: that what is fixed after the contract is like what is fixed at the time of the contract. Our proof is that halving is specific to what is fixed at the time of the contract. Therefore, the original mahr fixed at the time of the contract will be halved, but what is increased later will not be halved. And if the woman reduces some of her mahr, the reduction is valid because the mahr is her right, and reducing it in the state of continuation is within her authority. The summary is that at the beginning of the contract she cannot reduce it below ten dirhams due to a legal right, and she cannot reduce it below the mahr al-mithl due to the right of the guardians, and after the marriage contract while the marriage subsists, reduction is effective due to her own right, provided the man accepts the reduction in the same session.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage discusses two issues regarding mahr after the marriage contract: increase and decrease. It starts with the ruling on increasing the mahr. According to the Hanafi school (three Imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani), an increase in mahr after the contract is valid and becomes part of the mahr. Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i disagree, arguing that the increase is an independent gift separate from the contract. The Hanafi proof is the Quranic verse (4:24) which permits mutual agreement after the obligation. The passage then distinguishes this from the general principle of increasing price or commodity in sales, where the same dispute applies. The second issue is whether the increase is subject to tanseef (halving) when divorce occurs before consummation. Abu Yusuf initially held that the increase is also halved, but the relied-upon position (of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that only the original mahr fixed at the time of the contract is halved; the later increase is not halved because tanseef applies to what was fixed at the time of the contract. The third issue is the wife decreasing her own mahr. She cannot reduce it below ten dirhams (the minimum mahr) due to shariah, nor below mahr al-mithl due to guardians' rights, but after the contract, she can reduce it with her husband's acceptance in the same session.

Key Terms
تنصیف (tanseef): Halving of mahr when divorce occurs before consummation (before khulwah sahihah).
زیادتی (ziyādah): Increase in mahr after the marriage contract by mutual consent.
مہر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The mahr equivalent to that of women of similar status; a minimum threshold set by guardians.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a husband increases the mahr after the marriage contract and then divorces his wife before consummation, is the increase halved along with the original mahr?
A) Yes, the increase is halved because it is part of the mahr.
B) No, only the originally fixed mahr is halved; the increase remains full.
C) The increase is not valid at all, so it is disregarded.
D) It depends on whether the wife accepted the increase in the same session.

Key Takeaway
Increasing mahr after contract is valid per Hanafi by Quranic permission; the increase is not subject to tanseef upon divorce before consummation, and decreasing mahr after contract is valid with conditions.
